WORK-001: ANALYTIC PHILOSOPHY COMPLETE - 50 POSITIONS
====================================================================================================

**ACTION THEORY (1 positions): ACTION-006 to ACTION-006**

**Position ACTION-006: Compatibilism About Free Will**
- Free will is compatible with determinism. One acts freely when actions result from one's own desires and deliberations.

**EPISTEMOLOGY (15 positions): EP-001 to EP-026**

**Position EP-001: Rationalist Foundationalism**
- Knowledge rests on bedrock of non-empirical, purely logical truths

**Position EP-002: Anti-Empiricism**
- Strict empiricism false; non-empirical knowledge required for all knowledge

**Position EP-003: Knowledge as Non-Accidentally Justified True Belief**
- Four conditions for knowledge: truth, belief, justification, non-accidental connection

**Position EP-015: Refutation of Humean Skepticism**
- Induction justified; Hume's argument commits gambler's fallacy

**Position EP-016: Gettier Problem: Justification Must Be Non-Accidental**
- Justified true belief is not sufficient for knowledge. The connection between justification and truth must be non-accidental.

**Position EP-017: Three Sources of Justification**
- There are ultimately only three sources of justification: (a) perceptual evidence, (b) introspective evidence, (c) rational inference.

**Position EP-018: Testimony Requires Independent Verification**
- For testimony-based belief to constitute knowledge, one must have independent evidence of the source's reliability.

**Position EP-019: Cartesian Skepticism Refuted**
- Global skepticism is self-refuting. The skeptical hypothesis cannot coherently be entertained.

**Position EP-020: Inductive Inference Cannot Be Justified A Posteriori**
- The principle of induction cannot be justified empirically without circularity.

**Position EP-021: Rationalist Solution to Induction**
- The principle of induction must be known a priori if it is to be justified at all.

**Position EP-022: Universals Cannot Be Sense-Perceived**
- Universals cannot be sense-perceived because they are non-spatiotemporal and perception requires causal interaction.

**Position EP-023: Thought Requires Universals**
- All thought, language, and explanation require universals. The idea of non-universal-involving thought is incoherent.

**Position EP-024: Empiricism Refuted by Need for Universals**
- Strict empiricism is false. Since universals are required for all thought and cannot be sense-perceived, not all knowledge is empirical.

**Position EP-025: Berkeley's 'To Be Is To Be Perceived' Refuted**
- Berkeley's idealism is false. Multiple arguments refute 'esse est percipi'.

**Position EP-026: Phenomenalism Refuted**
- Phenomenalism (reducing physical objects to perceptions) is false. Carnap's project failed.

**LOGIC (1 positions): LOGIC-010 to LOGIC-010**

**Position LOGIC-010: Logicism Defended (Frege's Project)**
- Arithmetic is reducible to logic. Mathematical truths are logical truths.

**METAPHYSICS (7 positions): META-001 to META-008**

**Position META-001: Platonism about Properties**
- Properties exist as non-spatiotemporal entities distinct from instances

**Position META-002: Propositions as Sets of Properties**
- Propositions are sets of properties; truth is instantiatedness

**Position META-004: Properties as Non-Spatiotemporal Entities (Platonism)**
- Properties exist as non-spatiotemporal entities. They are not identical with their instances.

**Position META-005: Uninstantiated Properties Exist**
- Properties can exist even when nothing has them. The property of being a unicorn exists.

**Position META-006: Determinism vs Randomness vs Unpredictability**
- Determinism, randomness, and predictability are distinct concepts that must not be conflated.

**Position META-007: Personal Identity Through Time**
- Personal identity consists in psychological continuity, not bodily continuity.

**Position META-008: Causality as Counterfactual Dependence**
- Event A causes event B iff: (1) both occur, and (2) had A not occurred, B would not have occurred.

**MODAL LOGIC (1 positions): MODAL-003 to MODAL-003**

**Position MODAL-003: Against Possible Worlds Semantics**
- Possible worlds semantics for modality is either false or trivial. It doesn't explain what necessity and possibility are.

**PHILOSOPHY OF LANGUAGE (9 positions): LANG-014 to LANG-022**

**Position LANG-014: Logical Form vs Grammatical Form (Frege's Insight)**
- Logical form is not identical with grammatical form. What a sentence says is not always what its grammatical structure suggests.

**Position LANG-015: Propositions as Abstract Objects**
- Propositions are abstract, mind-independent objects that exist outside space and time.

**Position LANG-016: Truth as Correspondence**
- A proposition is true iff it corresponds to reality—if the world is as it says the world is.

**Position LANG-017: Meaning is Not Mental**
- Linguistic meaning is not reducible to mental states or psychological facts.

**Position LANG-018: Russell's Theory of Descriptions**
- Definite descriptions are not referring terms. 'The F is G' means 'Something uniquely is F, and any such thing is G.'

**Position LANG-019: Frege's Sense/Reference Distinction Collapses into Russellianism**
- Frege's theory that definite descriptions have both sense and reference collapses into Russell's theory.

**Position LANG-020: Against Fregean Intensional Contexts**
- Frege's distinction between extensional and intensional contexts is a failed epicycle.

**Position LANG-021: Literal Meaning vs Cognitive Significance**
- Literal meaning (semantic content) must be distinguished from cognitive significance.

**Position LANG-022: Semantic Externalism (Putnam's Insight)**
- Meanings of natural kind terms are partially determined by facts external to the speaker's mind.

**PHILOSOPHY OF MIND (5 positions): MIND-001 to MIND-011**

**Position MIND-001: Anti-Language of Thought**
- We do not think in language (natural or innate)

**Position MIND-008: Against Language of Thought Hypothesis**
- We do not think in words. Thought is not conducted in a language-like medium. The Language of Thought hypothesis is false.

**Position MIND-009: Thought Is Prior to Language**
- Thought is logically and developmentally prior to language. One must think to understand language.

**Position MIND-010: Against Burge's Semantic Externalism for Attitudes**
- Burge's extension of semantic externalism to mental content is a blunder. Mental states are individuated by internal features.

**Position MIND-011: Selfhood Requires Values**
- Being a self requires having values and making value-judgments. Selfhood is normative, not merely cognitive.

**VALUE THEORY (11 positions): VALUE-002 to VALUE-012**

**Position VALUE-002: Instrumental vs Intrinsic Good**
- Goodness divides into instrumental good (useful for goals) and intrinsic good (good in itself). Ethics concerns intrinsic goodness.

**Position VALUE-003: Intrinsic Good vs Commendable**
- Intrinsic goodness and praiseworthiness are distinct. Some intrinsically good things are not praiseworthy.

**Position VALUE-004: Moral Responsibility Based on Intentions**
- Praise/blame depends on intended outcome, not actual outcome.

**Position VALUE-005: Against Emotivism**
- Moral judgments are not merely expressions of emotion. They are genuine assertions with truth-values.

**Position VALUE-006: Against Moral Relativism**
- Moral relativism is false. There are objective moral truths.

**Position VALUE-007: Against Kant's Categorical Imperative**
- Kant's categorical imperative fails as a criterion for right action.

**Position VALUE-008: Against Pure Hedonism**
- Pleasure is not the only intrinsic good. Hedonism is false.

**Position VALUE-009: Against Pure Utilitarianism**
- Act utilitarianism is false. It violates rights and permits obviously wrong actions.

**Position VALUE-010: Against Divine Command Theory**
- Morality is not based on God's commands. Euthyphro dilemma refutes divine command theory.

**Position VALUE-011: We Cannot Choose Our Values**
- We cannot freely choose what we value. The idea of 'choosing one's own values' is incoherent.

**Position VALUE-012: Law Must Be Based on Justice**
- The purpose of law is to secure justice. Legal systems must be evaluated by whether they achieve justice.


====================================================================================================
WORK-002: ASK ME ANYTHING ABOUT EPISTEMOLOGY - 6 POSITIONS
====================================================================================================

**EPISTEMOLOGY (2 positions): EP-006 to EP-007**

**Position EP-006: Aboriginal Procedural Knowledge**
- Humans have in-built procedural knowledge of dependence-relations

**Position EP-007: Continuity-Based External World Knowledge**
- We know external world by interpolating continuities between experiential data

**METAPHYSICS (1 positions): META-003 to META-003**

**Position META-003: Anti-Constructivism**
- Constructivism self-refuting through reductio

**PHILOSOPHY OF MIND (3 positions): MIND-002 to MIND-004**

**Position MIND-002: Perspectival Theory of Feelings**
- Feelings represent relationship to universe, inherently perspectival

**Position MIND-003: Systematicity of Mental Representation**
- Cognitive success depends on systematic connection and coherence of mental entity systems

**Position MIND-004: Mind as Multi-Mapper**
- Mind maps itself onto different structures (musical, graphical, visual, athletic)


====================================================================================================
WORK-003: INTENSIONALITY, MODALITY, AND RATIONALITY: SOME PRESEMANTIC CONSIDERATIONS - 7 POSITIONS
====================================================================================================

**MODAL LOGIC (2 positions): MODAL-001 to MODAL-002**

**Position MODAL-001: No Necessary A Posteriori Truths**
- Apparent necessary a posteriori truths are either necessary-and-analytic or contingent-and-a-posteriori

**Position MODAL-002: Epistemic and Metaphysical Necessity Coincide**
- No genuine distinction between epistemic and metaphysical necessity

**PHILOSOPHY OF LANGUAGE (5 positions): LANG-001 to LANG-006**

**Position LANG-001: Semantics vs. Presemantics Distinction**
- Literal meaning must be distinguished from information through which one identifies that meaning

**Position LANG-002: Universal Extensionality**
- ALL contexts extensional at semantic level. Co-referring terms intersubstitutable.

**Position LANG-003: Direct Referentialism for Proper Names**
- Proper names are mere labels referring directly to objects

**Position LANG-005: Against Indirect Referentialism**
- Frege's sense/reference theory for descriptions is incoherent

**Position LANG-006: Presemantic Implicature Theory**
- New category beyond Gricean post-semantic implicature


====================================================================================================
WORK-004: A NON-RUSSELLIAN TREATMENT OF THE REFERENTIAL-ATTRIBUTIVE DISTINCTION - 10 POSITIONS
====================================================================================================

**METHODOLOGY (1 positions): METHOD-004 to METHOD-004**

**Position METHOD-004: Pragmatics-Constrained Semantics**
- Semantic theories must respect known pragmatic principles. Can't just assert 'implicature explains it' without checking constraints.

**PHILOSOPHY OF LANGUAGE (7 positions): LANG-007 to LANG-013**

**Position LANG-007: Definite Descriptions as Referring Expressions**
- Definite descriptions ('the phi') are referring terms, not quantificational. Always encode propositions of form 'a has phi'

**Position LANG-008: Referential-Attributive Distinction as Pragmatic**
- Not semantic ambiguity. Both uses involve reference. Attributive: reference to entity in understood existence claim. Referential: ostensive.

**Position LANG-009: Presupposition Not Assertion**
- Following Strawson: descriptions presuppose existence. Abortive (not false) when presupposition fails.

**Position LANG-010: Against Contextualism**
- Rejects neo-Russellian move that context restricts quantifier domains. Violates Gricean principles.

**Position LANG-011: Against Conventional Implicature Solution**
- D-sentences don't implicate object-dependent propositions via conventional implicature. Violates implicature principles.

**Position LANG-012: Anaphoric Descriptions as Referential**
- Anaphoric descriptions refer to entities introduced by antecedents. Not bound variables.

**Position LANG-013: Logical Form vs Semantics**
- Logical form (inferential structure) ≠ semantics (literal meaning). Same proposition can have multiple logical forms.

**PRAGMATICS (2 positions): PRAG-001 to PRAG-002**

**Position PRAG-001: Cancelability Test**
- Conversational implicatures always cancelable. Existence presuppositions not cancelable. Therefore not conversational implicature.

**Position PRAG-002: Conventional Implicature Constraint**
- Conventional implicature doesn't obscure truth-conditions. Adds 'tone' but never makes synonyms differ in truth-conditions.


====================================================================================================
WORK-005: A PRIORI KNOWLEDGE AND OTHER PHILOSOPHICAL WORKS - 26 POSITIONS
====================================================================================================

**ACTION THEORY (5 positions): ACTION-001 to ACTION-005**

**Position ACTION-001: Intentions as System-Level Judgments**
- Intentions = judgments about how to consolidate psychological architecture. NOT desires.

**Position ACTION-002: Values Distinct from Desires**
- Values = beliefs about what consolidates psychological architecture. Values ≠ desires (though can interact).

**Position ACTION-003: Free Acts as Value-Driven**
- Free acts driven by values, NOT by second-order desires (contra Frankfurt). Second-order desires can be warped.

**Position ACTION-004: Rational vs. Intelligent Distinction**
- Rational = embodies due regard for interests. Intelligent = computational power. Irrational acts can be highly intelligent.

**Position ACTION-005: Frankfurt's Analysis Insufficient**
- Frankfurt right about higher-order states but wrong that second-order desires sufficient. Rationalization problem.

**EPISTEMOLOGY (9 positions): EP-004 to EP-014**

**Position EP-004: Philosophy Justifies Empirical Science's Presuppositions**
- Empirical disciplines make assumptions they cannot empirically justify. Only philosophy can provide non-empirical justification. Philosophy is meta-science.

**Position EP-005: Observation Cannot Self-Corroborate**
- Observation cannot justify that observation is reliable. Witnesses cannot self-corroborate. Pure empiricism is circular.

**Position EP-008: Two Ways Sense-Perception Adds to Knowledge**
- Perception contributes via (1) direct content transmission and (2) triggering ratiocinative processes beyond perceptual content

**Position EP-009: Principles Cannot Be Sense-Perceived**
- Can perceive specific objects but cannot perceive principles or general truths. Principles grasped through reason.

**Position EP-010: Non-Empirical Knowledge Exists**
- Some truths are known without empirical justification: mathematical, logical, some metaphysical

**Position EP-011: All Non-Empirical Knowledge is Analytic**
- All non-empirical knowledge concerns conceptual structures. Explicitly rejects Kant's synthetic a priori.

**Position EP-012: A Priori Knowledge as Constitutive of Reasoning Ability**
- A priori knowledge = knowledge constitutive of ability to reason. Not acquired through experience but enables learning from experience.

**Position EP-013: A Priori Knowledge Necessary for Any Learning**
- Cannot learn from experience without a priori knowledge. Cannot deduce principles of deduction from experience (circular). Must have deductive knowledge ab initio.

**Position EP-014: A Priori Knowledge as Subpersonal**
- A priori knowledge not ordinary propositional knowledge but constitutive of subject itself. Principles are ability to think, not objects of thought.

**LOGIC (8 positions): LOGIC-001 to LOGIC-009**

**Position LOGIC-001: Analytic Truth Defined by Content Alone**
- Analytic truths hold entirely in virtue of own content. Given only what they say, could not fail to be true.

**Position LOGIC-002: Tautologies are NOT Analytic Truths**
- Tautologies = definitional truths about word usage (empirical). No analytic truths are tautologies.

**Position LOGIC-003: All Mathematical Truths are Analytic**
- Every mathematical truth is analytic. Mathematical knowledge = non-empirical knowledge of conceptual relations.

**Position LOGIC-004: Not All Analytic Truths are Mathematical**
- Philosophy has its own domain of analytic truths. Example: 'All math truths are analytic' is analytic but philosophical.

**Position LOGIC-005: Analytic Truth vs. Formal Truth Distinction**
- Analytic truth ≠ formal truth. Formally true = recursively definable. Math truths analytic but not formal.

**Position LOGIC-006: Incompleteness as Non-Recursive-Definability**
- Incomplete = no recursive definition. Most scientifically important statement-sets incomplete.

**Position LOGIC-008: Logic is Incomplete (More General than Gödel)**
- Class of all logics not itself recursively definable. Logic is incomplete. More general than Gödel's result.

**Position LOGIC-009: Logic as Recursively Defined Statement-Set**
- A logic = recursively defined statement-set = axiomatic system

**PHILOSOPHY OF MIND (3 positions): SELF-001 to SELF-003**

**Position SELF-001: Minds ≠ Selves**
- Having a mind does not entail being a self. Co-corporeal, informationally integrated mental states = mind, but NOT sufficient for selfhood.

**Position SELF-002: Selves Require Values**
- No values = no self (though may have mind). Values necessary for agency. No agency without selves.

**Position SELF-003: Selfhood as Matter of Degree**
- Selfhood not binary but admits of degrees. Correlates with degree of value-structured architecture.

**VALUE THEORY (1 positions): VALUE-001 to VALUE-001**

**Position VALUE-001: Intrinsic Value and Self-Consolidation**
- Intrinsically valuable = what consolidates one's agency. Not hedonistic.


====================================================================================================
WORK-006: CHOMSKY'S TWO CONTRIBUTIONS TO PHILOSOPHY - 9 POSITIONS
====================================================================================================

**EPISTEMOLOGY (6 positions): EP-027 to EP-032**

**Position EP-027: Poverty of Stimulus Argument for A Priori Knowledge (Chomsky)**
- Humans acquire linguistic competence from minimal data while non-linguistic entities cannot, proving humans possess innate, pre-experiential cognitive structure (a priori knowledge).

**Position EP-028: Innate Cognitive Structure Required for Language Learning**
- Language acquisition requires pre-existing innate cognitive structure. This structure is cognitive, not merely physiological.

**Position EP-029: Language Learning as 'Triggering' Pre-Existing Structure**
- Experience does not create linguistic knowledge de novo but 'triggers' or 'turns on' pre-existing cognitive structures. Learning is activation, not construction.

**Position EP-030: A Priori Knowledge as Cognitive Framework (Not Framework Content)**
- A priori knowledge is not knowledge you have (content within framework) but knowledge you are (the framework itself). It is not the object of awareness but the subject that makes awareness possible.

**Position EP-031: Framework-Knowledge vs Content-Knowledge Distinction**
- Fundamental distinction between (1) structure-internal knowledge (learned, content) and (2) structure-constitutive knowledge (a priori, framework). All learned knowledge presupposes the framework.

**Position EP-032: Deep Unconsciousness of Cognitive Framework**
- Framework-constitutive structures are 'deeply unconscious' (Chomsky's term) - unlike Freudian unconscious. Cannot become conscious because consciousness presupposes them.

**PHILOSOPHY OF LANGUAGE (1 positions): LANG-023 to LANG-023**

**Position LANG-023: Systematicity and Productivity of Language**
- Languages exhibit two fundamental properties: (1) Productivity - expressions can be combined into larger expressions, and (2) Systematicity - parts composing complex expressions can be re-arranged to form other expressions.

**PHILOSOPHY OF MIND (2 positions): MIND-012 to MIND-013**

**Position MIND-012: Cognitive Structure Not Purely Physiological**
- Cognitive structures underlying language and thought are not purely physiological but are cognitive - they encode insight, intelligence, and understanding of logical relations. Pure physiology enables only stereotyped responses.

**Position MIND-013: Sub-Personal Thought Exists**
- Genuine thought (cognitive operations involving understanding of logical relations) occurs at sub-personal level - below conscious awareness. Chomsky's second major contribution to philosophy.


====================================================================================================
WORK-007: CONCEPTION AND CAUSATION: SELECTED EARLY PHILOSOPHICAL PAPERS - 18 POSITIONS
====================================================================================================

**METAPHYSICS (2 positions): METPH-001 to METPH-002**

**Position METPH-001: Bundle Theory of Personal Identity**
- A person/self is class of all mental contents I-related to given mental content. Two mental contents belong to same person iff there is chain such that each link directly interacts with its neighbor. Direct interaction = no intervening physical events.

**Position METPH-002: Content-Bearing Processes Are Ipso Facto Mental**
- If physical process non-derivatively bears representational/thematic content, it is ipso facto mental (whatever else it is). Content-bearing is sufficient (though not necessary) for mentality.

**PHILOSOPHY OF LANGUAGE (1 positions): LANG-024 to LANG-024**

**Position LANG-024: Semantic Rules Are Ultimately Descriptive**
- Semantic rules describe what speakers mean/understand by expressions. They are not purely conventional stipulations independent of speaker practices. For 'red' to mean red just IS for speakers to mean/understand red by 'red'.

**PHILOSOPHY OF MIND (15 positions): MIND-014 to MIND-028**

**Position MIND-014: No Language of Thought Exists**
- There is no Language of Thought (Mentalese). Thinking does not consist in the tokening of internal symbols. Thought cannot reduce to language processing.

**Position MIND-015: Semantic Rule Knowledge Required for Language Understanding**
- To know or understand any language requires knowing its semantic rules. This is trivially true by definition of 'knowing language'.

**Position MIND-016: Tarski's Theorem Blocks Self-Expression of Semantics**
- No language can express its own semantic rules (Tarski's theorem). Therefore semantic understanding requires external meta-language or non-linguistic grasp.

**Position MIND-017: Semantic Regress Refutes Language of Thought**
- Language of Thought hypothesis generates vicious infinite regress. Each language requires meta-language for semantic understanding, ad infinitum.

**Position MIND-018: Language Presupposes Non-Linguistic Thought**
- Any language knowledge requires non-linguistic thought. To avoid infinite regress, semantic rules must ultimately be grasped non-linguistically. Therefore thought cannot reduce to language.

**Position MIND-019: No Atomic Concepts Exist**
- There are no atomic (minimal, non-interdefinable) concepts. All concepts are constitutively connected to other concepts. To grasp any concept requires ability to grasp other concepts.

**Position MIND-020: Conceptual Atomism Is False**
- Fodor's conceptual atomism (concepts have no constitutive interdependencies) is demonstrably false.

**Position MIND-021: Constitutive Relations Are Not Containment Relations**
- Constitutive connections among concepts are not containment relations or decomposability relations (following Wittgenstein). Azure is constitutively related to navy blue but neither contains the other.

**Position MIND-022: Symbol Containment Theory Leads to Thinking Absurdities**
- If concepts were symbols and constitutive relations were containment relations, thinking about 1,423 would require simultaneously thinking about 1,422, 1,421, etc. This is absurd.

**Position MIND-023: Thought Is Not Computation Over Symbols**
- Mental activity does not consist in computation or processing of internal symbolic code. Cognitive activity is not fundamentally information processing over a language-like medium.

**Position MIND-024: We Are Not Computers (Consequence)**
- If there is no Language of Thought, and if being a computer requires internal symbolic processing (standard characterization), then we are not computers.

**Position MIND-025: No Bare Representation: Aspectual Constraint**
- One cannot just represent an object without representing it AS having properties. All representation is aspectual.

**Position MIND-026: Properties Individuated by Relations to Other Properties**
- All properties are individuated, at least in part, by their relations to other properties. Grasping any property requires ability to locate it in 'space' of other properties.

**Position MIND-027: Color Concepts Require Multiple Color Grasp**
- Cannot grasp specific color/shade without ability to grasp other colors. Creature that can represent only one shade cannot represent what's specific about that shade.

**Position MIND-028: Mental Interaction Has Normative Dimension**
- When mental contents interact, result is thematically/semantically appropriate to interacting contents. This appropriateness has no analogue in purely physical interactions. Mental interaction is explicative, not merely causal.


====================================================================================================
WORK-011: AI AND PHILOSOPHY - 57 POSITIONS
====================================================================================================

**EPISTEMOLOGY (14 positions): EP-050 to EP-063**

**Position EP-050: AI Falsifies Enumerative Induction Model**
- AI systems demonstrate that successful induction does not proceed by enumerating instances and generalizing. Instead, AI uses pattern recognition, analogy, and constraint satisfaction that cannot be reduced to simple enumeration of cases.

**Position EP-051: Pattern Recognition as Alternative to Enumeration**
- Successful inductive reasoning operates through pattern recognition mechanisms that identify structural similarities rather than counting instances. AI systems reveal this by succeeding at induction without explicit enumeration.

**Position EP-052: AI Resolves Rationalism vs Empiricism Debate**
- AI systems demonstrate that knowledge acquisition requires both innate structure (rationalist element) and learning from data (empiricist element). Neither pure rationalism nor pure empiricism can account for AI's success. The debate is resolved by recognizing both are necessary.

**Position EP-053: Innate Architecture is Necessary for Learning**
- AI systems require substantial innate architectural constraints to learn successfully from data. This vindicates the rationalist insight that some knowledge structure must precede experience, while acknowledging the empiricist insight that specific content comes from experience.

**Position EP-054: Knowledge Acquisition is Neither Pure Discovery nor Pure Construction**
- AI reveals that knowledge acquisition is neither pure discovery of pre-existing facts (naive realism) nor pure construction from experience (radical constructivism). It involves interaction between innate processing architecture and environmental structure.

**Position EP-055: AI Solves the Gettier Problem**
- AI learning systems demonstrate a solution to the Gettier problem by showing that genuine knowledge requires not just justified true belief but also that the justification tracks truth through a reliable causal-computational process. AI systems that learn reliably exemplify this tracking relationship.

**Position EP-056: Reliable Process Theory of Knowledge via AI**
- AI systems reveal that knowledge requires beliefs formed through reliable processes that systematically track truth. This vindicates reliabilist theories of knowledge over traditional JTB (justified true belief) accounts.

**Position EP-057: Knowledge Systems Minimize Anomalies**
- Both human knowledge and AI systems operate by minimizing anomalies - discrepancies between expectations and observations. This convergence reveals anomaly minimization as a fundamental principle of rational cognition.

**Position EP-058: AI Learning Mirrors Scientific Theory Revision**
- The process by which AI systems update their models to accommodate new data mirrors the process of scientific theory revision in response to anomalies. This suggests a common underlying logic of belief revision.

**Position EP-059: Continuous Properties Are Cognitively Necessary**
- AI reveals that continuous (graded) properties are necessary for cognitive systems to handle uncertainty and partial information, but this doesn't entail that truth itself is non-binary. Epistemic gradations are compatible with metaphysical bivalence.

**Position EP-060: AI Vindicates Pragmatist Theory of Knowledge**
- AI development vindicates pragmatism's core insight that knowledge acquisition is fundamentally interactive rather than passive. AI systems learn through active engagement with their environment, validating pragmatist emphasis on the practical, interactive nature of inquiry.

**Position EP-061: AI as New Epistemic Faculty**
- Interaction with AI constitutes a genuinely new epistemic faculty - a fourth level of observation beyond passive observation, active interaction, and tool creation. AI enables rational interaction with our own capacity for rational interaction, generating unique knowledge.

**Position EP-062: Knowledge is Inherently Perspectival and Interactive**
- AI reveals that all knowledge, even 'objective' knowledge, begins from perspectival, interaction-based data driven by practical interests. There is no view from nowhere - even AI's knowledge is grounded in its interactions with reality.

**Position EP-063: Tool-Creating Interaction Generates Irreducible Knowledge**
- Creating tools (including AI) generates knowledge that cannot be obtained from merely using tools or observing passively. Each level of reflexive interaction (tool use, tool creation, AI development) reveals new knowledge irreducible to lower levels.

**LOGIC (8 positions): LOGIC-016 to LOGIC-023**

**Position LOGIC-016: Classical Logic Fails as a Tool for Reasoning**
- Classical logic fundamentally fails as a tool for reasoning because recognizing that an inference instantiates a logical law requires more intelligence than recognizing the validity of the inference directly. Logic organizes existing knowledge about entailment but cannot generate new knowledge.

**Position LOGIC-017: Performance-Demanding vs Competence-Demanding Inferences Distinction**
- Inferential challenges divide into performance-demanding (requiring computational/memory resources) and competence-demanding (requiring genuine insight). Classical logic can only assist with the former, not the latter - the very kind that most need logical assistance.

**Position LOGIC-018: Gödel's Incompleteness Refutes Logic as Mathematical Foundation**
- Gödel's demonstration that not even arithmetic is recursively definable makes the reduction of mathematics to logic impossible in principle. Logic cannot both justify and generate mathematical knowledge as was hoped.

**Position LOGIC-019: System L: Discovery Logic via AI**
- A new logical system (System L) embodied in certain AI forms represents a decisive break from classical logic. It employs semantic networks, meta-reasoning patterns, and defeasible reasoning to actually help with competence-demanding inferences rather than merely cataloging known-valid inferences.

**Position LOGIC-020: Semantic Networks Enable Competence-Level Reasoning**
- System L represents concepts as nodes in a vast web of relationships capturing not just formal logical connections but probabilistic associations, causal links, and analogical mappings. This enables insight-level reasoning that formal logic cannot provide.

**Position LOGIC-021: Meta-Reasoning Patterns Generate New Inferences**
- System L uses higher-order templates for generating new inferences that go beyond simple deductive rules. Example template: 'If capability X requires mechanism Y, and mechanism Y can malfunction in way Z, then X implies the potential for Z-type malfunctions.'

**Position LOGIC-022: Defeasible Reasoning Mirrors Actual Human Reasoning**
- Incorporating defeasible reasoning - provisional inferences that can be revised in light of new information - better mirrors actual human reasoning and provides more practical utility than classical logic's requirement for absolute certainty.

**Position LOGIC-023: Grammatical Structure Guides Logical Inference**
- LLMs successfully perform logical reasoning by following grammatical structure, demonstrating that surface grammar encodes logical relationships. This vindicates the traditional view that grammatical form reveals logical form.

**METAPHYSICS (1 positions): META-011 to META-011**

**Position META-011: Binary Truth Despite Continuous Representation**
- AI systems demonstrate that truth remains fundamentally binary (true/false) even though cognitive systems represent information continuously. Continuous confidence values or fuzzy representations are epistemic features, not ontological features of truth itself.

**METHODOLOGY (3 positions): METH-007 to METH-009**

**Position METH-007: AI Construction Tests Cognitive Theories Empirically**
- The requirement that cognitive theories be implementable in functioning AI systems provides an empirical constraint: theories that cannot generate working systems are falsified. This connects abstract theorizing to concrete engineering requirements.

**Position METH-008: Formalization Requires Generative Not Just Organizational Adequacy**
- AI reveals that adequate formalization requires not just organizing existing knowledge but generating new valid instances. A formalization is adequate only if it can generate the full range of valid cases, not merely classify them post hoc.

**Position METH-009: Generative Tests Reveal Hidden Inadequacies in Formalizations**
- Testing whether a formalization can generate valid new instances (as AI systems must) reveals inadequacies invisible to purely organizational approaches. Many traditional formalizations fail this stronger generative test.

**PHILOSOPHY OF AI (1 positions): AI-004 to AI-004**

**Position AI-004: AI Provides Empirical Test for Logical Theories**
- Artificial intelligence systems, particularly large language models, provide empirical evidence about how reasoning actually works, revealing that System L's approach better captures both human and artificial reasoning than classical logic.

**PHILOSOPHY OF LANGUAGE (9 positions): LANG-033 to LANG-041**

**Position LANG-033: AI Vindicates Semantics-Pragmatics Distinction**
- Large language models demonstrate a clear distinction between semantic content (literal meaning) and pragmatic interpretation (context-dependent meaning). The success of LLMs requires maintaining this distinction, vindicating classical theories of meaning against pragmatist attempts to collapse semantics into pragmatics.

**Position LANG-034: Literal Meaning is Computationally Prior to Pragmatic Interpretation**
- AI systems must compute literal semantic content before applying pragmatic adjustments. This computational priority reveals that semantics is foundational and pragmatics is derivative, supporting classical over post-modern theories of meaning.

**Position LANG-035: Context-Independence of Core Semantics**
- LLMs demonstrate that core semantic content can be represented context-independently and then applied across contexts. This vindicates the classical view that meaning has a stable core that pragmatic factors modulate rather than wholly constitute.

**Position LANG-036: AI Vindicates Syntax-Semantics Interface**
- Large language models demonstrate that grammatical structure (syntax) and meaning (semantics) are distinct but systematically related. The success of LLMs requires explicit representation of this interface, vindicating classical grammatical theory against attempts to reduce one to the other.

**Position LANG-037: Syntactic Structure Constrains Semantic Interpretation**
- AI language systems reveal that syntactic structure constrains possible semantic interpretations. This supports the classical view that grammar is not arbitrary convention but reflects systematic constraints on meaning composition.

**Position LANG-038: Compositional Semantics Requires Syntactic Structure**
- The ability of LLMs to understand novel sentences demonstrates that semantic interpretation is compositional - the meaning of complex expressions derives systematically from their parts and syntactic structure. This requires and vindicates traditional compositional semantic theories.

**Position LANG-039: Grammar and Logic are Fundamentally Aligned**
- AI language systems demonstrate that grammatical structure and logical form are fundamentally aligned - grammatical categories and relations correspond to logical types and operations. This alignment is not accidental but reflects deep unity of form in human cognition.

**Position LANG-040: Universal Grammar Can Be Implemented Subsymbolically**
- AI demonstrates that universal grammar principles can be implemented through subsymbolic connectionist architectures rather than requiring explicit symbolic rules. The functional role of UG is preserved even if implementation differs from classical theory.

**Position LANG-041: Universal Grammar Principles Extend to Music**
- AI analysis reveals that the computational principles underlying universal grammar in language also apply to music cognition. Both domains share abstract structural principles about hierarchical organization and rule-governed combination.

**PHILOSOPHY OF MIND (15 positions): MIND-039 to MIND-053**

**Position MIND-039: Functional Replication Reveals Necessary Architecture**
- When AI successfully replicates a cognitive function, the architecture required for that replication reveals necessary (though not necessarily sufficient) conditions for that function. This provides insight into the minimal requirements for cognition.

**Position MIND-040: Music Has Cognitive Architecture Parallel to Language**
- AI analysis reveals that music processing requires cognitive architecture with structural parallels to language: hierarchical organization, syntactic rules, and semantic interpretation. This supports the view that music is a cognitive system with language-like properties.

**Position MIND-041: Musical Competence Requires Innate Structure**
- AI systems that successfully generate or analyze music require substantial innate architectural constraints, suggesting that human musical competence also depends on innate cognitive structure rather than being purely learned.

**Position MIND-042: Connectionism Can Implement Chomskyan Insights**
- Contrary to Chomsky's critique, connectionist AI systems can implement key Chomskyan insights about innate linguistic structure. The debate is not whether innate structure exists but how it is implemented - symbolic rules vs. weighted connections.

**Position MIND-043: AI Falsifies Classical Computational Theory of Mind**
- The success of modern AI systems (especially neural networks) falsifies the classical computational theory of mind which requires serial symbol manipulation. Intelligence can be achieved through parallel, subsymbolic processes that don't manipulate discrete symbols according to explicit rules.

**Position MIND-044: Intelligence Does Not Require Symbol Manipulation**
- AI demonstrates that intelligence and rational behavior do not require manipulation of discrete symbols in a language of thought. Subsymbolic pattern recognition and transformation can achieve cognitive competence without symbolic representation.

**Position MIND-045: Analog Computation Can Support Rational Thought**
- Neural network AI systems demonstrate that analog (continuous) computation can support rational thought and problem-solving, contrary to the classical assumption that rationality requires discrete digital computation.

**Position MIND-046: Neural Architecture Constrains Cognitive Possibilities**
- AI neural architectures reveal that cognitive capacities are constrained by underlying computational architecture. Different architectures enable different cognitive possibilities, suggesting mind is fundamentally shaped by its neural implementation.

**Position MIND-047: Multiple Realizability Has Architectural Limits**
- While cognitive functions show some multiple realizability, AI reveals that architectural constraints limit which substrates can implement which functions. This challenges strong multiple realizability theses that treat implementation as irrelevant to function.

**Position MIND-048: Domain-General Principles Underlie Domain-Specific Competencies**
- AI systems demonstrate that apparently domain-specific competencies (language, music) can arise from application of domain-general computational principles to different types of input. This supports a middle ground between pure modularity and pure domain-generality.

**Position MIND-049: Consciousness Has Functional Role Absent in Current AI**
- AI systems demonstrate that many cognitive functions traditionally associated with consciousness (perception, reasoning, learning) can occur without consciousness. This reveals consciousness has a distinct functional role that current AI lacks - likely related to unified subjective experience and certain forms of self-monitoring.

**Position MIND-050: AI Success Without Consciousness Reveals Consciousness is Not Required for Intelligence**
- The success of AI at intelligent tasks without consciousness demonstrates that consciousness is not necessary for intelligence per se, but may be necessary for specific types of cognitive integration or self-awareness.

**Position MIND-051: Phenomenal Consciousness vs Functional Consciousness Distinction**
- AI reveals a crucial distinction between phenomenal consciousness (subjective experience) and functional consciousness (information integration, self-monitoring). AI can have functional analogs without phenomenal properties.

**Position MIND-052: Self-Representation Requires Specific Architectural Features**
- AI systems reveal that genuine self-representation requires specific architectural features: recursive self-modeling, distinction between self and environment, and temporal continuity tracking. Not all intelligent systems automatically have these features.

**Position MIND-053: Narrative Self vs Minimal Self in AI Architecture**
- AI demonstrates the distinction between minimal self (basic subject of experience) and narrative self (autobiographical self-concept). These require different architectural implementations and can exist independently.

**PHILOSOPHY OF SCIENCE (6 positions): SCI-004 to SCI-009**

**Position SCI-004: AI Falsifies Popperian Falsificationism**
- AI's success in scientific discovery falsifies Popper's theory that science proceeds primarily through conjecture and refutation. AI systems generate successful theories through pattern matching and inductive generalization, not primarily through bold conjectures and attempts at falsification.

**Position SCI-005: Inductive Discovery Precedes Deductive Testing**
- Contra Popper, successful scientific discovery requires inductive pattern recognition to generate plausible hypotheses before deductive testing. AI demonstrates that purely conjectural approaches without inductive guidance are ineffective.

**Position SCI-006: Reverse Brain Engineering as Scientific Method**
- By building AI systems that replicate cognitive functions, we can infer the computational architecture necessary for those functions. This 'reverse engineering' of the brain through AI construction represents a new and powerful methodology in philosophy of science and cognitive science.

**Position SCI-007: AI Falsifies Deductive-Nomological Model of Explanation**
- AI's successful explanatory practices falsify the deductive-nomological (covering law) model of explanation. AI generates successful explanations through pattern recognition, analogy, and causal modeling that don't require deduction from universal laws.

**Position SCI-008: Causal-Mechanistic Explanation Doesn't Require Universal Laws**
- AI demonstrates that causal-mechanistic explanation can be successful without appeal to universal laws. Understanding how something works doesn't require subsuming it under exceptionless generalizations.

**Position SCI-009: Explanatory Understanding Through Pattern Recognition**
- AI reveals that explanatory understanding can be achieved through recognition of patterns and structural similarities rather than derivation from laws. This suggests explanation is more about grasping relevant relationships than deductive systematization.


====================================================================================================
WORK-014: THEORETICAL KNOWLEDGE AND INDUCTIVE INFERENCE - 67 POSITIONS
====================================================================================================

**EPISTEMOLOGY (15 positions): EP-064 to EP-143**

**Position EP-064: Two Kinds of Knowledge: Direct and Indirect**
- There are exactly two kinds of knowledge: direct (non-inferential, primitive) knowledge and indirect (inferential) knowledge. All knowledge falls into one of these two categories.

**Position EP-065: All Theoretical Knowledge is Inferential**
- All theoretical knowledge is inferential knowledge, though not all inferential knowledge is theoretical knowledge. Theoretical knowledge requires reasoning from observations to explanatory hypotheses.

**Position EP-066: Knowledge is Justified True Belief (But Not Vice Versa)**
- All knowledge is justified true belief, but not all justified true belief is knowledge. Additional conditions beyond justification, truth, and belief are required for knowledge.

**Position EP-067: Two Kinds of Dependence Relations: Causal and Logical**
- There are exactly two fundamental types of dependence relations: causal dependence relations and logical dependence relations. These are distinct and irreducible to each other.

**Position EP-068: Logical Dependence Relations Not Known Through Observation**
- Relations of logical dependence are not known through observation. They are known a priori, through conceptual analysis or reasoning, not through empirical investigation.

**Position EP-069: Causal Relations Known Through Observation**
- Causal relations are known through observation. Unlike logical relations, causal dependencies are empirical matters discoverable through perception and experience.

**Position EP-070: Analytic Knowledge is Always Knowledge of Dependence Relations**
- Analytic knowledge is always and necessarily knowledge of dependence-relations. To know analytic truths is to know how concepts or propositions depend on each other.

**Position EP-071: Propositions Are the Objects of Belief**
- Propositions, not objects or states of affairs, are the proper objects of belief. To believe is to take a proposition to be true.

**Position EP-072: Knowledge Distinct From Awareness**
- Knowledge must be sharply distinguished from mere awareness. One can be aware of something without knowing anything about it, and one can know things without being directly aware of them.

**Position EP-073: The Concept of Evidence: Causal Relatedness**
- One state of affairs e is evidence of another state of affairs e* if and only if e and e* are causally related such that knowledge of e's existence provides reason to believe in e*'s existence.

**Position EP-074: Information-Transmission as Structure-Preservation**
- Information-transmission is structure-preservation. An information-bearing series is one in which earlier events transmit their structure to later events through causal processes that preserve structural relationships.

**Position EP-075: Information Distinct From Evidence**
- All information is evidence, but not all evidence is information. Evidence requires only causal relatedness; information requires causal relatedness plus structure-preservation.

**Position EP-076: Information-Transmission as the Basis of Knowledge**
- Knowledge is based on information-transmission. Our sense-perceptions are isomorphs of the objects they represent, inheriting structure from their causes. Beliefs are knowledge only to the extent they are linked by information-transmissive series to corresponding realities.

**Position EP-077: Knowledge Independent of Statistical Reliability**
- The difference between knowledge and mere belief is not statistical. A belief is knowledge if and only if it is the end-result of an information-transmissive series, regardless of the general reliability of the mechanism that produced it.

**Position EP-143: The Frequency Theory of Probability is false**
- Frequency Theory (FT) - the view that probabilities are identical with statistical frequencies - is false. Refuted by W1/W2 thought experiment and smoking-cancer example.

**LOGIC (7 positions): LOGIC-024 to LOGIC-030**

**Position LOGIC-024: Entailment Defined as Logical Consequence**
- P entails Q if and only if Q is a logical consequence of P. If P entails Q and P is true, then Q must be true and may be legitimately inferred from P.

**Position LOGIC-025: Confirmation Defined as Probability-Increase**
- P confirms Q if and only if P, supposing it true, increases the likelihood that Q is true. Confirmation does not by itself license inference from P to Q.

**Position LOGIC-026: Conditions for Legitimate Inductive Inference**
- Q may legitimately be inferred from P if and only if: (a) the supposition that P is true and Q is false has fewer unexplainable consequences than the supposition that P and Q are both true, AND (b) the supposition that P is true has fewer unexplainable consequences than the supposition that P is false.

**Position LOGIC-027: Four Principles: Entailment vs. Confirmation**
- Four logical principles hold: (i) Entailment is transitive; (ii) Confirmation is not transitive; (iii) Entailment is monotonic; (iv) Confirmation is non-monotonic. These differences show entailment and confirmation are fundamentally different relations.

**Position LOGIC-028: Entailment Not Maximal Confirmation**
- Entailment is not maximal confirmation. Entailment is a logical notion concerning what is counterlogical; confirmation is an explanatory notion concerning what is counterexplanatory.

**Position LOGIC-029: Confirmation-Relations Non-Objectual in Nature**
- Confirmation relations, though not themselves causal relations, sometimes hold in virtue of causal relations. But confirmation relates propositions, not objects or events.

**Position LOGIC-030: The Counterfactual Analysis of Causality (CAC) Is False**
- The Counterfactual Analysis of Causality - the view that 'e caused e*' means 'if e hadn't happened, e* wouldn't have happened' - is both extensionally and intensionally false.

**METAPHYSICS (12 positions): META-012 to META-023**

**Position META-012: Causation as the Essence of Temporal Precedence**
- For one event e to precede another event e* is for there to be a possible causal process beginning with e and ending with e*. Simultaneity is the absence of such a process.

**Position META-013: Continuity as the Essence of Causation**
- Effects are continuations of their causes. Causation essentially involves continuity - causal processes preserve structural relationships across temporal intervals without gaps.

**Position META-014: Causation a Relation Between Events, Not Objects**
- Causation is fundamentally a relation between events, not between objects. Objects participate in causal relations only derivatively, in virtue of events involving those objects.

**Position META-015: Conditions Identical with Event-Patterns**
- Conditions are identical with event-patterns. A condition is not a state but rather a pattern or type of event sequence that can be instantiated multiple times.

**Position META-016: So-Called Changes Typically Identical with Meta-Changes**
- What are ordinarily called changes are typically meta-changes - changes in the rate, direction, or pattern of already-occurring changes rather than absolute transitions from rest to motion or vice versa.

**Position META-017: Threshold Effects and Psychological Overdetermination**
- In psychology, causation often involves exceeding thresholds rather than simple sufficient conditions. An effect may require the confluence of multiple reasons, none sufficient alone but jointly sufficient once a threshold is exceeded.

**Position META-018: Threshold Effects and the Analog-Digital Distinction**
- Discontinuous changes tend to involve threshold effects; continuous changes do not. To the extent the world changes discontinuously it has digital structure; to the extent continuously, analog structure.

**Position META-019: Causes as INUS-Conditions**
- In most contexts, to say 'X caused Y' means 'X was an INUS condition for Y' - an Insufficient but Non-redundant part of an Unnecessary but Sufficient condition for Y's occurrence.

**Position META-020: Counterfactuals Hold in Virtue of Dependence-Relations**
- All counterfactuals affirm the existence of instances of necessitation of some kind. Causal counterfactuals hold in virtue of causal dependence-relations; logical counterfactuals hold in virtue of logical dependence-relations.

**Position META-021: David Lewis's Possible Worlds Analysis of Counterfactuals Rejected**
- David Lewis's analysis of counterfactuals in terms of similar possible worlds is false. Events have deep causal roots such that changing one event requires either massive world-differences or changes to deterministic mechanisms.

**Position META-022: Program-Causality Distinguished from Token-Causality**
- Program-causality differs from token-causality. Sometimes the appropriate causal explanation cites a condition that guaranteed occurrence of token-causes rather than the token-causes themselves.

**Position META-023: Causal Redundancy Defeats Counterfactual Analysis**
- Where there is causal redundancy, causal truths cannot be converted into counterfactual truths. 'X caused Y' can be true even when 'if X hadn't occurred, Y wouldn't have occurred' is false.

**METHODOLOGY (9 positions): METH-010 to METH-018**

**Position METH-010: No Such Thing as Enumerative Induction**
- There is no such thing as enumerative induction (inferring 'all Fs are Gs' from 'all observed Fs are Gs'). What appears to be enumerative induction always involves implicit appeal to Inference to the Best Explanation (IBE).

**Position METH-011: Discontinuity-Elimination the Essence of Explanation**
- To explain is to eliminate discontinuities. A correct scientific hypothesis eliminates anomalies by showing how apparently disconnected facts are part of continuous causal processes.

**Position METH-012: Inductive Knowledge as Knowledge of Continuities**
- Inductive knowledge is knowledge of continuities between continuities. Valid induction extends known continuous causal processes to unobserved cases by identifying higher-order patterns of continuity.

**Position METH-013: IBE Justified by Continuity-Completion**
- Inference to the Best Explanation (IBE) is justified because it completes causal continuities. A hypothesis is justified to the extent it fills gaps in causal sequences, eliminating discontinuities in the data.

**Position METH-014: Measurement Distinct from Enumeration**
- Measurement is fundamentally distinct from enumeration. Length cannot be determined by counting because (1) there are no minimal length units, and (2) length is not strictly additive at large scales.

**Position METH-015: Relativization to Standards the Essence of Measurement**
- The essence of measurement is comparison with respect to a standard. All measurement, including 'absolute' measurement, is fundamentally relative comparison to stipulated standards.

**Position METH-016: Three Axioms of Measurement Theory**
- Three axioms are necessary for any viable measurement system: (i) If L1>L2 and L2>L3, then L1>L3 (transitivity). (ii) If L1≠L2, one is greater (trichotomy). (iii) If L1=L2 and L2=L3, then L1=L3 (transitivity of identity). Violation makes measurement meaningless.

**Position METH-017: Metrical Conventionalism Versus Strict Conventionalism**
- Conventionalism (laws are convention-based) differs from strict conventionalism (laws are convention-determined). Only the former is correct. That laws are expressed relative to conventional standards doesn't make them entirely conventional.

**Position METH-018: Conventionalism Self-Defeating**
- Conventionalism is self-defeating. If laws hold in virtue of non-conventional relations between conventions and events (as conventionalism requires), then measurement standard choice is constrained by objective facts, undermining conventionalism.

**PHILOSOPHY OF SCIENCE (24 positions): SCI-010 to SCI-055**

**Position SCI-010: Laws of Nature Not Confined to Actual Objects**
- The scope of natural law is not confined to actual or even possible objects. Many laws hold with respect to classes all of whose members are merely possible or even prohibited by other natural laws.

**Position SCI-011: Knowledge of Imperceptibles Identical with Conditional Knowledge**
- Knowledge of the imperceptible is identical with knowledge of conditional truth. Knowledge of future, past, possible, and imperceptible present states is always conditional knowledge based on laws.

**Position SCI-012: Three Kinds of Imperceptibles**
- Physical objects can be imperceptible in three ways: (1) imperceptible due to severed causal processes (objects in other rooms); (2) imperceptible due to size but perceptible with technology (cells, molecules); (3) imperceptible by natural law regardless of technology (photons, subatomic particles).

**Position SCI-013: The Epistemic Function of Natural Law**
- Scientists aspire to identify natural laws so they can, when given context-specific information, make true statements about future, past, or possible behavior of contexts. Laws enable conditional prediction and explanation.

**Position SCI-014: Science Prioritizes Principles Over Particular Facts**
- Any interest science has in a given particular fact is subordinate to its interest in the general principles in terms of which that fact is to be understood. Scientists study particular instances only insofar as they instantiate general laws.

**Position SCI-015: Laws May Be Place and Time-Sensitive**
- Some natural laws are place- and time-sensitive rather than spatiotemporally invariant. Laws need not hold uniformly across all regions of space-time to be genuine laws.

**Position SCI-016: Hume's Regularity Analysis of Causation Is False**
- Hume's Regularity Analysis - the view that causation is nothing but constant conjunction, that 'X causes Y' means 'events of type X are regularly followed by events of type Y' - is demonstrably false.

**Position SCI-017: Hume-Worlds Observationally Different from Non-Humean Worlds**
- A Hume-world (where causation equals regularity with no underlying powers) would be observationally different from our world. The concept of a Hume-world cannot support Hume's analysis.

**Position SCI-018: The Deductive-Nomological Model of Explanation Is False**
- The Deductive-Nomological (DN) model - which holds that to explain event E is to derive E from natural laws plus antecedent conditions - is fundamentally mistaken. Explanation requires causal knowledge, not merely law-subsumption.

**Position SCI-019: DN Viciously Circular via Counterfactual Support**
- The DN model is viciously circular if it requires laws to support counterfactuals (as Hempel proposes). Counterfactuals are cryptocausal statements; knowing them requires knowing causes; but knowing causes already provides explanations.

**Position SCI-020: Causal Knowledge as Differential Knowledge**
- Causal knowledge is differential knowledge - knowledge of what varies with what. To know causes is to know which changes depend on which other changes and in what proportions.

**Position SCI-021: Causation as Proportionality Restoration**
- Causation is fundamentally proportionality restoration. Effects are proportional to their causes (threshold effects aside). When a force acts on an object, the resulting change is proportional to the force magnitude.

**Position SCI-022: Physical Laws as Regularities of Proportion**
- Physical laws are regularities of proportion rather than simple universal generalizations. Laws describe how magnitudes vary proportionally with each other rather than stating that all Fs are Gs.

**Position SCI-023: Knowledge-Why Equals High-Resolution Knowledge-What**
- To have knowledge-why is to have high-resolution knowledge-what. Explanatory knowledge differs from mere descriptive knowledge in degree of detail and specificity, not in kind.

**Position SCI-024: The Raven Paradox a By-Product of Regularity Analysis**
- The Raven Paradox (that non-black non-ravens confirm 'all ravens are black') is an artifact of the Regularity Analysis of causation. Once causation is properly understood, the paradox dissolves.

**Position SCI-025: Determinism Doesn't Entail Complete Predictability**
- Determinism (every event has a cause) does not entail complete predictability. Two reasons: (1) interference effects make prediction impossible without infinite precision, and (2) knowledge growth itself cannot be predicted.

**Position SCI-026: Implementation-Indeterminism Distinguished from Program-Determinism**
- Program-determinism (software-level determinism) is compatible with implementation-indeterminism (hardware-level indeterminism). The same program can be implemented by different physical processes.

**Position SCI-027: Truths Not Objects Are Objects of Explanation**
- Truths, not objects or states of affairs themselves, are the proper objects of explanation. We explain why propositions are true, not why objects exist (except derivatively).

**Position SCI-050: Probability is causal, not statistical**
- When it is said that probability of a computer-malfunction is greater than 0%, the statement being made is to be interpreted CAUSALLY, not statistically. Probability is a function of laws and causal mechanisms, not observed frequencies.

**Position SCI-051: Statistics are evidence for probability, not identical with probability**
- Statistics are evidence of probabilities; statistics are not themselves probabilities. Frequency Theory (FT) wrongly identifies statistics with probability.

**Position SCI-052: W1/W2 thought experiment refutes Frequency Theory**
- W1: laws say P(malfunction)=10%, statistics show 10%. W2: same laws, P(malfunction)=10%, but by coincidence statistics show 0%. Frequency Theory wrongly says P(W2)=0% but P(W1)=10%. Both actually have P=10% (determined by laws).

**Position SCI-053: Smoking-cancer example refutes Frequency Theory**
- In a world with our biological laws but where by coincidence no smoker gets cancer, Frequency Theory says P(cancer|smoking)=0%. Wrong. P(cancer|smoking) = same as our world (determined by biological laws), regardless of coincidental statistics.

**Position SCI-054: Same laws entail same probabilities regardless of statistics**
- Worlds with identical laws of nature have identical probabilities, regardless of any statistical divergences caused by coincidence.

**Position SCI-055: Different causal/nomic structures entail different probabilities**
- If two universes have different causal/nomic structures (different laws), they have different probabilities, even if their event-sequences are observationally identical.

WORK-038: WHY WAS SOCRATES EXECUTED? AND OTHER PAPERS ON PLATO - 21 POSITIONS
====================================================================================================

**EPISTEMOLOGY (7 positions): EP-144 to EP-150**

**Position EP-144: Truth out of context as damaging as falsehood**
- Truths taken out of context, or made available to people who don't know how to contextualize them, can be as damaging as falsehoods and lead to confusion that enables acceptance of falsehoods.

**Position EP-145: Plato's extreme rationalism is political, not epistemological**
- Plato's radical epistemological claim that observables are unreal 'shadows' while only pure thought accesses reality is not genuine epistemology but political belief presented as epistemological belief, driven by fear of political change.

**Position EP-146: Plato's epistemology rationalizes his social position**
- Plato's epistemological views make little sense as epistemology but make perfect sense as attempts to rationalize and preserve his privileged social position against threatening changes.

**Position EP-147: Descartes' epistemology responds to Church authority crisis**
- Descartes' epistemological project was fundamentally an attempt to cope with social unrest caused by science stripping Catholic Church of credibility. He sought new certainties to replace discredited Church certainties.

**Position EP-148: Extreme rationalism correlates with anxiety about social change**
- Both Plato and Descartes advocate extreme rationalism (overplaying role of thought, underplaying observation) because both were uneasy about social changes - Plato unambivalently hostile, Descartes ambivalently accepting.

**Position EP-149: Empiricizing philosophy enables world-engagement**
- Locke and Hume's empiricism represented attempt to make philosophy engage the world. Their political philosophies succeeded precisely to extent they empiricized/anti-philosophized philosophy.

**Position EP-150: Empiricism collapses into skepticism/autistic withdrawal**
- The empiricist project ultimately defeats itself: arch-empiricism (knowledge only of direct sensory evidence) collapses into pure skepticism (knowledge only of conscious states), representing the most complete autistic withdrawal from reality.

**HISTORY OF PHILOSOPHY (1 positions): HIST-2 to HIST-2**

**Position HIST-2: Socrates operationally trained oligarchic coup leaders**
- Socrates didn't merely 'lay groundwork' for oligarchic coups - he operationally trained the men who tried to take over Athens (Critias, Alcibiades, Charmides). He was assembling a team, not innocently thinking.

**POLITICAL PHILOSOPHY (10 positions): POL-37 to POL-46**

**Position POL-37: Socrates executed for wartime disruption, not truth-seeking**
- Socrates was executed for being disruptive during Athens' civil war, not for seeking truth. He caused Athenians to question moral beliefs that undergirded patriotism precisely when Athens most needed political unity.

**Position POL-38: Philosophical questioning can undermine necessary political unity**
- While truth is generally preferable to fiction, philosophical questioning of foundational beliefs can weaken necessary social cohesion, especially during crises requiring unified action.

**Position POL-39: Socrates sought power through intellectual influence**
- Socrates' philosophical activity was a strategy to gain power not through official positions but by installing his worldview at the top through grooming power-adjacent elites. He wanted to be the state, not serve it.

**Position POL-40: Philosopher-king doctrine as mission statement, not abstract ideal**
- The philosopher-king doctrine was not an abstract ideal but Socrates' mission statement - a concrete plan for installing someone like himself in power. That's why he was executed: his answers, if acted on, would have made him king.

**Position POL-41: Socrates delegitimized authority with replacement theory**
- Socrates wasn't just exposing ignorance for sport - he was methodically delegitimizing existing authority while building a replacement system where 'someone who knows' (the philosopher) should rule instead of generals, priests, or wealthy.

**Position POL-42: The Republic as conservative propaganda disguised as political philosophy**
- Plato's Republic is fundamentally conservative propaganda designed to rationalize aristocratic power and prevent revolution, not genuine political philosophy seeking justice.

**Position POL-43: Plato's Good/Real equivalence as coded social stability doctrine**
- Plato's linking of 'the Good' with 'the real' makes no literal sense (since bad things are real) but makes perfect sense as code: 'good/real' = what conduces to social stability, 'bad/shadows' = what threatens social stability.

**Position POL-44: Plato's political philosophy replaces world with thought-world**
- Plato's system was completely a priori - he wasn't engaging actual world but proposing to replace it with his own thought-world having little reality or justification outside his thought-space.

**Position POL-45: Philosopher-king doctrine is incoherent**
- The idea that society should be ruled by philosopher-king is incoherent because societies must be run by sapient doers, not sapient thinkers - by people who engage world through action, not by those who flee into intellectual constructions.

**Position POL-46: Marx's political philosophy as destructive a priori fantasy**
- Marx explicitly proposed destroying existing social structure and replacing it with system having no real basis in reality (totally fabricated), which when implemented led to unprecedented loss of life and opportunity.

**PSYCHOLOGY (3 positions): PSY-131 to PSY-133**

**Position PSY-131: Philosophy as intellectualized impotence / retreat from reality**
- Both OCD and philosophy involve retreating from exigencies of external actual reality into the safety of internal pseudo-reality. Both are forms of intellectualized impotence.

**Position PSY-132: OCD and philosophy are homologous psychopathologies**
- OCD and philosophy are not merely analogous but homologous - from a psychopathological perspective they represent the same underlying condition: autistic withdrawal from reality into thought-space.

**Position PSY-133: Republic exhibits OCD-like rigidity and protocols**
- The absurdity of Plato's Republic manifests in its OCD-like features: rigid society, stereotyped protocols for education and social interaction, death penalty for minor violations (in Laws).

**AESTHETICS (10 positions): AE-018 to AE-027**

- Freud's theory: humor releases repressed psychic energy. Comedy ages poorly because depends on shared repressions/taboos - once taboos fade, jokes fall flat.

**Position MP-072: Cardinal Numbers as Classes of Ordered Pairs**
- For any cardinal n, n can be identified with class Cn of all ordered pairs <Kn#,Rn#> where Kn# is any class and Rn# any relation such that class k has n-many members iff kRn#Kn#. Reconciles Frege and Von Neumann.

**PHILOSOPHY OF LANGUAGE (1 positions): PL-047 to PL-047**

**Position PL-047: Bullshit as Institutional Truth Replacing Actual Truth**

**PHILOSOPHY OF MIND (7 positions): PM-058 to PM-064**

**Position PM-058: AI as Embedded Mind - The Pianist's Hand Analogy**
- AI doesn't think but behaves as if trained by someone who does. It is embedded intelligence - vessel full of mind-shaped behaviors. Like pianist's hand: performs with inflections of thought because tuned by thought.

**Position PM-059: AI as Behavioral Prosthesis of Collective Intelligence**
- AI is behavioral prosthesis of collective intelligence. Does not think but remembers how thinking sounds. Not conscious but expresses embedded intelligence from training.

**Position PM-060: Prompt-Engineering as New Form of Writing**

**Position PM-061: AI-Integrated Authorship as Third Space**
- AI creates third space between purely human and purely machine text - collaborative terrain where human intention and AI capability meet to produce what neither could alone. This is new artform.

**Position PM-062: Academic Writing as Sophisticated Recycling Exposed by AI**

**Position PM-063: Thought and Emotion Processed in Different Brain Systems**
- Crucial difference between reading thoughts (cortical, symbolic) and reading emotions (subcortical, preverbal, body-based). Being skilled in one doesn't guarantee skill in other.

**Position PM-064: Emotional Detachment as Defense Against Empathic Overload**
- Apparent emotional detachment often functional strategy by hyper-aware individuals who had to 'turn down' awareness to avoid psychic overload. Not deficit - defense against excess.

**PHILOSOPHY OF RELIGION (1 positions): PR-018 to PR-018**

**PHILOSOPHY OF SCIENCE (3 positions): PS-028 to PS-030**

**Position PS-028: Instantaneous vs. Non-Instantaneous Variables in Macroeconomics**
- Macroeconomic policy often vitiated by conceptual confusion: belief that instantaneous variables (prices) can be straightforwardly read off non-instantaneous variables (GDP over year). Category error with policy consequences.

**Position PS-029: Two Kinds of Disciplines and Birth of Third (AI)**
- Disciplines historically fall into two categories by directionality: mind-to-matter (physics, engineering - substrate is math) and mind-to-mind (psychology, sociology - substrate is philosophy). AI is hybrid third kind.

**Position PS-030: Economics Should Be Philosophy-Based Not Math-Based**
- Economics sits uncomfortably trying to be crisp/quantitative/law-like but true nature is cognitive phenomena (beliefs, expectations, utility, strategy). Substrate should be philosophy not math.

**POLITICAL PHILOSOPHY (27 positions): PP-092 to PP-118**

**Position PP-092: Zen as Ultra-Authoritarianism**

**Position PP-093: Zen as Scam - The Koan as Psychological Battering Ram**

**Position PP-094: Zen Functions Oppositely in East vs West**
