**Position PP-095: Rawlsian Proceduralism as Civilizational Suicide**
- When Western civilization accepted proceduralism as its moral core, it signed its own death warrant. Proceduralism is elegant and scalable but dead inside - offering no conception of the good, only fairness.

**Position PP-096: In Democracy, Virtue Equals Bureaucracy**
- In procedural democracy, the only officially virtuous behavior is compliance with procedure. All other moral traits - courage, principle, loyalty - have no legal standing.

**Position PP-097: Democratic Systems Embody No Affirmative Morality**
- Pure democracy has no built-in conception of the good life - it is procedural mechanism, not moral framework. Meaningless systems are weak systems.

**Position PP-098: Proceduralism Makes Justice Expensive and Unattainable**
- Modern legal proceduralism transforms courtroom into stage for gamesmanship where justice depends on resources, not truth. Truth matters only if successfully formatted and introduced through proper channels.

**Position PP-099: Proceduralism is About Safety for Judge, Not Justice for Accused**
- Lawyers and judges love proceduralism because it keeps them physically safe by dissipating rage through abstraction, not because it produces justice.

**Position PP-100: Proceduralism Makes System More Punitive, Not Less**
- More proceduralist a legal system becomes, harsher its punishments - because when system finally proves guilt after vaulting labyrinth of hurdles, it throws the book at offender.

**Position PP-101: Proceduralism Probably Doesn't Lower Crime**
- Despite theory that procedural justice creates legitimacy reducing crime, US (most proceduralist system) has highest incarceration rate in developed world - suggesting proceduralism doesn't work as advertised.

**Position PP-102: There Are No Laws - Only a Legal System**
- Laws as objective, fairly-applied rules don't exist. What exists is a legal system - powerful and coercive, but outcomes depend on lawyer skill, resources, relationships, not 'the law'.

**Position PP-103: Every Procedural System Needs Moral Override**
- Purely procedural system will always fail because no rule set can account for every situation. Must include 'manual override clause' - structural way to be human when rules produce monstrosity.

**Position PP-104: Need for Evidentiary Override in Legal Systems**
- Legal systems need evidentiary override - formal recognition that truth sometimes appears out of order and innocence must not be overruled by filing error.

**Position PP-105: How to Build Scalable Legal System With Moral Override**
- Can design legal system that is scalable, predictable, commercially functional AND capable of recognizing when rules lead to absurd outcomes through three-layer architecture.

**Position PP-106: Law School Makes You Dumber**
- Legal education doesn't sharpen intellect - it blunts it. Doesn't cultivate truth-seeking - it conditions obedience. Is system designed to cripple independent judgment while masquerading as rigorous reasoning.

**Position PP-107: Lawyers Are Cognitively Crippled on Facts**
- Lawyers are clueless about facts not because stupid but because legal system is entirely proceduralist - trains them to follow procedure, not discover truth.

**Position PP-108: Circumscribed Psychopathy as Byproduct of Proceduralism**
- Lawyers display circumscribed psychopathy - not because evil but because system demands mind that can ignore reality when procedurally inconvenient.

**Position PP-109: Cognitive Homology Between Mafiosi and Lawyers**
- Mafiosi and lawyers undergo same cognitive mechanism - deliberate suppression of basic human drives. Mafioso suppresses empathy, lawyer suppresses truth-seeking. Same brain mechanisms.

**Position PP-110: Liberalism as Feminine and Therefore Doomed**
- Liberalism is fundamentally feminine archetype - grounded in dependency, seeking harmony not greatness. Its highest value is peace, not transcendence. This makes it unable to withstand rejection or opposition.

**Position PP-111: Liberalism and Libertarianism as Privative Doctrines**
- Both liberalism and libertarianism are privative - define by what they are NOT. Mistake absence of violence for presence of virtue. Both hollow twins that clear path for those who want something.

**Position PP-112: Libertarianism's False Affirmation: Darwinism in Place of Telos**
- Libertarianism smuggles in affirmative telos while claiming to have none - believes removing state unleashes Darwinian arena producing greatness. Markets are moral battlegrounds that will refine humanity.

**Position PP-113: Libertarianism as Trojan Horse for Capital**
- Libertarianism bankrolled by big capital to moralize dismantling of oversight. Real beneficiaries not individual entrepreneurs but multinationals, megabanks, billionaire investors. Foot soldiers sold fantasy.

**Position PP-114: Trickle-Down Darwinism: Selling Gods to Fools**
- Trickle-down economics is theological promise for libertarians: let market reign and you shall ascend. But wealth doesn't trickle, it coagulates. Libertarian foot soldiers serve Mammon thinking they'll become gods.

**Position PP-115: Soviet Union Gave American Proceduralism Undeserved Legitimacy**
- American proceduralism looked like moral clarity only because framed against Soviet totalitarianism. Once USSR fell, Americans saw system in isolation - procedure without purpose - and patriotism declined.

**Position PP-116: When Procedures Replace Purpose: Iron Cage Analysis**
- Proceduralism's promise of neutrality masks paradox: by refusing to endorse substantive virtues, implicitly elevates market logic as default metric of worth. Creates culture of castrated thinking.

**Position PP-117: Rawls vs. Stalin: Veil of Ignorance Assumes Moral Sameness**
- Rawls's veil of ignorance only works if everyone behind veil is basically like Rawls - liberal, mild, procedurally minded, risk-averse. Moment you introduce adversarial moral asymmetry (Stalin), framework collapses.

**Position PP-118: Rawlsian Proceduralism Leads to 'No Right to Exist' Position**
- Logical extreme of consent-based Rawlsian ethics: people don't have right to exist because they didn't consent to existence. Under fully proceduralist morality, even existence ethically suspect.

**PSYCHOLOGY (4 positions): PS-031 to PS-034**

**Position PS-031: Mafiosos and Cops Gain Cognitive Edge from Clarity About Human Nature**
- Mafiosos and cops exhibit sharpness within their domains because they have clarity about human nature. Cannot afford to assume best in people - survival depends on assuming base motives.

**Position PS-032: Why Dictators Wear Tunics**
- Dictators wear tunics because tunic is visual embodiment of psychological regime - declares control, not seduction. Anti-relational sexuality of domination without seduction.

**Position PS-033: 'Gifted Child' as Mother's Proxy Narcissism**
- 'Gifted child' label is mother's proxy narcissism filling void in her life. Child becomes identity, status marker, proof that she matters. Often occurs in father's absence.

**Position PS-034: New Meaning of 'Developer' - From Implementer to Idea Person**
- Word 'developer' shifting meaning - from person who writes code to bring someone else's idea to life, to idea person who can build it themselves using no-code/AI tools.

WORK-040: BLOG ESSAYS COLLECTION - SET 2 - 57 POSITIONS
====================================================================================================

**AESTHETICS (9 positions): AE-028 to AE-036**

**Position AE-028: Star Wars as Jungian Dreamscape**
- Star Wars (1977) is not space opera but Jungian dreamscape - every frame steeped in archetype, guided by mythic structure, powered by psychological machinery Jung mapped. About soul, not space.

**Position AE-029: Star Trek's Psychological Symmetry as Source of Durability**
- Star Trek's brilliance isn't stories but psychological symmetry: id pushes for passion, superego demands restraint, ego must choose/balance/synthesize/act. Each episode is microcosm of self in conflict.

**Position AE-030: Satire Fails Without Systems Understanding**
- Literary satire falls apart if you don't understand the system you're mocking. Writers like Lewis portray middle-class work as absurd without understanding capital flows, risk underwriting, legal frameworks, infrastructure coordination.

**Position AE-031: The Babbitt Problem: Mocking Components as Clowns**
- Babbitt may be windbag but he occupies place in real machinery of civilization - helps allocate space, facilitates growth, is node in economic network. Lewis doesn't see this because he never bothers. To him Babbitt is type not participant, clown not component.

**Position AE-032: The Frank Burns Problem: Mocking the Machinery That Makes Everything Possible**
- Hawkeye mocks Frank Burns, but Burns follows procedure and keeps system running. Hawkeye mocks the machinery, but it's the machinery that makes surgery possible. Satire without respect equals superficiality.

**Position AE-033: Snobbery as Epistemological Vice**
- Snobbery is not just social vice but epistemological one - a kind of built-in blindness. Lewis's portrayal of Babbitt suffers from defensiveness dressed up as superiority, presumption of guilt that ruins ability to see clearly.

**Position AE-034: The Anthropologist Analogy for Bad Satire**
- Imagine anthropologist who despises tribe he's meant to observe - thinks rituals stupid, beliefs primitive. Maybe feels threatened by their strength, cohesion, joy, so adopts supercilious posture. How much will he learn? Nothing. His fieldwork is already over.

**Position AE-035: Bach's Music as Engineering Not Just Expression**
- Bach's music isn't just expressive but engineered - in same sense as suspension bridge or cathedral. His fugues and chorales are systems: harmonic architectures, counterpunctual machines, vaults of sound built with structural intelligence and terrifying precision. This IS German engineering in musical form.

**Position AE-036: Music as Intelligible Emotion - Soul Through System**
- Music at its best is intelligible emotion - emotion made knowable through form. What happens when human feeling is passed through filter of logic, structure, constraint and transformed into something enduring. Emotion is energy, structure is geometry, music is fusion.

**EPISTEMOLOGY (9 positions): EP-151 to EP-159**

**Position EP-151: EMH 'Priced In' as Unfalsifiable Tautology**
- EMH's concept of 'priced in' is logically circular: if price moves, information was priced in; if price doesn't move, information was already priced in. This makes EMH immune to contradiction but also immune to usefulness.

**Position EP-152: EMH Collapses Signal-Noise Distinction**
- Under semi-strong and strong EMH, 'information' includes sentiment, rumors, trends, tweets, collective mood - leading to inversion where 'whatever drives prices is, by definition, information', collapsing distinction between signal and noise.

**Position EP-153: EMH as Theology of Price Not Theory of Value**
- EMH is theology of price - inviting trust in markets because everything is priced in. It confuses knowledge with movement, rationality with reaction, truth with trend, turning 'pricing in' from useful heuristic into circular article of faith.

**Position EP-154: Reverse Brain Engineering as New Epistemic Modality**
- Building AI systems that approximate human cognition is not merely technical feat but fundamentally new way of knowing - a reflexive, co-constructive epistemic loop between creator and creation that transcends deduction, induction, and abduction.

**Position EP-155: AI as Epistemic Partner Not Amplifier**
- Unlike telescope or particle accelerator (epistemic amplifiers that strengthen senses), AI systems theorize back. They embody theories in dynamic unfolding way, forcing us to confront limitations of our own cognition, intuitions, philosophical assumptions.

**Position EP-156: Recursive Co-Modeling as New Form of Knowledge Generation**
- Reverse brain engineering is recursive co-modeling - dialogical process where line between subject and object, knower and known, begins to blur. When we build artificial minds that help us understand our own, we create mirrors that talk back.

**Position EP-157: AI Development as Epistemological Turning Point**
- Just as writing changed not just what we knew but how we knew, construction of artificial minds marks turning point in epistemology. We're no longer simply thinking about mind - we're thinking with it in new synthetic form.

**Position EP-158: When Model Becomes Reality: Metaphysical Violence**
- When economists attempt to predict or restructure alien economies using only their own conceptual vocabulary, they aren't doing science - they're doing metaphysical violence. Converting world into format their models can digest, discarding everything else as noise.

**Position EP-159: Humility vs Equations in Understanding Alien Systems**
- If you want to understand a society, must allow it to remain strange - see its economy as living form of life not market-in-waiting. Takes humility, not equations. Without humility, economic theory isn't tool but colonizer with calculator.

**HISTORY AND CIVILIZATION (2 positions): HI-018 to HI-019**

**Position HI-018: Structural Music Emerges Only in Civilizations with Engineering/Logic**
- We don't get music of enduring formal complexity in cultures lacking corollary in engineering, architecture, mathematics, or theology-as-logic. Wherever civilization has deep commitment to structure, it gives rise to music reflecting that commitment.

**Position HI-019: Music as Civilizational Diagnostic**
- If you want to know where a civilization stands, don't look at its politics - look at its music. Music reveals whether civilization has structure, logic, theology, engineering, or has collapsed into formless expression.

**PHILOSOPHY OF MIND (9 positions): PM-065 to PM-073**

**Position PM-065: Minds as High-Order Counter-Entropic Systems**
- Minds are not metaphysical mysteries but thermodynamic marvels - the most structured counter-entropic systems known, capable of storing information, making predictions, and engineering further counter-entropy.

**Position PM-066: AI as Engineered Counter-Entropic System**
- AI represents a third kind of discipline - one that builds counter-entropy. Neural networks and large language models are designed to self-organize, self-correct, and self-model, creating artificial systems that push back against entropy in novel, non-biological ways.

**Position PM-067: Hero's Journey as Individuation Map**
- Jung's individuation (integration of all aspects of self: conscious, unconscious, shadow, anima/animus) is what hero's journey really maps - not story template but internal transformation.

**Position PM-068: Darth Vader as The Shadow**
- In Jungian terms, Vader represents the Shadow - the denied, repressed, projected part of self that is powerful, dangerous, and essential. He is the unclaimed part of Luke - what Luke could become if he gives in to power without balance.

**Position PM-069: The Force as Collective Unconscious**
- The Force is Jungian metaphor: impersonal, morally ambiguous, accessible through intuition, binding everything transcending language. It's deep substrate of shared symbolic life, not God or science.

**Position PM-070: Star Trek as Freudian Psychic Diagram**
- Star Trek: TOS wasn't just sci-fi but psychological diagram - Kirk/Spock/McCoy map exactly onto Freud's ego/superego/id and his three libidinal character types (narcissist/obsessional/libidinal).

**Position PM-071: Kirk as Ego - Mediator Between Impulse and Restraint**
- Kirk embodies Freudian ego and narcissist type: brash, confident, improvisational, making decisions and taking responsibility. He navigates between Spock's logic and McCoy's sentiment, integrating and synthesizing to act.

**Position PM-072: Spock as Superego - Harshest Internal Judge**
- Spock is superego embodied: reason, logic, restraint through repression of human half. He's obsessional character - intellectual, self-disciplined, defending against emotion. Embodies Freud's observation that superego is harshest judge of self.

**Position PM-073: McCoy as Id - Voice of Passion and Body**
- McCoy is not primitive brute but voice of passion, outrage, care, body - the libidinal type and structural id. He expresses energy, anger, yearning that others (especially Spock) suppress.

**POLITICAL PHILOSOPHY (7 positions): PP-119 to PP-125**

**Position PP-119: Cultural Hollowness Laments as Status Anxiety**
- When writers lament 'the hollowness of our times' (Eliot, Sartre, Camus, anti-capitalist intellectuals), they're not describing historical condition but their own status anxiety - they feel displaced by mass culture, new money, technology, change.

**Position PP-120: Snobbery as Performance of Half-Safe Position**
- Snobbery is something junior people do to impress senior people - 'please like me' disguised as 'I am above you.' It's the culture of the half-safe. When you're actually fighting for your life, you have no bandwidth for class-posturing.

**Position PP-121: Status Anxiety Disguised as Historical Diagnosis**
- Hollowness these writers see in world is really just echo of their own fading status. Their 'diagnosis' is job interview disguised as cultural criticism.

**Position PP-122: Freud's Misreading of American Vitality as Spiritual Hollowness**
- Freud treated American vitality (efficiency, productivity, optimism) as mask for decay rather than different mode of health. He had no serious understanding of how economies work and couldn't see that 'hollowness' was actually mass coordination, energy management, risk absorption at unprecedented scale.

**Position PP-123: American Aspiration vs European Repression as Different Health Modes**
- Freud believed psychic health came from facing darkness. America was full of people building rather than brooding. For Freud this looked like evasion. But maybe it was civilization powered not by repression but by aspiration.

**Position PP-124: Appeals Process as Ritual Audit Not Truth-Seeking**
- Appeals courts don't ask 'Was justice done?' but 'Were the rules followed?' They evaluate procedural/legal errors, not actual innocence. Legal system views trial as ritual and appellate process as ritual audit - concern is whether form was maintained, not whether defendant is innocent or guilty.

**Position PP-125: Scalia and Rawlsian Proceduralism: Fairness in Structure is Enough**
- Legal system embodies belief that fairness in structure is enough - if the system was followed, justice has been done. This is not only wrong in theory but devastating in practice, allowing innocent to be imprisoned while courts say 'paperwork was in order.'

**PSYCHOLOGY AND SCIENCE (21 positions): PS-035 to PS-055**

**Position PS-035: Fundamental Division in Science: Entropic vs Counter-Entropic Systems**
- The fundamental division in science is not between mental and physical, but between entropic systems (that degrade toward disorder) and counter-entropic systems (that build and maintain structure).

**Position PS-036: Economics Misplaced as Entropic Science**
- Economics deals with expectations, preferences, beliefs, and strategy (counter-entropic systems) but attempts to align itself with physics, producing models that are impressive in form but brittle in content because they model minds, not falling bodies.

**Position PS-037: 𝜉 (Xi) Metric: Price-Fundamental Correlation in Equities**
- Introduced proprietary metric 𝜉 (xi) measuring statistical degree to which changes in price correlate with changes in company fundamentals. For large-cap equities, 𝜉 is effectively zero - prices move independently of economic reality.

**Position PS-038: Large-Cap Price Decoupling from Fundamentals**
- Large-cap stock prices can rise or fall independently of any measurable change in core economic reality. Fundamental information becomes lagging background noise in markets dominated by order book dynamics, momentum patterns, and algorithmic traders.

**Position PS-039: Why Small and Mid-Cap Show Higher 𝜉**
- Smaller firms exhibit modestly higher 𝜉 because: (1) reduced algorithmic saturation, (2) greater transparency of fundamentals, (3) lower narrative interference, (4) analyst neglect paradox allows real performance to move price.

**Position PS-040: Markets Price Second-Order Beliefs Not Value**
- When 𝜉 is low, price reflects second-order beliefs (beliefs about what others believe) rather than about what is true. This reflexivity feeds a feedback loop in which narrative and structure supplant content.

**Position PS-041: Stocks as Claims on Imagined Futures Not Intrinsic Utility**
- Unlike commodities with intrinsic utility (wheat, copper), stocks are claims on imagined futures with no intrinsic use, only expectations. Their price depends on mood, narrative, and belief - making them more like luxury goods than commodities.

**Position PS-042: OCD as Adaptive Machinery in Overdrive**
- OCD is not just pathology but adaptive machinery pushed into overdrive. Built from traits that in right amounts helped ancestors survive: error detection, threat anticipation, long-range consequence modeling, rule-following, mental rehearsal, moral self-monitoring.

**Position PS-043: OCD Prototype in Prehistoric Context**
- 50,000 years ago in tight-knit band, someone who double-checked perimeter, insisted on ritual cleanliness, mentally simulated threats repeatedly, felt guilty after minor transgressions might have been liability in some ways but godsend in others - especially if compulsions aligned with group needs.

**Position PS-044: OCD as Misapplied Boundary-Maintenance System**
- In modern abstract, crowded, digital world, machinery that maintained physical/moral boundaries has no natural object. So turns inward, fixates on trivialities, creates imagined scenarios to defuse through ritual. System isn't broken - it's misapplied, doing its job too well in wrong context.

**Position PS-045: OCD as Sacred Function Misfiring**
- You don't get OCD from nowhere - you get it from same architecture that in another life might have made you priest, scout, healer, watchman. Pain is real but mind isn't broken - it's just tuned for world that no longer exists.

**Position PS-046: Economics Not Self-Contained Predictive System**
- Economics is not self-contained system that can predict itself. It's downstream of culture, politics, religion, personality, invention. Charismatic leader can redirect nation's economy in week. War, famine, singularity make mockery of best economic models. These events aren't noise - they're constitutive.

**Position PS-047: Economics vs Biology: Probabilistic vs Non-Self-Predictive**
- Biology is probabilistic but not arbitrary - state variables constrain future through non-random mechanisms. Economics not even robustly probabilistic. System never was self-predictive to begin with. Not that it's sound but occasionally disrupted - it's that it was never self-predictive.

**Position PS-048: Inca Example: Economics Records But Doesn't Explain Non-Economic Systems**
- To predict Inca behavior in 1457, look at 1456 rituals, laws, cosmic beliefs, cosmological metaphors - not marginal utility curves. Economics may record food stores and track trade but won't tell why workers redeployed to sacred site, surplus burned instead of stored, labor restructured to appease eclipse.

**Position PS-049: Serial Killerdom as Specific Cognitive-Behavioral Protocol**
- Serial murder is not random violence but premeditated, patterned, highly stylized behavior with limited recurring types (organized/disorganized, visionary/hedonistic, power/mission-oriented). This taxonomic stability suggests it's specific cognitive-behavioral protocol, not generic trauma response.

**Position PS-050: Serial Killerdom Not Modern Invention But Modern Category**
- Serial murder has long existed (Gilles de Rais, Elizabeth Báthory, slaughtering priests of empires). What's new isn't behavior but recognition as distinct category - product of modern bureaucratic state with tools to track, name, mythologize recurring patterns.

**Position PS-051: Trauma as Trigger Not Cause of Serial Killing**
- Many serial killers had disturbing upbringings but 'trauma = serial killer' doesn't track. Most abuse victims don't become serial murderers. Some notorious killers didn't experience abuse exceeding ordinary dysfunction. Trauma is trigger sparking very particular pre-existing architecture.

**Position PS-052: Serial Killerdom as Evolutionary Spandrel or Vestigial Adaptation**
- If behavior is specific, structured, eerily reproducible, must ask where it came from. Evolution repurposes, mutates, experiments with hyper-specialists. Serial killerdom perhaps: spandrel (byproduct of adaptive features), vestigial adaptation, or extreme failure mode of modules serving critical social functions.

**Position PS-053: Serial Killers as Overclocked Predator Mode**
- What sets serial killers apart isn't violence but method: they stalk, hunt, blend in, mimic normal social behavior with chilling precision. Not moral deformity but overactivation of predator mode made grotesque by misfiring reward circuits and unregulated internal narratives.

**Position PS-054: Economic Theory as Intellectual Colonization**
- When Western-trained economist attempts to manage non-Western economy, doesn't observe or listen but immediately translates: 'What's your interest rate? Marginal productivity? Utility function?' None make sense in native conceptual world, but economist is there to re-code not learn.

**Position PS-055: Flattening Sacred into Economic Data**
- Incan administrator describes labor system organized around sacred seasons, familial debt, reciprocal land stewardship. Economist replies: 'Ah yes, non-monetary kinship-based tax structure with redistributive efficiency function.' But that's not what it is - that's just bad translation. The ritual is no longer ritual, sacred no longer sacred.

KUCZYNSKI PHILOSOPHICAL DATABASE v27 - COMPLETE
Total Works: 37 | Total Positions: 836
====================================================================================================

1. [ACT-007] Psychopathy as Incapacity for Non-Pragmatic Agency
   Sources: Chapter Psychopathy characteristics
   Thesis: Psychopaths use others but do not have relationships with them except of a purely pragmatic kind. To the extent a person is a psychopath, he cannot have meaningful relations with others. Psychopathic agency is purely instrumental, treating others as tools rather than as ends in themselves or as genuine relational partners.

2. [ACTION-001] Intentions as System-Level Judgments
   Sources: WORK-005 (Essay 1)
   Thesis: Intentions = judgments about how to consolidate psychological architecture. NOT desires.

3. [ACTION-002] Values Distinct from Desires
   Sources: WORK-005 (Essay 1)
   Thesis: Values = beliefs about what consolidates psychological architecture. Values ≠ desires (though can interact).

4. [ACTION-003] Free Acts as Value-Driven
   Sources: WORK-005 (Essay 1)
   Thesis: Free acts driven by values, NOT by second-order desires (contra Frankfurt). Second-order desires can be warped.

5. [ACTION-004] Rational vs. Intelligent Distinction
   Sources: WORK-005 (Essay 1)
   Thesis: Rational = embodies due regard for interests. Intelligent = computational power. Irrational acts can be highly intelligent.

6. [ACTION-005] Frankfurt's Analysis Insufficient
   Sources: WORK-005 (Essay 1)
   Thesis: Frankfurt right about higher-order states but wrong that second-order desires sufficient. Rationalization problem.

7. [ACTION-006] Compatibilism About Free Will
   Sources: WORK-001 (Chapter 15)
   Thesis: Free will is compatible with determinism. One acts freely when actions result from one's own desires and deliberations.

8. [ACTION-007] Action requires unconscious intention, not conscious decision
   Sources: WORK-027 (lines 230-280, 1720-1770)
   Thesis: Voluntary action requires an unconscious intention (which may or may not reach consciousness) rather than a conscious decision. The readiness potential represents this unconscious intention forming. Conscious awareness (W) is epiphenomenal regarding the particular action, though it may affect future actions through approval/veto.

9. [ACTION-008] Action requires self-change
   Sources: WORK-034
   Thesis: To act is to change oneself. A being that cannot change itself cannot act.

10. [ACTION-009] Power presupposes freedom
   Sources: WORK-035
   Thesis: There is a distinction between freedom and power. Power is the ability to convert freedom into desired results. Power presupposes the existence of freedom and must be distinguished from it. A rock has power (effects) but not freedom or the ability to do things in the relevant sense.

11. [ACTION-010] Intentions vs desires in action explanation
   Sources: WORK-036
   Thesis: There is a crucial distinction between desires and intentions in explaining action. Intentions are grounded in one's personality; desires need not be. There are free-floating desires that are 'in one, but not of one.' Counterfeit intentions exist where conscious intention differs from unconscious intention.

12. [ACTION-011] Compulsive actions achieve opposite of conscious intention
   Sources: WORK-036
   Thesis: The end-result of a compulsively performed action is the opposite of the consciously intended result and coincides with the unconsciously intended result. Compulsive acts of kindness toward mother don't affect her like real kindness but like acts of hostility. Taking mother to endless doctors demoralizes her and weakens her immune system.

13. [ACTION-012] Authentic action requires alignment of values and desires
   Sources: WORK-036
   Thesis: Authentic actions must embody both values and desires in alignment. Actions driven by desire without values are instinctual reactions (real but not actions). Actions driven by values without desire are sublimations (actions but not real). Compulsive acts split into two half-actions - one all instinct, one all values - and thus aren't really anything.

14. [ACTION-013] Compulsive behavior as leaking not acting
   Sources: WORK-036
   Thesis: In compulsive acts, the actor isn't truly acting - rather, sadism or hatred is 'leaking out' of them. Although compulsive acts discharge negative emotions, it isn't the person doing the discharging. The beneficent side is intentional but lacks emotional support, making it behavior one 'undergoes' rather than 'engages in.'

15. [ACTION-014] Deracinated values possess the agent
   Sources: WORK-036
   Thesis: When values are deracinated (lacking instinctual basis), it is less appropriate to describe them as values that the agent has than as values that have the agent. The agent is possessed by external value structures rather than authentically holding values integrated with their desires.

16. [ACTION-015] True agency requires ideals not just passion
   Sources: WORK-036
   Thesis: True agency is about fulfillment of ideals (not necessarily ethical, but ideals of some kind), not mere desire satisfaction. Where there is desire without values, there is passion (in both contemporary and etymological senses) but not action. An instinctual reaction driven purely by desire is not authentic action.

17. [AI-001] AI Systems as Philosophical Evidence
   Sources: Throughout work
   Thesis: Operation of AI systems provides empirical evidence that can arbitrate between competing philosophical theories. How AI actually works reveals truths about reasoning, knowledge, language, mind.

18. [AI-002] Classical vs. AI Computing Architecture Alignment
   Sources: Essay 1
   Thesis: Classical logic's properties (explicit rules, step-by-step deduction, binary truth values, context-independence, compositional semantics) match classical computing architecture. System L's properties (flexible search, pattern-based reasoning, degrees of plausibility, context-sensitivity, holistic processing) align with AI systems.

19. [AI-003] AI Vindicates Non-Revisionist Epistemology
   Sources: Essay 5
   Thesis: AI operation provides empirical support for non-revisionist epistemology that accepts knowledge about unobservables/future/counterfactuals, recognizes necessary integration of empirical and rational components, understands theoretical knowledge as based on causal mechanisms and continuity, rejects pure empiricism while maintaining importance of empirical evidence.

20. [AI-004] AI Provides Empirical Test for Logical Theories
   Sources: WORK-011 (Essay 1: AI Logic vs Classical Logic)
   Thesis: Artificial intelligence systems, particularly large language models, provide empirical evidence about how reasoning actually works, revealing that System L's approach better captures both human and artificial reasoning than classical logic.

21. [ECON-001] Financial Stability Requires Counter-Cyclical Policy
   Sources: Analysis of Fed response to 1929 crash vs. 2008 crisis
   Thesis: Markets left to themselves exhibit boom-bust cycles. Preventing severe busts requires counter-cyclical intervention: tightening during booms, loosening during busts. The Fed's pro-cyclical tightening after 1929 crash turned it into Depression.

22. [ECON-002] Credit as Essential Economic Function
   Sources: Analysis of how 2008 banking crisis decapitalized banks and restricted credit
   Thesis: Economies depend on credit as much as on wealth. When credit dries up, economic activity contracts even if wealth remains. Banking crises are particularly dangerous because they destroy credit availability.

23. [ECON-003] Exchange Value is Perception-Based, Use Value is Reality-Based
   Sources: Chapter Harvey on Commodity Fetishism
   Thesis: Exchange value is fundamentally perception-based rather than reality-based, while use value is reality-based. For this reason, there is no limit to how much exchange value and use value can diverge from one another.

24. [ECON-004] Wealth Divergence Between Exchange and Use Value Exacerbates Inequality
   Sources: Chapter Harvey on Commodity Fetishism
   Thesis: The divergence between exchange value and use value tends to inflate the value of wealthy people's assets and deflate the value of poor people's assets, thereby exacerbating pre-existing inequalities.

25. [ECON-005] 2008 Crisis Exemplifies Dual Divergence of Exchange from Use Value
   Sources: Chapter Harvey on Commodity Fetishism
   Thesis: The 2008 financial crisis was caused by two distinct divergences between exchange value and use value: first, worthless housing was made to seem valuable; second, worthless housing-backed securities created additional false perception-based capital.

26. [ECON-006] Anti-Drug Laws Create Zero-Sum Bureaucracies That Are Net Economic Parasites
   Sources: Chapter Some Reflections on the Virtues of the Free Market
   Thesis: The state apparatus relating to drug prohibition - educators, probation officers, prison personnel - are zero-sum bureaucracies: useless parasites contributing nothing while being paid at taxpayer expense, actually harming those they supposedly help.

27. [ECON-007] Drug Prohibition is Economic Argument for Universal Drug Legalization
   Sources: Chapter An Economic Argument for Drug-legalization
   Thesis: For strictly economic reasons (not civil liberty reasons), it is necessary to make all drugs legal unconditionally. 90% of inmates are drug offenders; imprisoning them is expensive and prevents economic contribution; drug offenders are non-violent and don't abridge others' freedoms.

28. [ECON-008] Knowledge-Capital More Important Than Property-Capital in Market Economies
   Sources: Chapter Knowledge-capital
   Thesis: In today's market economy, knowledge is more important than property. Person with unlimited knowledge but no property can acquire unlimited property. Person with property but no knowledge can only hold position, not grow it. Knowledge alone enables satisfying market demands.

29. [ECON-009] Market Economies Incentivize Education, Command Economies Do Not
   Sources: Chapter Knowledge-capital
   Thesis: In feudal or command economies, property seldom passes between persons - such economies are static. Participants focus on property retention not acquisition, so investing in education doesn't pay since no guarantee of marketing it. In market economies there is such guarantee since one can always trade knowledge for property.

30. [ECON-010] Market Freedom Paradox: Freedom Used Rationally Produces Slavery
   Sources: Chapter Legal vs. Substantive Freedom and the Paradox of the Free Market
   Thesis: There is a paradox of market freedom: legal freedoms, when disposed of in most rational manner given available options, produce complete enslavement. Rationality and freedom turn against themselves to enslave their possessor.

31. [ECON-011] Fund Managers Profit by Exploiting Exchange-Use Value Divergences
   Sources: Chapter Harvey on Commodity Fetishism
   Thesis: Fund managers make money by dumping over-valued assets and buying under-valued assets. Their income depends entirely on detecting discrepancies between use-value and exchange-value. Their activities may themselves enlarge those discrepancies.

32. [ECON-012] Dodd-Frank's real problem is insufficient scope
   Sources: WORK-029 (lines 108)
   Thesis: Criticisms of Dodd-Frank (reduced liquidity, expensive infrastructure, hurts small banks, government overreach) are either false or outweighed by countercriticisms. The real problem with Dodd-Frank is that it doesn't go far enough. It prevents certain predatory behaviors but does nothing to limit bank size, and therefore does nothing to prevent the systemic damage megabanks can cause.

33. [ECON-013] Low interest rates and excessive government debt create policy trap
   Sources: WORK-029 (lines 127-138)
   Thesis: Thirty years of low interest rates (1990-2022) led to both inflation and massive government debt (140% debt-to-GDP). This creates a trap: raising rates to curb inflation makes servicing government debt prohibitively expensive, potentially forcing default; but lowering rates causes inflation to rise to unacceptable levels.

34. [ECON-014] Megabanks cause market concentration and poor service
   Sources: WORK-029 (lines 70-90)
   Thesis: The top 11 financial firms manage $46 trillion in a $125 trillion economy—massive market concentration. Moreover, megabanks provide worse service than smaller banks: fewer branches per capita, worse customer service, more fees. Their advantage is political, not economic: 'too big to fail' means they can take excessive risks knowing they'll be bailed out.

35. [ECON-015] FIRE economy shifts from production to speculation
   Sources: WORK-029 (lines 145-160)
   Thesis: The growth of the FIRE sector (Finance, Insurance, Real Estate) from 14% to 21% of GDP represents a shift from productive economic activity to rent-seeking, speculation, and wealth transfer. FIRE doesn't create wealth; it moves existing wealth around, extracting fees in the process. This represents a fundamental change in economic structure away from manufacturing and toward financialization.

36. [EP-001] Rationalist Foundationalism
   Sources: WORK-001 (Chapters 10-13), WORK-002 (Multiple exchanges), WORK-005 (Essays 2-3)
   Thesis: Knowledge rests on bedrock of non-empirical, purely logical truths

37. [EP-002] Anti-Empiricism
   Sources: WORK-001 (Chapter 13), WORK-002 (Multiple exchanges), WORK-005 (Essay 2)
   Thesis: Strict empiricism false; non-empirical knowledge required for all knowledge

38. [EP-003] Knowledge as Non-Accidentally Justified True Belief
   Sources: WORK-001 (Chapter 10), WORK-002 (VIPULMTR exchange)
   Thesis: Four conditions for knowledge: truth, belief, justification, non-accidental connection

39. [EP-004] Philosophy Justifies Empirical Science's Presuppositions
   Sources: WORK-005 (Essay 2)
   Thesis: Empirical disciplines make assumptions they cannot empirically justify. Only philosophy can provide non-empirical justification. Philosophy is meta-science.

40. [EP-005] Observation Cannot Self-Corroborate
   Sources: WORK-005 (Essay 2)
   Thesis: Observation cannot justify that observation is reliable. Witnesses cannot self-corroborate. Pure empiricism is circular.

41. [EP-006] Aboriginal Procedural Knowledge
   Sources: WORK-002 (ADI PERDANA exchange)
   Thesis: Humans have in-built procedural knowledge of dependence-relations

42. [EP-007] Continuity-Based External World Knowledge
   Sources: WORK-002 (TERIKA exchange)
   Thesis: We know external world by interpolating continuities between experiential data

43. [EP-008] Two Ways Sense-Perception Adds to Knowledge
   Sources: WORK-005 (Essay 2)
   Thesis: Perception contributes via (1) direct content transmission and (2) triggering ratiocinative processes beyond perceptual content

44. [EP-009] Principles Cannot Be Sense-Perceived
   Sources: WORK-005 (Essay 2)
   Thesis: Can perceive specific objects but cannot perceive principles or general truths. Principles grasped through reason.

45. [EP-010] Non-Empirical Knowledge Exists
   Sources: WORK-005 (Essay 2)
   Thesis: Some truths are known without empirical justification: mathematical, logical, some metaphysical

46. [EP-011] All Non-Empirical Knowledge is Analytic
   Sources: WORK-005 (Essay 2)
   Thesis: All non-empirical knowledge concerns conceptual structures. Explicitly rejects Kant's synthetic a priori.

47. [EP-012] A Priori Knowledge as Constitutive of Reasoning Ability
   Sources: WORK-005 (Essay 3)
   Thesis: A priori knowledge = knowledge constitutive of ability to reason. Not acquired through experience but enables learning from experience.

48. [EP-013] A Priori Knowledge Necessary for Any Learning
   Sources: WORK-005 (Essay 3)
   Thesis: Cannot learn from experience without a priori knowledge. Cannot deduce principles of deduction from experience (circular). Must have deductive knowledge ab initio.

49. [EP-014] A Priori Knowledge as Subpersonal
   Sources: WORK-005 (Essay 3)
   Thesis: A priori knowledge not ordinary propositional knowledge but constitutive of subject itself. Principles are ability to think, not objects of thought.

50. [EP-015] Refutation of Humean Skepticism
   Sources: WORK-001 (Chapter 12), WORK-002 (ADI PERDANA exchange)
   Thesis: Induction justified; Hume's argument commits gambler's fallacy

51. [EP-016] Gettier Problem: Justification Must Be Non-Accidental
   Sources: WORK-001 (Chapter 10)
   Thesis: Justified true belief is not sufficient for knowledge. The connection between justification and truth must be non-accidental.

52. [EP-017] Three Sources of Justification
   Sources: WORK-001 (Chapter 10)
   Thesis: There are ultimately only three sources of justification: (a) perceptual evidence, (b) introspective evidence, (c) rational inference.

53. [EP-018] Testimony Requires Independent Verification
   Sources: WORK-001 (Chapter 10)
   Thesis: For testimony-based belief to constitute knowledge, one must have independent evidence of the source's reliability.

54. [EP-019] Cartesian Skepticism Refuted
   Sources: WORK-001 (Chapter 11)
   Thesis: Global skepticism is self-refuting. The skeptical hypothesis cannot coherently be entertained.

55. [EP-020] Inductive Inference Cannot Be Justified A Posteriori
   Sources: WORK-001 (Chapter 12)
   Thesis: The principle of induction cannot be justified empirically without circularity.

56. [EP-021] Rationalist Solution to Induction
   Sources: WORK-001 (Chapter 12)
   Thesis: The principle of induction must be known a priori if it is to be justified at all.

57. [EP-022] Universals Cannot Be Sense-Perceived
   Sources: WORK-001 (Chapter 13)
   Thesis: Universals cannot be sense-perceived because they are non-spatiotemporal and perception requires causal interaction.

58. [EP-023] Thought Requires Universals
   Sources: WORK-001 (Chapter 13)
   Thesis: All thought, language, and explanation require universals. The idea of non-universal-involving thought is incoherent.

59. [EP-024] Empiricism Refuted by Need for Universals
   Sources: WORK-001 (Chapter 13)
   Thesis: Strict empiricism is false. Since universals are required for all thought and cannot be sense-perceived, not all knowledge is empirical.

60. [EP-025] Berkeley's 'To Be Is To Be Perceived' Refuted
   Sources: WORK-001 (Chapter 13)
   Thesis: Berkeley's idealism is false. Multiple arguments refute 'esse est percipi'.

61. [EP-026] Phenomenalism Refuted
   Sources: WORK-001 (Chapter 13)
   Thesis: Phenomenalism (reducing physical objects to perceptions) is false. Carnap's project failed.

62. [EP-027] Poverty of Stimulus Argument for A Priori Knowledge (Chomsky)
   Sources: WORK-006
   Thesis: Humans acquire linguistic competence from minimal data while non-linguistic entities cannot, proving humans possess innate, pre-experiential cognitive structure (a priori knowledge).

63. [EP-028] Innate Cognitive Structure Required for Language Learning
   Sources: WORK-006
   Thesis: Language acquisition requires pre-existing innate cognitive structure. This structure is cognitive, not merely physiological.

64. [EP-029] Language Learning as 'Triggering' Pre-Existing Structure
   Sources: WORK-006
   Thesis: Experience does not create linguistic knowledge de novo but 'triggers' or 'turns on' pre-existing cognitive structures. Learning is activation, not construction.

65. [EP-030] A Priori Knowledge as Cognitive Framework (Not Framework Content)
   Sources: WORK-006
   Thesis: A priori knowledge is not knowledge you have (content within framework) but knowledge you are (the framework itself). It is not the object of awareness but the subject that makes awareness possible.

66. [EP-031] Framework-Knowledge vs Content-Knowledge Distinction
   Sources: WORK-006
   Thesis: Fundamental distinction between (1) structure-internal knowledge (learned, content) and (2) structure-constitutive knowledge (a priori, framework). All learned knowledge presupposes the framework.

67. [EP-032] Deep Unconsciousness of Cognitive Framework
   Sources: WORK-006
   Thesis: Framework-constitutive structures are 'deeply unconscious' (Chomsky's term) - unlike Freudian unconscious. Cannot become conscious because consciousness presupposes them.

68. [EP-033] Causation as Continuity Not Regularity
   Sources: Solution to Riddle of Induction
   Thesis: For x to cause y is for y to be a continuation of x, not for x-like events to always precede y-like events. Knowledge of the future is based on continuities, not regularities.

69. [EP-034] Knowledge Without Known Justification
   Sources: Solution to Ratiocinator's Paradox
   Thesis: A belief must be justified to constitute knowledge, but it is not necessary that one know that justification. Knowledge starts with beliefs that are not themselves knowledge but are justified.

70. [EP-035] Knowledge-Seeking as Description Satisfaction
   Sources: Solution to Meno's Paradox
   Thesis: Seeking knowledge involves knowing of a description that it is uniquely instantiated but not knowing what that instance is. Finding knowledge involves learning of some object that it satisfies that description.

71. [EP-036] Learning Presupposes Constitutive Knowledge
   Sources: Solution to Learner's Paradox
   Thesis: The ability to learn presupposes knowledge of a kind, but such knowledge is constitutive of one's mind and therefore isn't acquired. All acquired knowledge is learned, but not all knowledge is acquired.

72. [EP-037] Experiential Learning Hierarchy
   Sources: Dialogue on learning effectiveness
   Thesis: Learning proceeds through stages of increasing retention and depth: 'I forget what I hear. I remember what I see. I learn what I do.' Active doing produces the deepest learning.

73. [EP-038] Wisdom from Bitter Experience
   Sources: Dialogue on source of wisdom
   Thesis: All wisdom is based on experience, specifically bitter experience. Wisdom involves turning darkness into light - extracting positive lessons from negative experiences.

74. [EP-039] Induction as Explanatory Not Enumerative
   Sources: Essay 2
   Thesis: Induction is inherently explanatory rather than purely enumerative. Successful inductive inference requires integrating statistical data with implicit theoretical frameworks concerning causation, continuity, and natural kinds. Pure enumerative induction is fundamentally inadequate.

75. [EP-040] Discovery Follows Logical Principles
   Sources: Essay 3
   Thesis: Scientific discovery follows identifiable logical principles that are truth-tracking rather than merely psychological. Discovery and justification are not categorically distinct but interrelated aspects of theoretical reasoning.

76. [EP-041] Reverse Brain Engineering as Philosophy of Science Method
   Sources: Essay 4
   Thesis: By building AI systems that successfully replicate scientific reasoning, we can reverse-engineer cognitive principles underlying scientific discovery, providing empirically-grounded philosophy of science.

77. [EP-042] AI Falsifies External World Skepticism
   Sources: Essay 5
   Thesis: AI systems' consistent success at tasks requiring external world knowledge (medical diagnosis, object tracking) demonstrates treating perceptions as causally connected to external reality leads to reliable knowledge. If external world skepticism were correct, such success would be miraculous.

78. [EP-043] Knowledge of Unobservables is Routine
   Sources: Essay 5
   Thesis: Knowledge of unobservables is not only possible but routine when proper theoretical frameworks are in place. AI systems successfully infer unobservable entities from observable patterns.

79. [EP-044] Future Knowledge Through Causal Understanding
   Sources: Essay 5
   Thesis: Knowledge of future is possible through understanding causal mechanisms and continuities. AI weather prediction demonstrates this through increasing accuracy.

80. [EP-045] Counterfactual Knowledge is Knowledge of Rule Systems
   Sources: Essay 5
   Thesis: Counterfactual knowledge is genuine knowledge of existing rule systems and their implications. AI systems like AlphaGo demonstrate this through successful counterfactual reasoning.

81. [EP-046] No Knowledge is Purely Observational
   Sources: Essay 5
   Thesis: All knowledge requires integration of empirical and conceptual/theoretical components. Pure observation without conceptual frameworks is insufficient for understanding.

82. [EP-047] Theoretical Understanding Requires Causation and Continuity
   Sources: Essay 5
   Thesis: Successful theoretical knowledge is based on understanding causal mechanisms and continuity. Statistical and theoretical components must be integrated—pure correlation is insufficient.

83. [EP-048] Gettier Problem Solution: Scalable Justification
   Sources: Essay 8
   Thesis: Knowledge requires more than justified true belief—it requires justification that serves as proper conduit between reality and belief. Gettier cases involve justification that isn't scalable: it may work in one case but fails systematically when applied broadly.

84. [EP-049] Coherentist Knowledge Architecture in AI
   Sources: Essay 8
   Thesis: Neural architecture of AI systems supports coherentist rather than foundationalist theory of knowledge. Both human and artificial knowledge are best understood as interconnected webs rather than hierarchical structures built on foundations.

85. [EP-050] AI Falsifies Enumerative Induction Model
   Sources: WORK-011 (Essay 2: How AI Falsifies Enumerative Induction)
   Thesis: AI systems demonstrate that successful induction does not proceed by enumerating instances and generalizing. Instead, AI uses pattern recognition, analogy, and constraint satisfaction that cannot be reduced to simple enumeration of cases.

86. [EP-051] Pattern Recognition as Alternative to Enumeration
   Sources: WORK-011 (Essay 2)
   Thesis: Successful inductive reasoning operates through pattern recognition mechanisms that identify structural similarities rather than counting instances. AI systems reveal this by succeeding at induction without explicit enumeration.

87. [EP-052] AI Resolves Rationalism vs Empiricism Debate
   Sources: WORK-011 (Essay 5: AI Resolves Epistemological Debates)
   Thesis: AI systems demonstrate that knowledge acquisition requires both innate structure (rationalist element) and learning from data (empiricist element). Neither pure rationalism nor pure empiricism can account for AI's success. The debate is resolved by recognizing both are necessary.

88. [EP-053] Innate Architecture is Necessary for Learning
   Sources: WORK-011 (Essay 5)
   Thesis: AI systems require substantial innate architectural constraints to learn successfully from data. This vindicates the rationalist insight that some knowledge structure must precede experience, while acknowledging the empiricist insight that specific content comes from experience.

89. [EP-054] Knowledge Acquisition is Neither Pure Discovery nor Pure Construction
   Sources: WORK-011 (Essay 5)
   Thesis: AI reveals that knowledge acquisition is neither pure discovery of pre-existing facts (naive realism) nor pure construction from experience (radical constructivism). It involves interaction between innate processing architecture and environmental structure.

90. [EP-055] AI Solves the Gettier Problem
   Sources: WORK-011 (Essay 11: AI and Gettier Problem)
   Thesis: AI learning systems demonstrate a solution to the Gettier problem by showing that genuine knowledge requires not just justified true belief but also that the justification tracks truth through a reliable causal-computational process. AI systems that learn reliably exemplify this tracking relationship.

91. [EP-056] Reliable Process Theory of Knowledge via AI
   Sources: WORK-011 (Essay 11)
   Thesis: AI systems reveal that knowledge requires beliefs formed through reliable processes that systematically track truth. This vindicates reliabilist theories of knowledge over traditional JTB (justified true belief) accounts.

92. [EP-057] Knowledge Systems Minimize Anomalies
   Sources: WORK-011 (Essay 19: Anomaly Minimization)
   Thesis: Both human knowledge and AI systems operate by minimizing anomalies - discrepancies between expectations and observations. This convergence reveals anomaly minimization as a fundamental principle of rational cognition.

93. [EP-058] AI Learning Mirrors Scientific Theory Revision
   Sources: WORK-011 (Essay 19)
   Thesis: The process by which AI systems update their models to accommodate new data mirrors the process of scientific theory revision in response to anomalies. This suggests a common underlying logic of belief revision.

94. [EP-059] Continuous Properties Are Cognitively Necessary
   Sources: WORK-011 (Essay 20: Binary Truth)
   Thesis: AI reveals that continuous (graded) properties are necessary for cognitive systems to handle uncertainty and partial information, but this doesn't entail that truth itself is non-binary. Epistemic gradations are compatible with metaphysical bivalence.

95. [EP-060] AI Vindicates Pragmatist Theory of Knowledge
   Sources: WORK-011 (Essay 21: Pragmatism and AI)
   Thesis: AI development vindicates pragmatism's core insight that knowledge acquisition is fundamentally interactive rather than passive. AI systems learn through active engagement with their environment, validating pragmatist emphasis on the practical, interactive nature of inquiry.

96. [EP-061] AI as New Epistemic Faculty
   Sources: WORK-011 (Essay 21)
   Thesis: Interaction with AI constitutes a genuinely new epistemic faculty - a fourth level of observation beyond passive observation, active interaction, and tool creation. AI enables rational interaction with our own capacity for rational interaction, generating unique knowledge.

97. [EP-062] Knowledge is Inherently Perspectival and Interactive
   Sources: WORK-011 (Essay 21)
   Thesis: AI reveals that all knowledge, even 'objective' knowledge, begins from perspectival, interaction-based data driven by practical interests. There is no view from nowhere - even AI's knowledge is grounded in its interactions with reality.

98. [EP-063] Tool-Creating Interaction Generates Irreducible Knowledge
   Sources: WORK-011 (Essay 21)
   Thesis: Creating tools (including AI) generates knowledge that cannot be obtained from merely using tools or observing passively. Each level of reflexive interaction (tool use, tool creation, AI development) reveals new knowledge irreducible to lower levels.

99. [EP-064] Two Kinds of Knowledge: Direct and Indirect
   Sources: WORK-014
   Thesis: There are exactly two kinds of knowledge: direct (non-inferential, primitive) knowledge and indirect (inferential) knowledge. All knowledge falls into one of these two categories.

100. [EP-065] All Theoretical Knowledge is Inferential
   Sources: WORK-014
   Thesis: All theoretical knowledge is inferential knowledge, though not all inferential knowledge is theoretical knowledge. Theoretical knowledge requires reasoning from observations to explanatory hypotheses.

101. [EP-066] Knowledge is Justified True Belief (But Not Vice Versa)
   Sources: WORK-014
   Thesis: All knowledge is justified true belief, but not all justified true belief is knowledge. Additional conditions beyond justification, truth, and belief are required for knowledge.

102. [EP-067] Two Kinds of Dependence Relations: Causal and Logical
   Sources: WORK-014
   Thesis: There are exactly two fundamental types of dependence relations: causal dependence relations and logical dependence relations. These are distinct and irreducible to each other.

103. [EP-068] Logical Dependence Relations Not Known Through Observation
   Sources: WORK-014
   Thesis: Relations of logical dependence are not known through observation. They are known a priori, through conceptual analysis or reasoning, not through empirical investigation.

104. [EP-069] Causal Relations Known Through Observation
   Sources: WORK-014
   Thesis: Causal relations are known through observation. Unlike logical relations, causal dependencies are empirical matters discoverable through perception and experience.

105. [EP-070] Analytic Knowledge is Always Knowledge of Dependence Relations
   Sources: WORK-014
   Thesis: Analytic knowledge is always and necessarily knowledge of dependence-relations. To know analytic truths is to know how concepts or propositions depend on each other.

106. [EP-071] Propositions Are the Objects of Belief
   Sources: WORK-014
   Thesis: Propositions, not objects or states of affairs, are the proper objects of belief. To believe is to take a proposition to be true.

107. [EP-072] Knowledge Distinct From Awareness
   Sources: WORK-014
   Thesis: Knowledge must be sharply distinguished from mere awareness. One can be aware of something without knowing anything about it, and one can know things without being directly aware of them.

108. [EP-073] The Concept of Evidence: Causal Relatedness
   Sources: WORK-014
   Thesis: One state of affairs e is evidence of another state of affairs e* if and only if e and e* are causally related such that knowledge of e's existence provides reason to believe in e*'s existence.

109. [EP-074] Information-Transmission as Structure-Preservation
   Sources: WORK-014
   Thesis: Information-transmission is structure-preservation. An information-bearing series is one in which earlier events transmit their structure to later events through causal processes that preserve structural relationships.

110. [EP-075] Information Distinct From Evidence
   Sources: WORK-014
   Thesis: All information is evidence, but not all evidence is information. Evidence requires only causal relatedness; information requires causal relatedness plus structure-preservation.

111. [EP-076] Information-Transmission as the Basis of Knowledge
   Sources: WORK-014
   Thesis: Knowledge is based on information-transmission. Our sense-perceptions are isomorphs of the objects they represent, inheriting structure from their causes. Beliefs are knowledge only to the extent they are linked by information-transmissive series to corresponding realities.

112. [EP-077] Knowledge Independent of Statistical Reliability
   Sources: WORK-014
   Thesis: The difference between knowledge and mere belief is not statistical. A belief is knowledge if and only if it is the end-result of an information-transmissive series, regardless of the general reliability of the mechanism that produced it.

113. [EP-080] Biological Impossibility of Extreme Relativist Beliefs
   Sources: Chapter Main text
   Thesis: It is biologically impossible to actually believe extreme relativist or deconstructionist positions. No one is drawn to such positions because they believe them; they perpetrate fraud for reasons of convenience, ego, and hate.

114. [EP-081] Parental Instincts as Embodied Knowledge
   Sources: Chapter Introduction
   Thesis: Knowledge of the importance of healthy early-life attachments for psychological health is embodied in parental instincts. Parents, especially mothers, are naturally inclined to bond with their children, particularly when they are young and vulnerable, indicating innate recognition of attachment's developmental significance.

115. [EP-082] Sellars' Myth of the Given
   Sources: Chapter Main argument
   Thesis: According to Sellars, what makes a given bit of phenomenal content have particular representational content is the addition of background knowledge and contextualizing information. To think that phenomenal content has intrinsic representational content is to commit 'the myth of the given' - a spurious epistemic foundationalism.

116. [EP-083] Sensations as Property-Indeterminate Without Background Knowledge
   Sources: Chapter Tie shop and goggles arguments
   Thesis: Visual sensations (and sensory qualia generally) are property-indeterminate by themselves. In non-standard perceptual conditions (e.g., unusual lighting in the tie shop, or wearing magnifying goggles), the same sensation could correspond to different objective properties. Background knowledge about conditions of perception is required to determine which property the sensation represents.

117. [EP-084] Two Versions of Anti-Foundationalism
   Sources: Chapter Theoretical summary
   Thesis: Sellars' attack on the myth of the given comes in two strengths. Weak version: it is not typically true that qualia by themselves constitute awareness (knowledge) of anything external - something extra is needed to make a quale epistemic. Strong version: it is not typically true that qualia by themselves constitute representations - something extra is needed to give them representational content. Both versions are correct.

118. [EP-085] Intentionalism Commits the Myth of the Given
   Sources: Chapter Conclusion
   Thesis: Intentionalism is a strong form of foundationalism guilty of the myth of the given in both its forms. Intentionalism holds that qualia by themselves have determinate representational content without needing background knowledge, and that background knowledge cannot affect their representational content. This makes qualia foundational, performing representational and epistemic roles in isolation from epistemic context - precisely the foundationalism Sellars refuted.

119. [EP-086] Learning Correspondence Rules for Non-Standard Perceptual Conditions
   Sources: Chapter Correspondence rule acquisition
   Thesis: When perceptual conditions are non-standard, subjects must learn correspondence rules mapping sensations-under-those-conditions to objective properties. This learning requires checking sensations against how things appear under standard conditions. Once internalized, these rules enable immediate perception of properties even under non-standard conditions.

120. [EP-087] Kant's Synthetic A Priori is Really Hard Analytic
   Sources: Chapter Part 1, Sections III-IX
   Thesis: Kant's 'synthetic a priori' truths (like 7+5=12 and 'a straight line is the shortest distance between two points') are not actually synthetic but rather 'hard analytic' - they are analytic truths that are difficult to recognize as such, requiring cognitive effort rather than immediate apprehension.

121. [EP-088] Easy Analytic Versus Hard Analytic Distinction
   Sources: Chapter Part 1, Section IX
   Thesis: Analytic truths divide into 'easy analytic' and 'hard analytic.' Easy analytic truths (e.g., 'circles are round,' 'triangles have three sides') are such that grasping them suffices for knowing their truth - denying them involves psychological as well as logical incoherence. Hard analytic truths (e.g., 'a circle is a class of points equidistant from a given point in a plane') involve only logical incoherence when denied; a sane person could believe their negation without psychic fragmentation.

122. [EP-089] A Priori as Epistemological, Not Logical Property
   Sources: Chapter Part 1, Section II
   Thesis: For Kant, a priority is a property of our knowledge of propositions, not of propositions themselves. A proposition is a priori not in virtue of intrinsic logical properties but in virtue of how one comes to know it. Consequently, a proposition could in principle be a priori for one creature and a posteriori for another.

123. [EP-090] Ex Nihilo Events are Logically Impossible
   Sources: Chapter Part 2, Section VI
   Thesis: There are no ex nihilo (uncaused) events. The spatio-temporal manifold would comprise ex nihilo events only if it comprised events not co-located with other events - only if it comprised events it didn't comprise. Propositions alleging uncaused events (e.g., 'the newspaper spontaneously combusted') are self-contradictory when properly understood.

124. [EP-091] Induction Justified by Analog Data, Not Digital Propositions
   Sources: Chapter Part 2, Sections VII-VIII
   Thesis: Induction is justified by continuous, analog sensory data rather than by discrete digital propositions. The logical basis for induction is precisely what is lost in digitization involved in embodying knowledge in propositions like 'every swan I've seen is white.' We subtly misrepresent our grounds for inductive belief when we try to propositionalize (digitize) them.

125. [EP-092] Propositions as Schematic Meta-Data, Not Data
   Sources: Chapter Part 2, Section VIII
   Thesis: Propositions like 'every swan I've ever seen is white' are not the data that motivate or legitimate inductive beliefs - they are meta-data. Describing such propositions as 'data' is like identifying a court's finding of guilty with actuality of guilt. We cannot work backwards from meta-data to data, just as we cannot recover subtle speech inflections from stenographer's transcript.

126. [EP-093] Digital-Analog Compatibility Distinction
   Sources: Chapter Part 2, Section IX
   Thesis: We must distinguish digital-compatibility from analog-compatibility - what is permissible given propositions from what is permissible given the analog data those propositions schematically represent. Propositions 'the rock will sprout wings' and 'no stone has ever sprouted wings' are digitally compatible, but their analog correlates involve discontinuities and perforations of space-time manifold making them analog-incompatible.

127. [EP-094] Goodman's Grue Problem Exposes Hume's Circularity
   Sources: Chapter Part 3, Section VIII
   Thesis: As Nelson Goodman showed, given any explanatorily useful property x, we can construct explanatorily useless property y (like 'grue' or 'plopper') such that x and y are indistinguishable from purely statistical viewpoint. This exposes circularity in Hume's reasoning: properties like 'copper' are not inductively innocent but already embody causal/inductive commitments.

128. [EP-095] Phenomenal States Require Theoretical Context (Sellars)
   Sources: Chapter Part 3, Section VIII
   Thesis: Following Sellars' Empiricism and the Philosophy of Mind: purely phenomenal states are representationally and epistemically empty except in context of knowledge concerning conditions under which they are experienced. Relevant contextual information can be given only in inductively and theoretically committed terms.

129. [EP-096] Religious sentiment cannot be understood in strictly medical terms; it cannot be deconstructed
   Sources: WORK-024 (Introduction - VRE contentions)
   Thesis: Religious sentiment cannot be understood in strictly medical terms; it cannot be deconstructed

130. [EP-097] Religious sentiment must be understood on its own terms
   Sources: WORK-024 (Introduction - VRE contentions)
   Thesis: Religious sentiment must be understood on its own terms

131. [EP-098] All empirical beliefs involve an element of faith - a 'will to believe'
   Sources: WORK-024 (Introduction - WTB discussion)
   Thesis: All empirical beliefs involve an element of faith - a 'will to believe'

132. [EP-099] Empirical beliefs are necessarily underdetermined by the data
   Sources: WORK-024 (Introduction - WTB discussion)
   Thesis: Empirical beliefs are necessarily underdetermined by the data

133. [EP-100] Empirical beliefs, when justified, are justified by their consequences
   Sources: WORK-024 (Introduction - WTB discussion)
   Thesis: Empirical beliefs, when justified, are justified by their consequences

134. [EP-101] Religious beliefs are justified by their consequences and are therefore justified in the same way as other empirical beliefs
   Sources: WORK-024 (Introduction - WTB discussion)
   Thesis: Religious beliefs are justified by their consequences and are therefore justified in the same way as other empirical beliefs

135. [EP-102] All hypotheses, including quintessentially scientific ones, involve an initial leap of faith; their legitimacy is established by their consequences
   Sources: WORK-024 (VRE Lecture I summary)
   Thesis: All hypotheses, including quintessentially scientific ones, involve an initial leap of faith; their legitimacy is established by their consequences

136. [EP-103] A belief is rational if it benefits the person who has it
   Sources: WORK-024 (VRE Lecture I summary)
   Thesis: A belief is rational if it benefits the person who has it

137. [EP-104] The rationality of belief is justified only by its consequences
   Sources: WORK-024 (VRE Lecture I summary)
   Thesis: The rationality of belief is justified only by its consequences

138. [EP-105] Religious belief involves a leap of faith, but this leap often proves worth making
   Sources: WORK-024 (VRE Lecture I summary)
   Thesis: Religious belief involves a leap of faith, but this leap often proves worth making

139. [EP-106] The trench-atheist is not really making a leap of faith because he is surrendering to a part of himself (his conscience), not to an external deity
   Sources: WORK-024 (Faith vs. Psychosis)
   Thesis: The trench-atheist is not really making a leap of faith because he is surrendering to a part of himself (his conscience), not to an external deity

140. [EP-107] The alcoholic is only making a 'leap of faith' relative to what his conscious mind knows, not what his mind as a whole knows; therefore he isn't really making a leap of faith
   Sources: WORK-024 (The Alcoholic's Leap of Faith)
   Thesis: The alcoholic is only making a 'leap of faith' relative to what his conscious mind knows, not what his mind as a whole knows; therefore he isn't really making a leap of faith

141. [EP-108] Only principled (not accidental) generalizations can be confirmed
   Sources: WORK-008 (Raven Paradox)
   Thesis: Only principled (not accidental) generalizations can be confirmed

142. [EP-109] When 'all x's are y's' is read as principled generalization, it has nomic/causal content and is not equivalent with 'all non-y's are non-x's'
   Sources: WORK-008 (Raven Paradox)
   Thesis: When 'all x's are y's' is read as principled generalization, it has nomic/causal content and is not equivalent with 'all non-y's are non-x's'

143. [EP-110] 'All ravens are black' (when principled) says that being a raven grounds or causes blackness
   Sources: WORK-008 (Raven Paradox)
   Thesis: 'All ravens are black' (when principled) says that being a raven grounds or causes blackness

144. [EP-111] Knowledge of the future is based on continuities, not regularities
   Sources: WORK-008 (Riddle of Induction)
   Thesis: Knowledge of the future is based on continuities, not regularities

145. [EP-112] Regularities often tell us where to look for continuities, but knowledge of regularities never constitutes knowledge of continuities
   Sources: WORK-008 (Riddle of Induction)
   Thesis: Regularities often tell us where to look for continuities, but knowledge of regularities never constitutes knowledge of continuities

146. [EP-113] Enumerative induction is either non-existent or illegitimate
   Sources: WORK-008 (Riddle of Induction)
   Thesis: Enumerative induction is either non-existent or illegitimate

147. [EP-114] When we make legitimate inferences about the future, it is on the basis of knowledge of continuities, not observation of repetitions
   Sources: WORK-008 (Riddle of Induction)
   Thesis: When we make legitimate inferences about the future, it is on the basis of knowledge of continuities, not observation of repetitions

148. [EP-115] We may have knowledge of continuities without knowledge of repetitions; we can know x caused y even with no other cases of x-like events followed by y-like events
   Sources: WORK-008 (Riddle of Induction)
   Thesis: We may have knowledge of continuities without knowledge of repetitions; we can know x caused y even with no other cases of x-like events followed by y-like events

149. [EP-116] One often knows x causes y without knowing exactly how y is continuous with x, by knowing secondary continuities that require positing a continuity
   Sources: WORK-008 (Riddle of Induction)
   Thesis: One often knows x causes y without knowing exactly how y is continuous with x, by knowing secondary continuities that require positing a continuity

150. [EP-117] Goodman's 'new riddle of induction' is a non-riddle, since it's continuities not concomitances that ground knowledge
   Sources: WORK-008 (New Riddle of Induction)
   Thesis: Goodman's 'new riddle of induction' is a non-riddle, since it's continuities not concomitances that ground knowledge

151. [EP-118] Although a belief must be justified to be knowledge, it isn't necessary that one know that justification
   Sources: WORK-008 (Ratiocinator's Paradox)
   Thesis: Although a belief must be justified to be knowledge, it isn't necessary that one know that justification

152. [EP-119] Knowledge starts with beliefs that are not knowledge; if such a belief is useful (consistent with data, justified), its owner likely retains it
   Sources: WORK-008 (Ratiocinator's Paradox)
   Thesis: Knowledge starts with beliefs that are not knowledge; if such a belief is useful (consistent with data, justified), its owner likely retains it

153. [EP-120] A belief can be justified without its owner knowing what that justification is; this blocks the epistemic regress
   Sources: WORK-008 (Ratiocinator's Paradox)
   Thesis: A belief can be justified without its owner knowing what that justification is; this blocks the epistemic regress

154. [EP-121] Looking for information involves knowing a description is uniquely instantiated but not knowing what instantiates it
   Sources: WORK-008 (Meno's Paradox)
   Thesis: Looking for information involves knowing a description is uniquely instantiated but not knowing what instantiates it

155. [EP-122] Finding information involves learning of some object that it satisfies a description one already knows to be instantiated
   Sources: WORK-008 (Meno's Paradox)
   Thesis: Finding information involves learning of some object that it satisfies a description one already knows to be instantiated

156. [EP-123] The ability to learn presupposes knowledge of a kind, but such knowledge is constitutive of one's mind and therefore isn't acquired
   Sources: WORK-008 (Learner's Paradox)
   Thesis: The ability to learn presupposes knowledge of a kind, but such knowledge is constitutive of one's mind and therefore isn't acquired

157. [EP-124] Introspection cannot settle causal questions
   Sources: WORK-027 (lines 1545-1570)
   Thesis: Introspection can reveal what mental states we're in but cannot reveal causal relations between mental states and behavior. Causal questions are empirical, requiring observation of patterns across cases, not introspective certainty. Therefore, introspection cannot establish that conscious will causes action.

158. [EP-125] Role of Intuition in Modal Knowledge
   Sources: WORK-031 (lines 2226-2233)
   Thesis: Modal intuitions (about what's possible/necessary) play a crucial but problematic role in modal epistemology and cannot be simply dismissed.

159. [EP-126] Arbitrariness as Theoretical Vice
   Sources: WORK-031 (lines Part V discussions, MODAL-014)
   Thesis: When theoretical claims depend on arbitrary choices (with no principled basis), this is a serious theoretical defect even if the theory is formally consistent.

160. [EP-127] Modal Knowledge via Structural Analysis
   Sources: WORK-031 (lines 2259-2290)
   Thesis: We know modal truths by examining the internal structure of propositions—how their constituent concepts are arranged and related—not by surveying alternative worlds.

161. [EP-128] Conceptual Understanding as Basic
   Sources: WORK-031 (lines 2259-2290, implicit throughout)
   Thesis: Some forms of understanding (like grasping concepts and their relations) are basic and cannot be further analyzed or reduced to other cognitive processes.

162. [EP-129] Meaning cannot be reduced to observable consequences
   Sources: WORK-032 (lines 61-86)
   Thesis: The pragmatist thesis (i) that 'the meaning of a hypothesis lies in its observable consequences' is false. The relationship between a hypothesis and its observable consequences is always contingent, never analytic, as it depends on what operative conditions and causal mechanisms obtain.

163. [EP-130] Truth is not identical with utility or power
   Sources: WORK-032 (lines 301-312)
   Thesis: The pragmatist thesis (ii) that 'a true idea is one that allows us to control the world' conflates truth with knowledge. What pragmatism incorrectly represents as a virtue of truth itself should be correctly understood as a virtue of our knowledge of truth. It isn't truth that is empowering: it is knowledge.

164. [EP-131] Truth is not identical with assimilability
   Sources: WORK-032 (lines 283-296)
   Thesis: The pragmatist thesis (iii) that 'true ideas are those we can assimilate, false ones are those we cannot' is false when taken literally. There are highly assimilable false ideas and highly non-assimilable true ones. Truth is not assimilability; rather, knowledge is assimilated truth.

165. [EP-132] Externalism threatens self-knowledge
   Sources: WORK-033 (lines Chapter 19)
   Thesis: If externalism is true—if mental content is individuated by external factors unknown to the subject—then subjects cannot have privileged access to their own thoughts. This conflicts with the apparent fact that we have immediate, authoritative knowledge of what we're thinking.

166. [EP-138] Counterfactuals as epistemic probability relations
   Sources: WORK-037
   Thesis: Counterfactuals are not statements about states of affairs in alternative worlds, but rather express relations of probabilification holding among statements. They register confirmation relations among propositions - the degree of credibility that certain propositions confer on other propositions.
