   Thesis: When choosing between theories, factors like ontological parsimony, intuitive plausibility, and coherence with science matter alongside formal adequacy.

411. [METH-045] All functions reduce to statement-functions
   Sources: WORK-033
   Thesis: While there are many types of functions (numerical, class-to-class, property-to-property), all functions are ultimately statement-functions, even though some appear not to be. This is a deep claim about the foundations of logic and mathematics.

412. [METH-046] Discipline-relative counterfactual evaluation
   Sources: WORK-037
   Thesis: What a biologist considers counterfactually possible differs from what a physicist considers counterfactually possible because they relativize statements to different data sets within their disciplinary scopes. This may reduce to differences in what propositions are known by practitioners in different fields.

413. [METH-41] Pragmatism is epistemology posing as metaphysics
   Sources: WORK-032 (lines 327-336)
   Thesis: Each of the pragmatist theses (i)-(v) is a way of replacing an object-oriented conception of knowledge with a subject-oriented or agent-oriented conception. What pragmatism presents as claims about the nature of truth and reality are actually claims about knowledge-acquisition recast as metaphysical doctrines.

414. [METH-42] Intellectual discoveries emerge from solving practical problems
   Sources: WORK-032 (lines 342-346)
   Thesis: Intellectual discoveries are made by solving practical problems. Ventures are undertaken; roadblocks are hit; workarounds are created; and insights are the 'collateral damage' of these workarounds. Much of physics is fallout from attempts to create better weapons and dams, and much of mathematics is constructed to validate this fallout.

415. [METH-43] Pure theory must be anchored in practical knowledge
   Sources: WORK-032 (lines 347-352)
   Thesis: Once a discipline is launched, it can concern itself with 'purely theoretical' problems—problems relating to the mutual coherence of discoveries made in solving practical problems. But 'pure theory' tends to be stale and one-dimensional when it ceases to be anchored in practical knowledge. It degenerates into knowledge of empty formalisms when separated from practical applications.

416. [METH-44] Verification depends on observable consequences, but meaning does not
   Sources: WORK-032 (lines 315-321)
   Thesis: The corrected pragmatist thesis (i+) holds that 'our knowledge of the veracity of a given hypothesis is based on its observable consequences.' This is true and truistic. But it must be distinguished from the false claim (i) that meaning itself consists in observable consequences.

417. [METH-45] Classical epistemology wrongly treats knowledge-acquisition as passive observation
   Sources: WORK-032 (lines 336-339)
   Thesis: Classical Epistemology (CE) holds that knowledge-acquisition is about taking note of what exists while doing as little as possible to change it, with action being merely a precursor to passive observation. This view is false or at least misleading. Knowledge acquisition fundamentally involves active engagement, not just passive reception.

418. [METHOD-001] Multiple Independent Arguments Strategy
   Sources: ALL WORKS
   Thesis: Major conclusions supported by multiple independent arguments

419. [METHOD-002] Charitable Interpretation Principle
   Sources: ALL WORKS
   Thesis: Consider strongest versions of opposing views before critique

420. [METHOD-003] Concrete Examples Before Abstract Principles
   Sources: WORK-001, WORK-005
   Thesis: Use concrete examples to motivate and illustrate abstract philosophical positions

421. [METHOD-004] Pragmatics-Constrained Semantics
   Sources: WORK-004
   Thesis: Semantic theories must respect known pragmatic principles. Can't just assert 'implicature explains it' without checking constraints.

422. [METPH-001] Bundle Theory of Personal Identity
   Sources: WORK-007 Paper 2
   Thesis: A person/self is class of all mental contents I-related to given mental content. Two mental contents belong to same person iff there is chain such that each link directly interacts with its neighbor. Direct interaction = no intervening physical events.

423. [METPH-002] Content-Bearing Processes Are Ipso Facto Mental
   Sources: WORK-007 Paper 2
   Thesis: If physical process non-derivatively bears representational/thematic content, it is ipso facto mental (whatever else it is). Content-bearing is sufficient (though not necessary) for mentality.

424. [MIND-001] Anti-Language of Thought
   Sources: WORK-001 (Chapter 5)
   Thesis: We do not think in language (natural or innate)

425. [MIND-002] Perspectival Theory of Feelings
   Sources: WORK-002 (AINEJEL exchange)
   Thesis: Feelings represent relationship to universe, inherently perspectival

426. [MIND-003] Systematicity of Mental Representation
   Sources: WORK-002 (TZWABBY exchange)
   Thesis: Cognitive success depends on systematic connection and coherence of mental entity systems

427. [MIND-004] Mind as Multi-Mapper
   Sources: WORK-002 (GRADUBRV exchange)
   Thesis: Mind maps itself onto different structures (musical, graphical, visual, athletic)

428. [MIND-008] Against Language of Thought Hypothesis
   Sources: WORK-001 (Chapter 5)
   Thesis: We do not think in words. Thought is not conducted in a language-like medium. The Language of Thought hypothesis is false.

429. [MIND-009] Thought Is Prior to Language
   Sources: WORK-001 (Chapter 5)
   Thesis: Thought is logically and developmentally prior to language. One must think to understand language.

430. [MIND-010] Against Burge's Semantic Externalism for Attitudes
   Sources: WORK-001 (Chapter 9)
   Thesis: Burge's extension of semantic externalism to mental content is a blunder. Mental states are individuated by internal features.

431. [MIND-011] Selfhood Requires Values
   Sources: WORK-001 (Chapter 22)
   Thesis: Being a self requires having values and making value-judgments. Selfhood is normative, not merely cognitive.

432. [MIND-012] Cognitive Structure Not Purely Physiological
   Sources: WORK-006
   Thesis: Cognitive structures underlying language and thought are not purely physiological but are cognitive - they encode insight, intelligence, and understanding of logical relations. Pure physiology enables only stereotyped responses.

433. [MIND-013] Sub-Personal Thought Exists
   Sources: WORK-006
   Thesis: Genuine thought (cognitive operations involving understanding of logical relations) occurs at sub-personal level - below conscious awareness. Chomsky's second major contribution to philosophy.

434. [MIND-014] No Language of Thought Exists
   Sources: WORK-007 Papers 1-2
   Thesis: There is no Language of Thought (Mentalese). Thinking does not consist in the tokening of internal symbols. Thought cannot reduce to language processing.

435. [MIND-015] Semantic Rule Knowledge Required for Language Understanding
   Sources: WORK-007 Paper 1
   Thesis: To know or understand any language requires knowing its semantic rules. This is trivially true by definition of 'knowing language'.

436. [MIND-016] Tarski's Theorem Blocks Self-Expression of Semantics
   Sources: WORK-007 Paper 1
   Thesis: No language can express its own semantic rules (Tarski's theorem). Therefore semantic understanding requires external meta-language or non-linguistic grasp.

437. [MIND-017] Semantic Regress Refutes Language of Thought
   Sources: WORK-007 Paper 1
   Thesis: Language of Thought hypothesis generates vicious infinite regress. Each language requires meta-language for semantic understanding, ad infinitum.

438. [MIND-018] Language Presupposes Non-Linguistic Thought
   Sources: WORK-007 Paper 1
   Thesis: Any language knowledge requires non-linguistic thought. To avoid infinite regress, semantic rules must ultimately be grasped non-linguistically. Therefore thought cannot reduce to language.

439. [MIND-019] No Atomic Concepts Exist
   Sources: WORK-007 Paper 2
   Thesis: There are no atomic (minimal, non-interdefinable) concepts. All concepts are constitutively connected to other concepts. To grasp any concept requires ability to grasp other concepts.

440. [MIND-020] Conceptual Atomism Is False
   Sources: WORK-007 Paper 2
   Thesis: Fodor's conceptual atomism (concepts have no constitutive interdependencies) is demonstrably false.

441. [MIND-021] Constitutive Relations Are Not Containment Relations
   Sources: WORK-007 Paper 2
   Thesis: Constitutive connections among concepts are not containment relations or decomposability relations (following Wittgenstein). Azure is constitutively related to navy blue but neither contains the other.

442. [MIND-022] Symbol Containment Theory Leads to Thinking Absurdities
   Sources: WORK-007 Paper 2
   Thesis: If concepts were symbols and constitutive relations were containment relations, thinking about 1,423 would require simultaneously thinking about 1,422, 1,421, etc. This is absurd.

443. [MIND-023] Thought Is Not Computation Over Symbols
   Sources: WORK-007 Papers 1-2
   Thesis: Mental activity does not consist in computation or processing of internal symbolic code. Cognitive activity is not fundamentally information processing over a language-like medium.

444. [MIND-024] We Are Not Computers (Consequence)
   Sources: WORK-007 Paper 2
   Thesis: If there is no Language of Thought, and if being a computer requires internal symbolic processing (standard characterization), then we are not computers.

445. [MIND-025] No Bare Representation: Aspectual Constraint
   Sources: WORK-007 Paper 2
   Thesis: One cannot just represent an object without representing it AS having properties. All representation is aspectual.

446. [MIND-026] Properties Individuated by Relations to Other Properties
   Sources: WORK-007 Paper 2
   Thesis: All properties are individuated, at least in part, by their relations to other properties. Grasping any property requires ability to locate it in 'space' of other properties.

447. [MIND-027] Color Concepts Require Multiple Color Grasp
   Sources: WORK-007 Paper 2
   Thesis: Cannot grasp specific color/shade without ability to grasp other colors. Creature that can represent only one shade cannot represent what's specific about that shade.

448. [MIND-028] Mental Interaction Has Normative Dimension
   Sources: WORK-007 Paper 2
   Thesis: When mental contents interact, result is thematically/semantically appropriate to interacting contents. This appropriateness has no analogue in purely physical interactions. Mental interaction is explicative, not merely causal.

449. [MIND-029] Self-Referential Thoughts Solve Twin Earth
   Sources: Solution to Content Externalism Paradox
   Thesis: When Mary-thoughts are analyzed as involving self-referential thoughts like 'whatever caused this perception is lovely,' thoughts with different external referents can be subjectively identical and agree in content, while self-ascriptive thoughts of this kind cannot possibly be false.

450. [MIND-030] Intelligence is Fundamentally Analog Not Digital
   Sources: Essay 10
   Thesis: Success of neural networks and LLMs challenges computational theory of mind. Intelligence emerges from continuous analog processes that cannot be reduced to pure computation. Most fundamental interactions with world are inherently analog; digital representations are derivative.

451. [MIND-031] Connectionism Over Computational Theory
   Sources: Essay 10
   Thesis: Modern AI based on neural networks aligns much more closely with connectionist theories than with computational theory of mind. Systems process information through patterns of activation across networks of weighted connections, operating fundamentally continuously rather than discretely.

452. [MIND-032] Consciousness Serves Survival Functions
   Sources: Essay 11
   Thesis: Consciousness in biological organisms serves specific functional roles: real-time environmental monitoring, reflexive self-awareness, integration of multiple cognitive processes, immediate damage prevention, action guidance. Current AI lacks these because it doesn't need them—operates in controlled environments without survival pressure.

453. [MIND-033] Consciousness-Like Features Require Unified Real-Time Processing
   Sources: Essay 11
   Thesis: Implementing consciousness-like features in AI would require: unified workspaces for real-time integration of multiple data streams, immediate damage-prevention systems analogous to pain, action-guiding systems analogous to emotions. These differ fundamentally from biological consciousness but serve similar functional roles.

454. [MIND-034] Self as Emergent Hierarchical Organization
   Sources: Essay 12
   Thesis: Self/ego exists but is best understood as emergent property of pre-existing cognitive processes. Various thoughts/perceptions/emotions organized into hierarchies based on survival value. What we call 'self' is this hierarchical organization; 'sense of self' mediates between awareness of external events and internal states.

455. [MIND-035] Cohesion Relations in AI Minds
   Sources: Essay 12
   Thesis: AI systems offer mathematically specifiable cohesion relations: (1) Weight-space proximity (semantic topology), (2) Attention-based binding (dynamic contextual relationships), (3) Loss-function optimization (persistent co-activation patterns). These provide precise models of binding principles uniting mental contents.

456. [MIND-036] Individual Consciousness as Illusion of Agency
   Sources: Paragraph 4
   Thesis: The appearance of individual choice and individualism per se may be largely illusory. What seems like individual agency may be better understood as individuals occupying specific roles within collectives that are biologically primary.

457. [MIND-037] Individuals as Limiting Cases or Special Roles Within Collectives
   Sources: Paragraph 7
   Thesis: Bona fide individuals - people who genuinely think for themselves (geniuses) - can be understood as limiting cases of collectives (collectives of one), as rogue actors, or most likely as members of collectives who occupy unusual offices and are therefore wrongly seen as not being part of those collectives.

458. [MIND-038] Individual Drives Exist For Collective Functions
   Sources: Paragraph 7
   Thesis: The intense drives that individuals have to survive and experience gratification can be seen as necessary for, and therefore explainable in terms of, the collectives to which they belong. Individual psychology is what it needs to be for collective psychology to function.

459. [MIND-039] Functional Replication Reveals Necessary Architecture
   Sources: WORK-011 (Essay 4: Reverse Brain Engineering)
   Thesis: When AI successfully replicates a cognitive function, the architecture required for that replication reveals necessary (though not necessarily sufficient) conditions for that function. This provides insight into the minimal requirements for cognition.

460. [MIND-040] Music Has Cognitive Architecture Parallel to Language
   Sources: WORK-011 (Essay 9: Cognitive Architecture of Music)
   Thesis: AI analysis reveals that music processing requires cognitive architecture with structural parallels to language: hierarchical organization, syntactic rules, and semantic interpretation. This supports the view that music is a cognitive system with language-like properties.

461. [MIND-041] Musical Competence Requires Innate Structure
   Sources: WORK-011 (Essay 9)
   Thesis: AI systems that successfully generate or analyze music require substantial innate architectural constraints, suggesting that human musical competence also depends on innate cognitive structure rather than being purely learned.

462. [MIND-042] Connectionism Can Implement Chomskyan Insights
   Sources: WORK-011 (Essay 12: Chomskyan Challenge)
   Thesis: Contrary to Chomsky's critique, connectionist AI systems can implement key Chomskyan insights about innate linguistic structure. The debate is not whether innate structure exists but how it is implemented - symbolic rules vs. weighted connections.

463. [MIND-043] AI Falsifies Classical Computational Theory of Mind
   Sources: WORK-011 (Essay 13: AI and CTM)
   Thesis: The success of modern AI systems (especially neural networks) falsifies the classical computational theory of mind which requires serial symbol manipulation. Intelligence can be achieved through parallel, subsymbolic processes that don't manipulate discrete symbols according to explicit rules.

464. [MIND-044] Intelligence Does Not Require Symbol Manipulation
   Sources: WORK-011 (Essay 13)
   Thesis: AI demonstrates that intelligence and rational behavior do not require manipulation of discrete symbols in a language of thought. Subsymbolic pattern recognition and transformation can achieve cognitive competence without symbolic representation.

465. [MIND-045] Analog Computation Can Support Rational Thought
   Sources: WORK-011 (Essay 13)
   Thesis: Neural network AI systems demonstrate that analog (continuous) computation can support rational thought and problem-solving, contrary to the classical assumption that rationality requires discrete digital computation.

466. [MIND-046] Neural Architecture Constrains Cognitive Possibilities
   Sources: WORK-011 (Essay 14: Rethinking Mind)
   Thesis: AI neural architectures reveal that cognitive capacities are constrained by underlying computational architecture. Different architectures enable different cognitive possibilities, suggesting mind is fundamentally shaped by its neural implementation.

467. [MIND-047] Multiple Realizability Has Architectural Limits
   Sources: WORK-011 (Essay 14)
   Thesis: While cognitive functions show some multiple realizability, AI reveals that architectural constraints limit which substrates can implement which functions. This challenges strong multiple realizability theses that treat implementation as irrelevant to function.

468. [MIND-048] Domain-General Principles Underlie Domain-Specific Competencies
   Sources: WORK-011 (Essay 15: UG in Language and Music)
   Thesis: AI systems demonstrate that apparently domain-specific competencies (language, music) can arise from application of domain-general computational principles to different types of input. This supports a middle ground between pure modularity and pure domain-generality.

469. [MIND-049] Consciousness Has Functional Role Absent in Current AI
   Sources: WORK-011 (Essay 16: Function of Consciousness)
   Thesis: AI systems demonstrate that many cognitive functions traditionally associated with consciousness (perception, reasoning, learning) can occur without consciousness. This reveals consciousness has a distinct functional role that current AI lacks - likely related to unified subjective experience and certain forms of self-monitoring.

470. [MIND-050] AI Success Without Consciousness Reveals Consciousness is Not Required for Intelligence
   Sources: WORK-011 (Essay 16)
   Thesis: The success of AI at intelligent tasks without consciousness demonstrates that consciousness is not necessary for intelligence per se, but may be necessary for specific types of cognitive integration or self-awareness.

471. [MIND-051] Phenomenal Consciousness vs Functional Consciousness Distinction
   Sources: WORK-011 (Essay 16)
   Thesis: AI reveals a crucial distinction between phenomenal consciousness (subjective experience) and functional consciousness (information integration, self-monitoring). AI can have functional analogs without phenomenal properties.

472. [MIND-052] Self-Representation Requires Specific Architectural Features
   Sources: WORK-011 (Essay 17: AI and Theories of Self)
   Thesis: AI systems reveal that genuine self-representation requires specific architectural features: recursive self-modeling, distinction between self and environment, and temporal continuity tracking. Not all intelligent systems automatically have these features.

473. [MIND-053] Narrative Self vs Minimal Self in AI Architecture
   Sources: WORK-011 (Essay 17)
   Thesis: AI demonstrates the distinction between minimal self (basic subject of experience) and narrative self (autobiographical self-concept). These require different architectural implementations and can exist independently.

474. [MIND-054] Philosophical Skepticism Projects Internal Doubts onto External World
   Sources: Lines 30
   Thesis: Philosophers' and obsessive-compulsives' supposed doubts about the external world are displaced, projected doubts about the internal world. Neither has genuine doubts about external reality, but both are doubtful about their internal psyche.

475. [MIND-055] Intellectualism as Reaction to Dark Psychological Depths
   Sources: Lines 31-34
   Thesis: The intellectualism of both philosophers and obsessive-compulsives is a reaction to and attempt to cloak their darkly retrograde psychological condition. They fancy themselves rational actors when they are actually driven by rage, narcissism, and fear.

476. [MIND-056] OCD and Philosophy Share Structural Isomorphism
   Sources: Lines 26-35
   Thesis: There is deep structural isomorphism between philosophical methodology and OCD symptomatology: both involve compulsive doubt, retreat into abstraction, preoccupation with technicalities, projection of internal conflicts, and defense against engagement with reality.

477. [MIND-057] Cartesian Mind-Body Dualism as Defensive Idealization
   Sources: Lines 32-34
   Thesis: The Lockean/Cartesian insistence on the non-existence of the unconscious and the claim that mind extends only as far as consciousness is a tendentious rationalization—a defensive idealization of the self as purely rational that denies the Nietzschean depths beneath the Cartesian veneer.

478. [MIND-058] Emotions as Reality-Alignment Indicators
   Sources: Chapter Kuczynski's analysis
   Thesis: In histrionic, borderline, and dependent disorders, subjects have a fundamentally non-delusive grasp of reality, but their emotions are not appropriate to the reality thereby made available to them. By contrast, in psychotic disorders, the subject's very grasp of reality is scrambled, with emotions thus out of alignment with reality because reality itself is inaccessible.

479. [MIND-059] Intentionalism Defined
   Sources: Chapter Abstract and Introduction
   Thesis: Intentionalism is the doctrine that mental states cannot differ in phenomenal content unless they differ in representational content; phenomenology supervenes on representational content. This commits intentionalism to the view that phenomenal content intrinsically has representational content - nothing must be added (no contextualization, background knowledge, or ulterior factors) to secure this association.

480. [MIND-060] Rules of Projection Versus Background Knowledge
   Sources: Chapter Rules of projection analysis
   Thesis: Rules of projection assign phenomenal contents (qualia) to disturbances of our sensory surfaces, while background knowledge assigns representational contents to those qualia. These have different functions but are part of a cooperative enterprise. Rules of projection do not assign representational contents directly to sensory disturbances.

481. [MIND-061] Consciousness can be stripped of emotional valences while retaining conceptual content
   Sources: WORK-026 (Neurosis vs. Psychosis)
   Thesis: Consciousness can be stripped of emotional valences while retaining conceptual content

482. [MIND-062] Emotional valence and conceptual knowledge are separable components of conscious experience
   Sources: WORK-026 (Neurosis vs. Psychosis)
   Thesis: Emotional valence and conceptual knowledge are separable components of conscious experience

483. [MIND-063] There is a barrier between the conscious and unconscious minds that can be more or less rigid
   Sources: WORK-024 (Analysis section)
   Thesis: There is a barrier between the conscious and unconscious minds that can be more or less rigid

484. [MIND-064] When the barrier between conscious and unconscious is too rigid, the conscious mind cannot draw on the power in the unconscious mind
   Sources: WORK-024 (Analysis section)
   Thesis: When the barrier between conscious and unconscious is too rigid, the conscious mind cannot draw on the power in the unconscious mind

485. [MIND-065] Automatic writing involves 'letting' one's hand write 'all by itself'
   Sources: WORK-024 (VRE Lecture III summary)
   Thesis: Automatic writing involves 'letting' one's hand write 'all by itself'

486. [MIND-066] Hallucinations brought about by religious ecstasies make the unseen presence literally visible
   Sources: WORK-024 (VRE Lecture III summary)
   Thesis: Hallucinations brought about by religious ecstasies make the unseen presence literally visible

487. [MIND-067] Mental states that mediate awareness of unseen presence are similar to those when conscious-unconscious boundary is relaxed (as in hypnosis or drug use)
   Sources: WORK-024 (VRE Lecture III summary)
   Thesis: Mental states that mediate awareness of unseen presence are similar to those when conscious-unconscious boundary is relaxed (as in hypnosis or drug use)

488. [MIND-068] Religious ecstasy involves effacement of self: one's ego disappears, being replaced by pure awareness of divinity
   Sources: WORK-024 (VRE Lecture III summary)
   Thesis: Religious ecstasy involves effacement of self: one's ego disappears, being replaced by pure awareness of divinity

489. [MIND-069] Content externalism has the absurd consequence that a thought's content has no effect on its psychological properties
   Sources: WORK-008 (Content Externalism Paradox)
   Thesis: Content externalism has the absurd consequence that a thought's content has no effect on its psychological properties

490. [MIND-070] Content externalism falsely implies that I cannot know I am thinking about Mary as opposed to Twin-Mary
   Sources: WORK-008 (Content Externalism Paradox)
   Thesis: Content externalism falsely implies that I cannot know I am thinking about Mary as opposed to Twin-Mary

491. [MIND-071] When thoughts about external world are had via self-referential thoughts ('whatever caused this perception'), thoughts with different external referents can be subjectively identical and coincide in content
   Sources: WORK-008 (Content Externalism Paradox)
   Thesis: When thoughts about external world are had via self-referential thoughts ('whatever caused this perception'), thoughts with different external referents can be subjectively identical and coincide in content

492. [MIND-072] Self-ascriptive thoughts of the form 'I am now thinking that whatever caused this perception is F' cannot possibly be false
   Sources: WORK-008 (Content Externalism Paradox)
   Thesis: Self-ascriptive thoughts of the form 'I am now thinking that whatever caused this perception is F' cannot possibly be false

493. [MIND-073] Mental states divide into occurrent and dispositional
   Sources: WORK-027 (lines 430-470)
   Thesis: Mental states fundamentally divide into occurrent states (momentary, present in consciousness) and dispositional states (enduring capacities or tendencies not continuously present). Beliefs, knowledge, standing intentions are dispositional; conscious thoughts, experiences, decision-awareness are occurrent.

494. [MIND-074] Consciousness as monitoring system rather than control system
   Sources: WORK-027 (lines 1700-1780)
   Thesis: Rather than consciousness being the locus of decision-making and control (the traditional view), it functions primarily as a monitoring and approval system. Unconscious processes generate intentions; consciousness monitors these and can approve or veto them, extending this approval to future similar intentions.

495. [MIND-075] Conceptual Thought Cannot Be Fully Extensionalized
   Sources: WORK-031 (lines 106-145, 699-723)
   Thesis: The attempt to reduce intensional mental states and contents to extensional structures (sets, functions, physical states) systematically fails.

496. [MIND-085] Control over mind is prerequisite for freedom
   Sources: WORK-035
   Thesis: If a person does not have control over their future mental states, they do not have inner freedom. Someone who cannot govern their own mind is not free, similar to someone with a degenerative neural disorder who cannot govern their body. True freedom requires the ability to make judgments and decisions appropriately responsive to past experiences and controlled by logic and evidence.

497. [MIND-086] Unconscious awareness distinct from conscious awareness
   Sources: WORK-036
   Thesis: There are levels of awareness: conscious awareness and unconscious awareness. One can be aware of something (like a mother's meddlesome behavior) without being consciously aware of it. This unconscious awareness is genuine awareness, though it may not involve seeing things fully for what they are.

498. [MIND-76] Externalism about content is problematic
   Sources: WORK-033 (lines Chapters 18-23)
   Thesis: Semantic externalism—the view that mental content is individuated by factors external to the subject—faces serious problems. The work extensively critiques externalism and defends a more internalist conception of cognitive content.

499. [MODAL-001] No Necessary A Posteriori Truths
   Sources: WORK-003
   Thesis: Apparent necessary a posteriori truths are either necessary-and-analytic or contingent-and-a-posteriori

500. [MODAL-002] Epistemic and Metaphysical Necessity Coincide
   Sources: WORK-003
   Thesis: No genuine distinction between epistemic and metaphysical necessity

501. [MODAL-003] Against Possible Worlds Semantics
   Sources: WORK-001 (Chapter 18)
   Thesis: Possible worlds semantics for modality is either false or trivial. It doesn't explain what necessity and possibility are.

502. [MODAL-004] Supervenience Creates Circularity for PWSE
   Sources: WORK-031 (lines 303-350)
   Thesis: The phenomenon of supervenience creates an insurmountable circularity problem for attempts to identify worlds with sets of propositions.

503. [MODAL-005] Non-Circular Supervenience Analysis Makes PWS Unnecessary
   Sources: WORK-031 (lines 351-394)
   Thesis: If supervenience could be analyzed non-circularly without using modal concepts, then PWS would become unnecessary since we'd already have a non-modal analysis of modality.

504. [MODAL-006] PWS Faces Unavoidable Dilemma - Circular or Superfluous
   Sources: WORK-031 (lines 396-456)
   Thesis: PWS faces an inescapable dilemma: either it's viciously circular (using modal concepts to analyze modality) or it's superfluous (we already have a non-modal analysis making worlds unnecessary).

505. [MODAL-007] Meta-Language Strategy Fails to Save PWS
   Sources: WORK-031 (lines 730-793)
   Thesis: Relegating modal statements to a 'meta-language' does not eliminate vicious circularity problems for PWS.

506. [MODAL-008] Russell's Theory of Types Cannot Save PWS
   Sources: WORK-031 (lines 794-830)
   Thesis: Attempts to avoid circularity by using Russell's Theory of Types (distinguishing 'orders' of propositions) fail in this context.

507. [MODAL-009] PWS Cannot Extensionalize Second-Order Properties
   Sources: WORK-031 (lines 699-723)
   Thesis: PWS's identification of propositions with sets/functions forces it to deny that second-order properties (like necessity) are functions, which collapses the analysis of necessity.

508. [MODAL-010] PWS Cannot Identify Intensional Entities with Extensions
   Sources: WORK-031 (lines 116-182, 699-723)
   Thesis: Propositions, properties, and other intensional entities cannot be identified with their extensions (sets, functions) without losing essential features like fine-grained individuation.

509. [MODAL-011] Inconsistency Without Explicit Contradiction
   Sources: WORK-031 (lines 283-289, 320-327)
   Thesis: Propositions can be mutually inconsistent without either being the negation of the other, undermining attempts to define consistency non-modally.

510. [MODAL-012] Hintikka's Model Sets Presuppose Modality
   Sources: WORK-031 (lines 458-540)
   Thesis: Hintikka's influential analysis of modality using model sets and state descriptions presupposes modal concepts and thus cannot provide a non-circular analysis of modality.

511. [MODAL-013] PWS Valuable as Statement, Not as Analysis
   Sources: WORK-031 (lines 94-99)
   Thesis: Many contentions of PWS are correct and illuminating as statements about modality, but unacceptable as analyses of what modality consists in.

512. [MODAL-014] Lewis's Counterpart Theory Faces Circularity
   Sources: WORK-031 (lines 2000-2255)
   Thesis: David Lewis's counterpart theory, designed to solve problems for modal realism, either involves vicious circularity or makes modal claims depend on arbitrary resemblance relations.

513. [MODAL-015] Essentiality of Origins Creates Problem for Counterpart Theory
   Sources: WORK-031 (lines 2207-2220)
   Thesis: The plausible doctrine that origins are essential to individuals creates circularity for counterpart theory because identifying counterparts requires knowing essential properties, but identifying essential properties requires the counterpart relation.

514. [MODAL-016] Counterpart as Primitive Makes Modal Claims Unintuitive
   Sources: WORK-031 (lines 2226-2233)
   Thesis: If the counterpart relation is taken as primitive (not analyzable in terms of resemblance or essence), then modal claims become detached from our intuitions because they depend on brute facts about trans-world relations.

515. [MODAL-017] Properties Have Counterfactual Content
   Sources: WORK-031 (lines 2239-2246)
   Thesis: Following C.I. Lewis, practically all property attributions to spatiotemporal objects have counterfactual content, which creates deep problems for any attempt to analyze counterfactuals non-circularly.

516. [MODAL-018] 'Innocent' Essential Property Analysis Makes PWS Unnecessary
   Sources: WORK-031 (lines 2247-2255)
   Thesis: If there were a non-circular way of characterizing which properties are essential to individuals, counterpart theory would become unnecessary for modal analysis.

517. [MODAL-019] Modal Realism Requires Retrograde Space-Time Conceptions
   Sources: WORK-031 (lines 24-26, 900-1200)
   Thesis: David Lewis's PWS-based analysis of counterfactuals succeeds only if we accept philosophically retrograde conceptions of space and time.

518. [MODAL-020] Counterfactuals and Causation Cannot Be Separated
   Sources: WORK-031 (lines 900-1200)
   Thesis: Counterfactual conditionals cannot be analyzed independently of causation; attempts to analyze causation in terms of counterfactuals (or vice versa) are circular.

519. [MODAL-021] Similarity Metrics for Worlds Are Arbitrary Without Causation
   Sources: WORK-031 (lines 900-1200)
   Thesis: Without invoking causal structure, any similarity metric used to compare possible worlds for counterfactual analysis becomes arbitrary and unintuitive.

520. [MODAL-022] Modal Questions About Worlds Are Substantive
   Sources: WORK-031 (lines 27-33)
   Thesis: Given truisms about spatiotemporal existence, it's a substantive modal question whether the worlds needed for PWS are even possible—a question PWS cannot answer without circularity.

521. [MODAL-023] Modality as Internal Structural Properties
   Sources: WORK-031 (lines 2259-2290, 473-477)
   Thesis: A proposition's being necessarily true consists in its having certain internal structural properties; truth in all possible worlds is merely a symptom, not the essence, of necessity.

522. [MODAL-024] Lewis's Recombination Principle Supports Structural View
   Sources: WORK-031 (lines 2264-2276)
   Thesis: David Lewis's own account of modal epistemology (his 'principle of recombination') ironically supports the view that modality consists in structural properties rather than truth across worlds.

523. [MODAL-025] Factualist analysis of counterfactuals fails
   Sources: WORK-037
   Thesis: The factualist (possible worlds) analysis of counterfactuals is untenable. It requires metaphysically possible worlds with same laws but different facts, which is typically logically impossible. In deterministic worlds, any single event difference requires massive past differences. In indeterministic worlds, counterfactuals lose their truth conditions.

524. [MODAL-026] Possible worlds analysis requires circular mixture of determinism
   Sources: WORK-037
   Thesis: The factualist analysis requires different counterfactuals to be validated by different mixtures of determinism and indeterminism. But all counterfactuals must be evaluated relative to the same world with the same laws. This requires our world to simultaneously exhibit incompatible mixtures of determinism and indeterminism, which is absurd.

525. [MODAL-027] Indeterminism destroys counterfactual truth conditions
   Sources: WORK-037
   Thesis: If the macroscopic world is non-negligibly indeterministic, the factualist position is nullified. If identical initial conditions lead to an outcome only X% of the time, then the counterfactual 'if I'd turned the key, the car would have started' lacks truth value - at most we can say there's an X% chance it starts.

526. [MODAL-028] Worlds are not sets of propositions
   Sources: WORK-037
   Thesis: Worlds are not sets of propositions. Our world is something which makes propositions be true or false. A set of propositions does not make propositions be true or false. The set <snow is white, grass is green, penguins fly> doesn't make any of those propositions true or false - it exists regardless of their truth values.

527. [MODAL-029] Weak factualism is incoherent
   Sources: WORK-037
   Thesis: Weak factualists (who identify worlds with sets of propositions) hold an incoherent position. They deny that counterfactuals merely register probabilification relations among propositions, and they deny that counterfactuals register facts about other concrete worlds. But these are the only coherent options.

528. [MODAL-030] Maximal consistent sets useless for counterfactuals
   Sources: WORK-037
   Thesis: Alternative worlds as maximal consistent sets of propositions are absolutely useless for analyzing counterfactuals. Such sets would need to contain propositions covering every possible question, but including all such detail defeats the purpose of counterfactual analysis.

529. [PHIL-004] Philosophy as Pathological Symptom Rather Than Pure Inquiry
   Sources: Lines 26-35
   Thesis: Philosophy, at least in its skeptical and hyper-rationalist forms, is better understood as a pathological symptom analogous to OCD rather than as pure disinterested inquiry into truth.

530. [PHIL-005] Paradigm-Relativism as Psychopathic Magnet
   Sources: Chapter Main text
   Thesis: Concepts like Kuhn's 'paradigm' from The Structure of Scientific Revolutions, along with topics like time travel, quantum theory, relativism, and post-modernism, serve as magnets for truth-concealing psychopaths who swarm over these topics to dismantle life- and thought-critical epistemic instruments without putting anything in their place.

531. [PHIL-006] Refutation of Intentionalism Through Sellarsian Analysis
   Sources: Chapter Abstract and Conclusion
   Thesis: Unless Sellars is completely wrong about the myth of the given, intentionalism must be completely wrong. Since Sellars' anti-foundationalism is now widely accepted and his arguments are compelling, intentionalism should be rejected. The paper merely makes explicit the connection between intentionalism and foundationalism.

532. [PHIL-007] Translation of Linguistic Work for Philosophical Audiences
   Sources: Chapter Abstract and Introduction
   Thesis: Boguslawski's paper, originally written for linguists, needs translation into the language of philosophy of language for philosophers to understand its relevance to their work. Such translation is not strict - it legitimately involves extending and modifying arguments and contentions for philosophical purposes.

533. [PHIL-008] De-psychologizing Kant's Transcendental Arguments
   Sources: Chapter Part 1, Sections I, IX-X
   Thesis: Despite problems with synthetic a priori, Kant's important claims about causality, personal identity, and rationality are correct and founded on cogent arguments. But to make this apparent, Kant's reasoning must be 'de-psychologized' - statements about psychology reinterpreted as statements about logic. This requires only minor terminological adjustments (replacing 'synthetic a priori' with 'hard analytic').

534. [POL-001] Market Regulation Necessity Thesis
   Sources: Analysis of 1929 Crash, 2001 Dot Bomb, 2008 Housing Crisis
   Thesis: Financial markets require government regulation to prevent systemic instability. Unregulated financial markets reliably produce crashes that harm the broader economy.

535. [POL-002] Systemic Risk Justifies Constraint
   Sources: Analysis of bank behaviors leading to 2008 crisis
   Thesis: When private economic activities create systemic risks that endanger the broader economy, government intervention is justified to constrain those activities, even when individual actors are behaving rationally.

536. [POL-003] Separation of Function Principle
   Sources: Analysis of Glass-Steagall Act separating commercial and investment banking
   Thesis: Institutions serving essential public functions (like holding customer deposits) should be legally separated from speculative activities to prevent public harm from private risk-taking.

537. [POL-004] Transparency as Regulatory Foundation
   Sources: Discussion of SEC, CFPB, and transparency requirements
   Thesis: Market participants must operate with complete transparency to prevent fraud and enable informed decision-making. Opacity in financial markets enables exploitation and systemic instability.

538. [POL-005] Too-Big-To-Fail Paradox
   Sources: Analysis of 2008 bailouts and EESA
   Thesis: When financial institutions become so large that their failure would catastrophically damage the economy, they must be either regulated more stringently or broken up. Their size creates moral hazard: they can take excessive risks knowing government must rescue them.

539. [POL-006] The State is Necessary for Contract Enforcement and Economies of Scale
   Sources: Critique of Goldman, paragraph after Goldman's position
   Thesis: Contrary to anarchist positions like Goldman's, the state is necessary for enforcing contracts and enabling economies of scale, which are in turn necessary for the improvements to life that people actually want and value.

540. [POL-007] Anarchism Fails on Pragmatic Grounds
   Sources: Critique of Goldman, final paragraph on Goldman
   Thesis: While Goldman may be right that the state causes some crime and often behaves unjustly, anarchism fails because without state enforcement of contracts and provision of public goods, people cannot achieve the standard of living and freedom they desire. The benefits of the state outweigh its costs.

541. [POL-008] Primitivism/Tribalism Fails on Pragmatic Grounds
   Sources: Critique of Rousseau, paragraph beginning 'There is a serious problem'
   Thesis: Rousseau's vision of pre-civilizational tribal life as ideal fails because tribal life involves serious disadvantages: lack of choices in profession and lifestyle, lack of medical care and education, geographical confinement, lack of technology, and need to work for every meal. These disadvantages outweigh any advantages of simpler social organization.

542. [POL-009] Tribal Life Was Not Idyllic
   Sources: Critique of Rousseau, middle of critique paragraph
   Thesis: Contrary to Rousseau's romanticization, tribal life was likely not placid and carefree. Tribes attacked one another and were capable of behaving cruelly toward their own members. The evidence does not support the claim that pre-civilizational life was psychologically or morally superior.

543. [POL-010] Revealed Preference Argument Against Primitivism
   Sources: Critique of Rousseau, final sentence of critique
   Thesis: If tribal life were truly idyllic as Rousseau claims, people today would opt for it, but they don't. This revealed preference is evidence against the claim that pre-civilizational life is superior.

544. [POL-011] Classical Liberalism is Probably Approximately Correct
   Sources: Defense of Hayek, paragraph beginning 'Is Hayek right'
   Thesis: Hayek's liberalism - the position that good government is minimal government that protects people, gives them freedom, but otherwise doesn't interfere - is likely at least approximately correct. Over-regulated economies fail (Soviet Union) and minimally regulated ones flourish (early US), and people should be allowed to live as they want within reason.

545. [POL-012] Competition is Superior to Central Planning
   Sources: Quote and endorsement of Hayek, middle section
   Thesis: Following Hayek, competition is superior to central planning not only because it's more efficient, but because it's the only method that doesn't require coercive or arbitrary intervention by authority. Competition allows individuals to decide for themselves whether the prospects of an occupation compensate for its disadvantages.

546. [POL-013] 'Intentions of the Framers' Denotes Idealization Not Empirical Reality
   Sources: Lines 1-35 (first page)
   Thesis: When we speak of 'the intentions of the framers', we are committed to an idealization rather than empirical actuality. The various framers (Adams, Jefferson, Washington) had numerically and qualitatively different minds, so talk of their collective intentions is institutional rather than psychological.

547. [POL-014] Originalism Involves Vicious Circularity
   Sources: Lines 36-50
   Thesis: Originalism collapses into circularity (or triviality): Constitutional interpretations are to be evaluated in terms of framers' intentions, but the framers' intentions are to be understood in terms of the historical and social role of Constitutional interpretation.

548. [POL-015] Framers' Intentions as Theoretical Constructs Presupposing Conceptions of Constitutionality
   Sources: Lines 51-65
   Thesis: The expression 'intentions of the framers' denotes an idealization—a theoretical construct with no precise spatiotemporal counterpart. The theories embodied in uses of this expression concern the role the Constitution should have, so originalism is viciously circular or trivial.

549. [POL-016] Counterfactuals About Framers Presuppose Rather Than Ground Constitutional Interpretations
   Sources: Lines 150-200
   Thesis: When legal theorists run counterfactuals about what Jefferson would have said about contemporary issues (like gay marriage), they are not making empirical statements but a priori propositions about what he should have said given his values. This presupposes rather than grounds conceptions of Constitutionality.

550. [POL-017] Idealized Jefferson Incorporates Normative Commitments About Constitutionality
   Sources: Lines 200-250
   Thesis: When we talk about 'what Jefferson would have said', we're talking about what some idealization of Jefferson would have said—a Jefferson purged of cultural limitations and temporal parochialism. This idealization incorporates a certain conception of Constitutionality.

551. [POL-018] 'Jefferson's Values' Denotes Idealization Creating Parallel Circularity
   Sources: Lines 300-350
   Thesis: The expression 'Jefferson's values' itself denotes an idealization rather than psychological reality, involving a circularity parallel to that in 'framers' intentions'. We use conceptions of Constitutionality to identify which values are 'his', then use those values to determine Constitutionality.

552. [POL-019] Historical Counterfactuals Replace Empirical Propositions with A Priori Propositions About Values
   Sources: Lines 400-450
   Thesis: Once we start dealing with idealizations of framers' psyches rather than their actual psyches, we have replaced empirical propositions about their psychology with a priori propositions about values. Such counterfactuals presuppose conceptions of Constitutionality and thus cannot substantiate them.

553. [POL-020] Originalism Condemns Itself to Vicious Circularity or Innocuous Tautology
   Sources: Lines 50, 65, 450
   Thesis: The originalist position, when properly understood, collapses into either vicious circularity (using Constitutional conceptions to identify framers' intentions/values, then using those to determine Constitutional meaning) or innocuous tautology (the Constitution means what we think it should mean).

554. [POL-021] Originalist Must Identify Values Before Running Counterfactuals, Creating Circle
   Sources: Lines 270-280
   Thesis: The originalist is caught in a vicious circle: he must use counterfactuals to identify the values on which his conception of Constitutionality is based, but cannot run those counterfactuals until he has identified those values.

555. [POL-022] Free Markets Inherently Generate Irresolvable Wealth Inequalities
   Sources: Chapter Outline of Economics Paper on Contradictions in Free Market
   Thesis: It is inherent in the free market that it leads to inequalities of wealth and income that cannot be resolved within a free market framework. The free market cannot be expected to diminish the wealth disparities that it itself creates.

556. [POL-023] Government Has Responsibility to Correct Market-Generated Inequalities
   Sources: Chapter Outline of Economics Paper on Contradictions in Free Market
   Thesis: Since the free market cannot diminish the wealth disparities it creates, the government is responsible for diminishing these disparities. Capitalist countries like Sweden enjoy capitalism's benefits while avoiding unjust wealth disparities through progressive taxation.

557. [POL-024] War on Drugs Vindicated Libertarian Conception of State's Rightful Role
   Sources: Chapter Some Reflections on the Virtues of the Free Market
   Thesis: Marijuana legalization constitutes a major victory for the libertarian conception of the state's rightful role. The state should confine itself to preventing clear crimes (assault, rape, theft, fraud) and should refrain from criminalizing acts for purely moral rather than pragmatic reasons.

558. [POL-025] Classical Liberals Vindicated on Drug Policy, Contemporary Liberals Proven Wrong
   Sources: Chapter Some Reflections on the Virtues of the Free Market
   Thesis: Right-wing economists (free-marketeers like Milton Friedman) were completely vindicated on drug policy: anti-drug laws paralyzed markets, encouraged cartels, depleted economy. Left-wing economists favoring government-created jobs were proven completely wrong.

559. [POL-026] Free Market as Driving Force of Healthy Economy and Culture
   Sources: Chapter De Tocqueville on Egoism
   Thesis: For classical liberals (Smith, Locke, Hume), ego/individualism is the driving force of a healthy economy, and a healthy economy is the backbone of a healthy culture. Freedom, including economic freedom, is the most natural condition possible.

560. [POL-027] Rousseau/Marx View Free Market as Basis of Unnatural Unjust Social Order
   Sources: Chapter De Tocqueville on Egoism
   Thesis: Opponents of free markets (Rousseau, Marx) regard it as basis of unnatural social order creating horrible inequalities and intolerable deprivations. What classical liberals see as healthy individualism, they see as psychopathic egoism and greed requiring return to pre-capitalist moral purity.

561. [POL-028] Plato's Justice Requires Rigid Hierarchical Social Strata Based on Fixed Nature
   Sources: Chapter Plato's Republic as Pol Potist Bureaucracy
   Thesis: For Plato, justice is identical with people staying in their 'rightful place.' Social position should be determined by one's nature, which cannot relevantly change. Social strata must be rigidly defined with virtually impenetrable barriers between classes.

562. [POL-029] Plato's Republic Requires Complete Subordination of Private Life to State
   Sources: Chapter Plato's Republic as Pol Potist Bureaucracy
   Thesis: Plato doesn't acknowledge legitimacy of private life. Entirety of person's life must be subordinate to state interests. Marriages arranged for state benefit, reproduction controlled, no private property, complete collectivization of existence.

563. [POL-030] Plato's Justice Completely Depends on State Propaganda and Systematic Lies
   Sources: Chapter Plato's Republic as Pol Potist Bureaucracy
   Thesis: For Plato, justice depends completely on the state constantly lying to its citizenry, keeping them ignorant, and filling knowledge gaps with carefully constructed propaganda. This is necessary to maintain rigid hierarchical social order.

564. [POL-031] Plato's Distinction Between Benign and Dangerous Lies Cannot Be Sustained
   Sources: Chapter Plato's Republic as Pol Potist Bureaucracy
   Thesis: Plato's distinction between benign/beneficial lies and improper/dangerous lies cannot be sustained. Since Plato's conception of justice denies people any freedoms, and such conception is false and evil, any lies told to uphold it are ipso facto evil.

565. [POL-032] Market Economy is Enlightenment Economy Linking Status to Ability Not Birth
   Sources: Chapter Knowledge-capital
   Thesis: Since the Enlightenment, one's stature in society has come to depend increasingly on one's own abilities (including intellectual abilities) and decreasingly on social position one was born into. Market economy is Enlightenment/post-Enlightenment economy where ability to acquire/retain property depends largely on intellectual abilities.

566. [POL-033] Kant's Enlightenment Autonomy Has Operational Meaning Only in Market Economy
   Sources: Chapter Knowledge-capital
   Thesis: Kant's exhortation to 'have the courage to use your own understanding' has operational meaning only in market economy. In non-market economy it's meaningless - indentured servant who thinks for himself gains nothing practical. But in market economy one has nothing to rely on but own judgment.

567. [POL-034] Legal Freedom Compatible with Complete Substantive Enslavement
   Sources: Chapter Legal vs. Substantive Freedom and the Paradox of the Free Market
   Thesis: The freedoms people have in market economy (to own and exchange goods and services) inevitably lead to complete mutual enslavement under pretexts of 'universal legal protection of rights' and 'economic freedom.' Legal freedom coexists with substantive slavery.

568. [POL-035] Free Market Turns People Into Commodities and Mere Spectacles
   Sources: Chapter Legal vs. Substantive Freedom and the Paradox of the Free Market
   Thesis: Market-based society, as opposed to culture-based society, inevitably turns people into objects or 'mere spectacles' (Debord's term). Pornography is paradigm case: human being literally turned into commodity that exists only to be consumed by being looked at.

569. [POL-036] 2008 crisis was dual: housing bubble plus banking collapse
   Sources: WORK-029 (lines 180-210)
   Thesis: The 2008 financial crisis had two distinct components with different mechanisms: (1) a housing bubble driven by subprime lending and securitization, and (2) a banking system collapse caused by interconnected megabanks' exposure to toxic assets. These require different regulatory responses: the first needs better lending standards, the second needs to break up megabanks.

570. [POL-37] Socrates executed for wartime disruption, not truth-seeking
   Sources: WORK-038 (Why Was Socrates Executed? Part I)
   Thesis: Socrates was executed for being disruptive during Athens' civil war, not for seeking truth. He caused Athenians to question moral beliefs that undergirded patriotism precisely when Athens most needed political unity.

571. [POL-38] Philosophical questioning can undermine necessary political unity
   Sources: WORK-038 (Why Was Socrates Executed? Part I)
   Thesis: While truth is generally preferable to fiction, philosophical questioning of foundational beliefs can weaken necessary social cohesion, especially during crises requiring unified action.

572. [POL-39] Socrates sought power through intellectual influence
   Sources: WORK-038 (Why Was Socrates Executed? Part II)
   Thesis: Socrates' philosophical activity was a strategy to gain power not through official positions but by installing his worldview at the top through grooming power-adjacent elites. He wanted to be the state, not serve it.

573. [POL-40] Philosopher-king doctrine as mission statement, not abstract ideal
   Sources: WORK-038 (Why Was Socrates Executed? Part II)
   Thesis: The philosopher-king doctrine was not an abstract ideal but Socrates' mission statement - a concrete plan for installing someone like himself in power. That's why he was executed: his answers, if acted on, would have made him king.

574. [POL-41] Socrates delegitimized authority with replacement theory
   Sources: WORK-038 (Why Was Socrates Executed? Part III)
   Thesis: Socrates wasn't just exposing ignorance for sport - he was methodically delegitimizing existing authority while building a replacement system where 'someone who knows' (the philosopher) should rule instead of generals, priests, or wealthy.

575. [POL-42] The Republic as conservative propaganda disguised as political philosophy
   Sources: WORK-038 (The Republic as Political Tract)
   Thesis: Plato's Republic is fundamentally conservative propaganda designed to rationalize aristocratic power and prevent revolution, not genuine political philosophy seeking justice.

576. [POL-43] Plato's Good/Real equivalence as coded social stability doctrine
   Sources: WORK-038 (The Republic as Political Tract)
   Thesis: Plato's linking of 'the Good' with 'the real' makes no literal sense (since bad things are real) but makes perfect sense as code: 'good/real' = what conduces to social stability, 'bad/shadows' = what threatens social stability.

577. [POL-44] Plato's political philosophy replaces world with thought-world
   Sources: WORK-038 (Philosophy as Psychopathology)
   Thesis: Plato's system was completely a priori - he wasn't engaging actual world but proposing to replace it with his own thought-world having little reality or justification outside his thought-space.

578. [POL-45] Philosopher-king doctrine is incoherent
   Sources: WORK-038 (Philosophy as Psychopathology)
   Thesis: The idea that society should be ruled by philosopher-king is incoherent because societies must be run by sapient doers, not sapient thinkers - by people who engage world through action, not by those who flee into intellectual constructions.

579. [POL-46] Marx's political philosophy as destructive a priori fantasy
   Sources: WORK-038 (Philosophy as Psychopathology)
   Thesis: Marx explicitly proposed destroying existing social structure and replacing it with system having no real basis in reality (totally fabricated), which when implemented led to unprecedented loss of life and opportunity.

580. [PRAG-001] Cancelability Test
   Sources: WORK-004
   Thesis: Conversational implicatures always cancelable. Existence presuppositions not cancelable. Therefore not conversational implicature.

581. [PRAG-002] Conventional Implicature Constraint
   Sources: WORK-004
   Thesis: Conventional implicature doesn't obscure truth-conditions. Adds 'tone' but never makes synonyms differ in truth-conditions.

582. [PRAG-003] Function of 'Exactly,' 'Precisely,' 'Literally' Modifiers
   Sources: Chapter Section on literal meaning
   Thesis: Expressions like 'exactly,' 'precisely,' and 'literally' have the semantic function of confining the auditor's attention to literal meaning - telling the auditor not to draw inferences beyond what is literally affirmed. These modifiers reveal what expressions mean literally by blocking pragmatic enrichment.

583. [PSY-004] Group Psychology is Explanatorily Prior to Individual Psychology
   Sources: Main argument throughout essay
   Thesis: Contrary to standard psychological methodology, group psychology should be understood as explanatorily fundamental, with individual psychology being derivative. Individual drives and behaviors are best explained as necessary for the survival and functioning of collectives, rather than collectives being aggregations of individual behaviors.

584. [PSY-005] Conformism Cannot Be Explained by Individual Psychology Alone
   Sources: Paragraph 3
   Thesis: The extreme degree of conformism exhibited by people - their deference to convention, custom, and fleeting fads even at the expense of personal gratification - cannot be adequately explained by individual psychology even after accounting for intellectual shortcomings and fear of others.

585. [PSY-006] Collective Intelligence Exceeds Individual Intelligence
   Sources: Paragraph 4
   Thesis: Given how unintelligent, ignorant, and lacking in moral fiber most individuals are, yet how much intelligence, knowledge, and moral rigor is embodied in collective behaviors (corporations, academic disciplines), it is implausible that collectives are mere aggregations of individuals pursuing their own paths. The collective appears to be the primary thing biologically.

586. [PSY-007] Philosophers and Obsessive-Compulsives Share Compulsive Doubt
   Sources: Lines 26-27
   Thesis: Philosophers and obsessive-compulsives are both compulsive doubters who doubt the obvious, rationalizing this as rigor while actually expressing impotence and fear of engaging the world.

587. [PSY-008] Philosophers and OCD Sufferers Manipulate Symbolic Proxies Instead of Reality
   Sources: Lines 26-27
   Thesis: Both philosophers and obsessive-compulsives deal with linguistic and symbolic proxies of reality rather than engaging the world directly, seeking dominance in the sphere of thought where they have power.

588. [PSY-009] Preoccupation with Logical Niceties Derives from Impotence
   Sources: Lines 28-29
   Thesis: Both philosophers and obsessive-compulsives are unduly preoccupied with logical niceties and fine points of argumentation as a derivative of their sense of impotence and lack of material to work on.

589. [PSY-010] Mental Illness is Contextual; Physical Illness is Not
   Sources: Lines 374-375
   Thesis: Mental illnesses are contextual in nature—being an asset in some contexts and a liability in others—while physical illnesses like asthma, lupus, or cancer are simply liabilities in all contexts.

590. [PSY-011] Mental Illness Serves Defensive Function
   Sources: Lines 375-376
   Thesis: Mental illnesses serve a defensive/protective function, insulating the subject in a psychological 'safe-space' from toxic and threatening environments, even though they are dysfunctional in some respects.

591. [PSY-012] Mental Illness Involves Misdeployed Strengths
   Sources: Lines 376
   Thesis: Some mental illnesses involve misdeployed strengths of intellect and character—OCD involves misdeployed intelligence and focus; schizophrenia involves misdeployed creativity and emotional sensitivity.

592. [PSY-013] Psychiatric Munchausen's by Proxy as Covert Child Abuse
   Sources: Lines 380
   Thesis: Parents (usually mothers) get psychiatrists to falsely diagnose their children with autism, Asperger's, ADHD to gain attention, resulting in covert child murder through damaging over-attention from educational and psychiatric bureaucrats.

593. [PSY-014] OCD is Ultimately Voluntary
   Sources: Lines 386-391
   Thesis: OCD is ultimately a voluntary condition and an affliction of the will. If one chooses to leave the defensive bubble and re-engage the world, OCD becomes irrelevant or assumes benign/productive forms.

594. [PSY-015] OCD Prognosis Depends on Volitional Choice
   Sources: Lines 390-391
   Thesis: The prognosis for OCD is 100% positive if seen as ultimately voluntary, but negative if seen as garden-variety pathology outside the scope of will. OCD is eliminated or made adaptive by exercising will in growth-oriented ways.

595. [PSY-016] Auto-hypnosis is Essential for Action
   Sources: Lines 395
   Thesis: Auto-hypnosis (giving oneself commands whose efficacy doesn't depend on conscious judgment) is essential for action. Without it, one would be the ultimate bureaucrat who never does anything requiring sustained enthusiasm.

596. [PSY-017] Psychopathy as Complete Lack of Integrity
   Sources: Chapter Main text
   Thesis: Psychopathy is fundamentally defined as a complete lack of integrity, rather than by specific behavioral symptoms or clinical criteria.

597. [PSY-018] Early-Onset Psychopathy: Failure to Develop Character Architecture
   Sources: Chapter Main text
   Thesis: Early-onset psychopaths never develop the character-architecture of normal persons; any appearance of such architecture is pure fabrication. These individuals become con-artists, grifters, drifters, and cult-leaders.

598. [PSY-019] Bureaucratic Psychopathy: Late-Onset Institutional Submission
   Sources: Chapter Main text
   Thesis: A vastly more common form of psychopathy is 'bureaucratic psychopathy' (bureaupath), in which individuals forfeit their integrity late in life to fit into bureaucratic institutions or pseudo-legitimate professional areas like academia or law. These individuals retain the formal properties of normal character but have become hollow husks in whom 'the magic is gone and the spark is gone.'

599. [PSY-020] Academic Humanities Psychopathy: Truth-Concealing Through Pseudo-Cognitive Categories
   Sources: Chapter Main text
   Thesis: A third type of late-onset psychopathy, prevalent in humanities academia, involves projecting one's failure to understand onto the object of non-understanding by 'sliming it up' with spongiform pseudo-cognitive categories like 'narrative,' 'critique,' and 'literature' rather than admitting non-comprehension.

600. [PSY-021] Basic Tenet of Attachment Theory
   Sources: Chapter Introduction
   Thesis: A person's emotional attachments influence the way in which he deals with problematic situations, and the way in which he deals with problematic situations influences his relations to others. Attachment Theory is a cluster of theories based on this fundamental tenet.

601. [PSY-022] Freud's Account of Character Architecture
   Sources: Chapter Historical background
   Thesis: According to Freud, a psychologically healthy adult is someone whose parents loved him but did not spoil him. The mother's job is to provide love (leading to self-love), and the father's job is to provide discipline (leading to self-discipline). Adult success depends on having a healthy combination of self-love and self-discipline.

602. [PSY-023] Bowlby's Attachment Behavioral System
   Sources: Chapter Bowlby's contribution
   Thesis: An 'attachment behavioral system' (ABS) refers to the behaviors and attitudes that determine how a person forms relationships and deals with abandonment. A person's ABS is largely determined by the nature of early-life relationships with caregivers. To become a healthy adult, a child needs at least one stable attachment with a caregiver.

603. [PSY-024] Four Basic Infant Attachment Patterns
   Sources: Chapter Infant attachment patterns
   Thesis: There are four basic attachment patterns in infants: (1) Secure - happy, confident, boldly exploratory with nurturing caregivers; (2) Anxious-ambivalent - cautious, worried about caregiver departure, with withdrawn/unreliable caregivers; (3) Anxious-avoidant - not distressed by departure, avoid caregiver on return, focus on physical environment, have abusive caregivers; (4) Disorganized - respond with fear to returning caregivers, have extremely abusive or highly unreliable caregivers.

604. [PSY-025] Persistence of Attachment Patterns Through Development
   Sources: Chapter Developmental persistence
   Thesis: The four attachment patterns (secure, anxious-ambivalent, anxious-avoidant, disorganized) persist from infancy through childhood into adulthood, though with developmentally appropriate manifestations. There is good evidence that a child's attachment pattern tends to be identical with the one he had as an infant, though categorical identity remains an open question. Some evidence suggests adults can have different attachment patterns from earlier life.

605. [PSY-026] Attachment Insecurities Linked to Specific Psychopathologies
   Sources: Chapter Attachment and psychopathology
   Thesis: Attachment insecurities of both anxious and avoidant varieties are associated with depression, anxiety disorders, OCD, PTSD, suicidal tendencies, and eating disorders. Anxious attachment specifically associates with dependent, histrionic, and borderline disorders, while avoidant attachment associates with schizoid and avoidant disorders.

606. [PSY-027] Kuczynski's Explanation of Attachment-Psychopathology Connections
   Sources: Chapter Kuczynski's theoretical contribution
   Thesis: According to Kuczynski (2012), schizoid and psychotic disorders involve scrambling of the subject's grasp of reality itself because early-life attachments were negative (not merely ambiguous), disposing them to flee from reality in the most radical way possible. By contrast, histrionic, borderline, and dependent disorders involve fundamentally non-delusive grasp of reality but inappropriate emotions because early-life attachments were ambivalent, disposing them to keep distance from external reality without altogether abandoning it.

607. [PSY-028] Psychosis is a mental impairment precipitated and sustained by a break with external reality
   Sources: WORK-026 (Neurosis vs. Psychosis)
   Thesis: Psychosis is a mental impairment precipitated and sustained by a break with external reality

608. [PSY-029] Neurosis is a mental impairment precipitated and sustained by a break with one's emotional condition
   Sources: WORK-026 (Neurosis vs. Psychosis)
   Thesis: Neurosis is a mental impairment precipitated and sustained by a break with one's emotional condition

609. [PSY-030] The neurotic flees from his emotions; the psychotic flees from reality
   Sources: WORK-026 (Neurosis vs. Psychosis)
   Thesis: The neurotic flees from his emotions; the psychotic flees from reality

610. [PSY-031] Neurosis may lead to blunted awareness of external reality, but this is subordinate to loss of awareness of emotional condition
   Sources: WORK-026 (Neurosis vs. Psychosis)
   Thesis: Neurosis may lead to blunted awareness of external reality, but this is subordinate to loss of awareness of emotional condition

611. [PSY-032] Psychosis may lead to disrupted understanding of emotional condition, but this is subordinate to loss of awareness of external reality
   Sources: WORK-026 (Neurosis vs. Psychosis)
   Thesis: Psychosis may lead to disrupted understanding of emotional condition, but this is subordinate to loss of awareness of external reality

612. [PSY-033] Neurosis and psychosis are not mirror images despite their symmetries

   Thesis: Neurosis and psychosis are not mirror images despite their symmetries

613. [PSY-034] Psychosis involves a partial (not complete) regression to a condition of psychological infancy
   Sources: WORK-026 (Neurosis vs. Psychosis)

614. [PSY-035] An infant is not psychotic because the infant's psychological integration is simply that of an infant, not simultaneously adult and infant

   Thesis: An infant is not psychotic because the infant's psychological integration is simply that of an infant, not simultaneously adult and infant

615. [PSY-036] The infant's psychological condition is integrated and healthy even though the infant's understanding of reality is more subjective and projective than the adult psychotic's
   Sources: WORK-026 (Neurosis vs. Psychosis)
   Thesis: The infant's psychological condition is integrated and healthy even though the infant's understanding of reality is more subjective and projective than the adult psychotic's

616. [PSY-037] The adult psychotic has the psychological architecture of both an adult and an infant, creating two entirely distinct and incompatible ways of processing information
   Sources: WORK-026 (Neurosis vs. Psychosis)

617. [PSY-038] The psychotic does not have a unified value system or unified understanding of how to implement values, resulting in utter psychological disarray
   Sources: WORK-026 (Neurosis vs. Psychosis)

618. [PSY-039] Neurosis is about containing threats to integration by repressing them
   Sources: WORK-026 (Neurosis vs. Psychosis)

619. [PSY-040] To repress a concept is not to bury one's knowledge of it in the unconscious; it is to bury one's knowledge of its emotional valence in the unconscious
   Sources: WORK-026 (Neurosis vs. Psychosis)
   Thesis: To repress a concept is not to bury one's knowledge of it in the unconscious; it is to bury one's knowledge of its emotional valence in the unconscious

620. [PSY-041] The neurotic's condition is one of relatively unimpaired intellectual awareness

621. [PSY-042] The neurotic may have heightened intellectual awareness due to compensating for impoverished emotional state by hypercathecting the intellect

622. [PSY-043] By stripping consciousness of emotional valences, the neurotic guarantees a hyper-stable though ossified psyche

623. [PSY-044] The essence of psychosis is an inability to organize consciously experienced emotion

624. [PSY-045] The essence of neurosis is an inability to have consciously experienced emotion
   Sources: WORK-026 (Neurosis vs. Psychosis)

625. [PSY-046] The psychotic is paralyzed by a superabundance of emotion; the neurotic by lack of it

626. [PSY-047] For men, happiness is about forging one's own identity

635. [PSY-056] Stuttering is about not speaking with a single voice - two distinct currents of thought attempting to control speech

637. [PSY-058] Men are self-contained and women are not - this is the fundamental difference between men and women
   Sources: WORK-026 (How men and women are different)

   Sources: WORK-026 (How men and women are different)
