700. [PSY-121] Without self-awareness, one tends not to adapt well, since adaptation requires revising and being aware of one's conduct
   Sources: WORK-008 (Self-absorption Paradox)
   Thesis: Without self-awareness, one tends not to adapt well, since adaptation requires revising and being aware of one's conduct

701. [PSY-122] Self-awareness makes one self-critical and prone to forms of distress to which non-self-aware people are not prone
   Sources: WORK-008 (Self-absorption Paradox)
   Thesis: Self-awareness makes one self-critical and prone to forms of distress to which non-self-aware people are not prone

702. [PSY-123] Optimism is a form of denial; one believes 'everything will be ok' when one has reason to believe otherwise but lacks self-confidence to confront that fact
   Sources: WORK-008 (Stockdale Paradox)
   Thesis: Optimism is a form of denial; one believes 'everything will be ok' when one has reason to believe otherwise but lacks self-confidence to confront that fact

703. [PSY-124] Optimism is motivated by insecurity-driven lack of realism and leads to failure; self-belief is motivated by confidence-driven realism and leads to success
   Sources: WORK-008 (Stockdale Paradox)
   Thesis: Optimism is motivated by insecurity-driven lack of realism and leads to failure; self-belief is motivated by confidence-driven realism and leads to success

704. [PSY-125] Attempting not to have thoughts of a certain kind tends to make such thoughts more likely to occur (Ironic Process Theory)
   Sources: WORK-008 (Ironic Process Theory)
   Thesis: Attempting not to have thoughts of a certain kind tends to make such thoughts more likely to occur (Ironic Process Theory)

705. [PSY-126] Polytheistic impulses may be psychologically basic
   Sources: WORK-028 (lines 615-640)
   Thesis: The historical prevalence of polytheism and its apparent 'revival' in Christianity's Trinitarian development suggest polytheistic religious instincts may be more psychologically basic than monotheism. Humans may naturally tend toward recognizing multiple divine beings, with monotheism being the culturally constructed exception.

706. [PSY-127] Religious conceptions reflect relational needs
   Sources: WORK-028 (lines 670-700)
   Thesis: Human conceptions of divinity are shaped by psychological needs for relationship, protection, and meaning. Smith's theology reflects this: God is conceived as having the attributes (limited power/knowledge, personal concern, accessibility) that enable the required guardian-child relationship, rather than attributes following from abstract philosophical reasoning.

707. [PSY-128] Brain Centers for Militant Atheism and Fundamentalism Are Identical
   Sources: WORK-030 (lines 43)
   Thesis: The brain structures that mediate militant atheism are the same as those mediating religious fundamentalism.

708. [PSY-129] Denying Spiritualism Causes Psychological Morbidity
   Sources: WORK-030 (lines 29, 194-198)
   Thesis: According to James, Otto, and Eliade, genuinely lacking belief in transcendence (not merely lacking explicit religion) leads to various forms of psychological disorder.

709. [PSY-130] Historical Variation in Fundamental Psychology
   Sources: WORK-030 (lines 36-37, 164-174)
   Thesis: Basic psychological structures (like perception and meaning-making) vary fundamentally across historical and cultural contexts, challenging universalist psychology.

710. [PSY-131] Consciousness maximizes energy efficiency
   Sources: WORK-034
   Thesis: Mental/psychological dimensions make organisms more energy-efficient than they would otherwise be. Psychological growth is a particularly extreme way of increasing an organism's level of energy-efficiency.

711. [PSY-131] Philosophy as intellectualized impotence / retreat from reality
   Sources: WORK-038 (Philosophy as Psychopathology)
   Thesis: Both OCD and philosophy involve retreating from exigencies of external actual reality into the safety of internal pseudo-reality. Both are forms of intellectualized impotence.

712. [PSY-132] Obsessive beliefs are pseudo-beliefs
   Sources: WORK-036
   Thesis: Obsessive beliefs are pseudo-beliefs - if someone obsessionally believes that such and such, what they actually believe is the opposite. Obsessive hatred represents lingering attachment that won't be admitted. Obsessing that someone is listening to phone calls expresses fear that no one cares.

713. [PSY-132] OCD and philosophy are homologous psychopathologies
   Sources: WORK-038 (Philosophy as Psychopathology)
   Thesis: OCD and philosophy are not merely analogous but homologous - from a psychopathological perspective they represent the same underlying condition: autistic withdrawal from reality into thought-space.

714. [PSY-133] Compulsive actions are pseudo-actions
   Sources: WORK-036
   Thesis: Compulsive acts are pseudo-actions - if one compulsively does such and such, one's real intention is to do the opposite. Compulsive avoidance of an ex-girlfriend indicates wanting to see her. Compulsive doting on mother actually expresses hatred for her.

715. [PSY-133] Republic exhibits OCD-like rigidity and protocols
   Sources: WORK-038 (Philosophy as Psychopathology)
   Thesis: The absurdity of Plato's Republic manifests in its OCD-like features: rigid society, stereotyped protocols for education and social interaction, death penalty for minor violations (in Laws).

716. [PSY-134] OCD essence is ambivalence
   Sources: WORK-036
   Thesis: The essence of OCD is ambivalence - simultaneously loving and hating the same object. The compulsively doting son both loves and hates his mother. Because he loves her, his desire not to be with her must express itself circuitously through compulsive behaviors.

717. [PSY-135] Doing and undoing in OCD
   Sources: WORK-036
   Thesis: The obsessional engages in 'doing and undoing' (Freud) - does something, then undoes it, then undoes the undoing. Driving to mother's house, then turning back for wallet, then back again for stove. This represents the stalemate between love and hatred, with each emotion expressing itself through the oscillating behavior.

718. [PSY-136] OCD behavior as overdetermined
   Sources: WORK-036
   Thesis: OCD behaviors are overdetermined (Freud) - they serve multiple unconscious functions simultaneously. Back-and-forth driving serves both to express ambivalence toward mother and to discharge sexual frustration through piston-like repetitive motion mimicking the sexual act.

719. [PSY-137] Symbolic representation in OCD symptoms
   Sources: WORK-036
   Thesis: OCD symptoms involve symbolic representation of unconscious desires and conflicts. Fear about stove being left on represents undischarged libido; the stove symbolizes passionate desire. Driving behavior symbolizes sexual act. 'Fear' the stove will explode is really desire that genital region will 'explode.'

720. [PSY-138] Awareness without consciousness in the obsessional
   Sources: WORK-036
   Thesis: The obsessional is aware of underlying dynamics (mother's treachery, sexual frustration) without being consciously aware. One can be aware of something at the level of unconsciousness. The person doesn't quite see irritating behaviors for what they are even unconsciously, but is surely aware at some level.

721. [PSY-139] Single ultimate determinant despite overdetermination
   Sources: WORK-036
   Thesis: Despite overdetermination, behavior may have a single ultimate determinant. The son's behavior is overdetermined by both ambivalence toward mother and sexual frustration, but ultimately the sexual frustration is primary - ambivalence exists because mother causes sexual frustration. The two causes operate as a single cause in this context.

722. [PSY-140] Consciousness of hatred eliminates compulsions
   Sources: WORK-036
   Thesis: When unconscious hatred becomes conscious, associated compulsions vanish. The compulsiveness exists precisely because the true feelings are unconscious. Once awareness reaches consciousness, the need for disguised expression through compulsion disappears.

723. [PSY-141] Compulsive time management as defense
   Sources: WORK-036
   Thesis: Compulsive punctuality (showing up two hours early) serves as a hedge against the unconscious wish not to show up at all. Being 'hyper on time' insulates against the desire to avoid the obligation entirely. This is another form of doing and undoing.

724. [PSYCH-001] Problem Portability
   Sources: Dialogue on transferring schools/cities
   Thesis: Wherever you go, there you are. Your problems tend to follow you. External change without internal change doesn't solve problems.

725. [PSYCH-002] Universal Beauty Under Blindness
   Sources: Dialogue on ugliness in the world
   Thesis: Everything is beautiful, but most people are blind to most of the beauty. The ugliness perceived in the world reflects perceptual limitations rather than absence of beauty.

726. [PSYCH-003] Ability-Demand Asymmetry
   Sources: Dialogue on abilities being economically useful
   Thesis: Ability will never catch up with the demand for it. There is always more need for ability than supply of it.

727. [REL-001] God progressed to divinity from humanity
   Sources: WORK-028 (lines 56-169)
   Thesis: Joseph Smith's King Follett Discourse argued that God was once a man who became divine through spiritual development. This represents a radical break from traditional Christian theology, implying divinity is not an absolute status but an achieved state, and the distinction between God and humanity is one of degree rather than kind.

728. [REL-002] God created through organization, not ex nihilo
   Sources: WORK-028 (lines 246-258)
   Thesis: God did not create the world ex nihilo but by organizing pre-existing chaotic matter. The Hebrew 'baurau' means to organize, not to create from nothing. Pure elements are eternal and indestructible—they can be organized and reorganized but never created or destroyed.

729. [REL-003] Human spirits are immortal and have always existed
   Sources: WORK-028 (lines 274-300)
   Thesis: The intelligence of human spirits has no beginning and no end. If something is immortal (has no end), logic dictates it also had no beginning. Therefore, human beings have always existed eternally. This eternal pre-existence follows from the same principle that makes God self-existent.

730. [REL-004] Multiple gods exist in hierarchical arrangement
   Sources: WORK-028 (lines 205-232)
   Thesis: Although there is a supreme God, multiple lesser gods also exist. This follows from the doctrine of eternal progression: if humans can become gods through spiritual development, and this process has been ongoing eternally, then many gods must exist. The Hebrew 'Elohim' (Gods, plural) indicates this plurality.

731. [REL-005] King Follett vision transcends its arguments
   Sources: WORK-028 (lines 98-108)
   Thesis: Smith's arguments for his theological positions in KFD, even if assumed cogent, would not lead anyone to accept his radical vision. The merits of the vision lie in the vision itself, not in the arguments. This raises the historiographical question: where did Smith's vision originate?

732. [REL-006] Smith's theology evolved from monotheism to polytheism
   Sources: WORK-028 (lines 556-608)
   Thesis: Joseph Smith's theology underwent systematic evolution. Early period (1820-1835): unambiguous monotheism. Middle period (1835): God and Jesus treated as distinct entities. Later Nauvoo period (1839-1844): full polytheism—God has a father, belongs to a council of gods, humans can become gods. Hebrew study accelerated the shift.

733. [REL-007] Orthodox Christianity is crypto-polytheistic
   Sources: WORK-028 (lines 528-539)
   Thesis: Orthodox Christianity is not strictly monotheistic despite its claims. If Jesus is truly the son of God (not God himself), and the Holy Ghost is a distinct force, and God is an exalted person-like being, then there are at least three divine beings, making Christianity crypto-polytheistic. The doctrine that God, Jesus, and Holy Ghost are 'three but one' is absurd and logically incoherent.

734. [REL-008] Christianity represents revival of polytheistic instincts
   Sources: WORK-028 (lines 616-634)
   Thesis: Historically, polytheism is the rule and monotheism the exception. Christianity may represent a revival of polytheistic instincts. Early Church Doctors needed at least two divinities (God and Jesus) but couldn't openly embrace polytheism. They therefore affirmed absurdly that God and Jesus, though two, are one.

735. [REL-009] Smith's theology prioritizes divine-human relationship
   Sources: WORK-028 (lines 658-696)
   Thesis: Smith's fundamental question was: What must God be like if humans are to have the required relationship with Him? This breaks with both philosophical and Christian traditions that focus on logical puzzles about God's attributes. Smith starts with the assumption that God is psychologically able and willing to serve as guardian, attributing only as much power and knowledge as is compatible with this relational requirement.

736. [REL-010] Logical proofs of God turn Him into impersonal force
   Sources: WORK-028 (lines 695-700)
   Thesis: Attempts to prove God's existence inevitably turn Him into an impersonal force or principle, stripping Him of the ability to have relationships with humans. If 'God' is defined as 'maximally perfect being,' 'guarantor of natural law,' or 'unmoved mover,' this abstracts away the personal characteristics necessary for divine-human relationship.

737. [REL-011] Three Attitudes Toward Religion
   Sources: WORK-030 (lines 22-28)
   Thesis: There are fundamentally three attitudes toward religion: (1) uncritical acceptance, (2) rejection, and (3) critical/reflective acceptance.

738. [REL-012] Contemporary Fundamentalism is Reactive, Not Uncritical
   Sources: WORK-030 (lines 35-37)
   Thesis: Contemporary religious fundamentalists are not genuinely 'uncritically accepting' of religion because they live in pluralistic societies and are reacting against non-religious views.

739. [REL-013] Contemporary Atheism as Herd Mentality
   Sources: WORK-030 (lines 40-43)
   Thesis: Most contemporary atheists are simply following social norms rather than reasoning independently, making their mentality similar to medieval religious believers.

740. [REL-014] Reductive vs. Non-Reductive Accounts of Religion
   Sources: WORK-030 (lines 44-49)
   Thesis: There are both reductive (explanatory/causal) and non-reductive (phenomenological/essential) truths about religion, and the essence of religion lies in non-reductive truths.

741. [REL-015] Religion Requires Unshakable Conviction in Transcendence
   Sources: WORK-030 (lines 29)
   Thesis: The essence of religious sentiment is the unshakable conviction that 'this world is not all that there is' and that psychological health requires this view.

742. [REL-016] Writing as the Basis of Rationalism
   Sources: WORK-030 (lines 13, 50-100)
   Thesis: The development of writing is the foundation of rationalism, creating economies of scale and enabling the linearization of time.

743. [REL-017] Economies of Scale Cause Time-Linearization
   Sources: WORK-030 (lines 13, 50-100)
   Thesis: Large-scale economic and social organization causes the shift from circular to linear conceptions of time characteristic of rationalism.

744. [REL-018] James, Otto, and Eliade Describe Animism, Not Institutional Religion
   Sources: WORK-030 (lines 168-174)
   Thesis: When James, Otto, and Eliade discuss 'religion,' they are actually describing pre-civilizational animistic spiritualism, not institutional religions like Christianity or Islam.

745. [REL-019] Spiritualism vs. Rationalism as Fundamental Orientations
   Sources: WORK-030 (lines 176-193)
   Thesis: For the spiritualist, the world is a living subject and partner; for the rationalist, the world is dead matter existing only to be used as an object.

746. [REL-020] Humans Cannot Become Non-Spiritual
   Sources: WORK-030 (lines 194-198)
   Thesis: Just as we cannot become asexual (per Freud), we cannot become non-spiritual; we can only mistakenly believe we are non-spiritual and thereby undermine our biological condition.

747. [REL-021] Rationalism as Extension of Spiritualism, Not Rejection
   Sources: WORK-030 (lines 198)
   Thesis: Rationalism is a 'rarefied extension' of spiritualism, not a rejection of it; the error is seeing rationalism as anti-spiritual.

748. [REL-022] Contemporary 'Spiritualism' is Actually Nihilism
   Sources: WORK-030 (lines 30-33)
   Thesis: 21st-century self-described 'spiritual but not religious' people manifest nihilism and absence of genuine spiritualism, not its presence.

749. [REL-023] Omniscience precludes action
   Sources: WORK-034
   Thesis: An all-knowing being cannot act because action presupposes ignorance. If one knows with certainty what will happen, one cannot coherently attempt to influence what will happen and therefore cannot intend to act.

750. [REL-024] Omnipotence precludes feeling
   Sources: WORK-034
   Thesis: An all-powerful being cannot experience feelings. Only a being capable of being changed can experience feelings, and if a being is incapable of being changed, it cannot feel.

751. [REL-025] Immutability precludes self-change
   Sources: WORK-034
   Thesis: A being incapable of being changed cannot change itself. To change oneself is to be changed, albeit by oneself. A being that cannot be changed cannot be changed by anything, including itself.

752. [REL-026] Omnipotence entails impotence
   Sources: WORK-034
   Thesis: If a being is all-powerful (omnipotent), it is completely impotent. The concept of an all-powerful being is incoherent because such a being could neither act nor change.

753. [REL-027] Traditional divine attributes are incoherent
   Sources: WORK-034
   Thesis: The concepts of an all-knowing being and an all-powerful being are both incoherent. To the extent we conceptualize God as all-knowing and all-powerful, we are conceptualizing Him incoherently.

754. [REL-028] Consciousness is inherent in existence itself
   Sources: WORK-034
   Thesis: It is inherent in existence that existence be conscious. The universe is disintegrating (lacking consciousness) only to the extent it is ceasing to be what it is. To the extent the universe is growing and becoming what it truly is, it has consciousness. Therefore, there is ipso facto a God - the universe itself, which is pulsating with life and thought rather than being cold and mechanical.

755. [SCI-001] Confirmation Requires Principled Generalizations
   Sources: Solution to Raven Paradox
   Thesis: Only principled (nomic/causal) generalizations, not accidental generalizations, can be confirmed. When 'All ravens are black' is read as a principled generalization, it has nomic content and is not equivalent to 'All non-black things are non-ravens.'

756. [SCI-002] AI Systems Test Philosophical Theories Empirically
   Sources: Throughout work
   Thesis: Philosophical theories about reasoning, knowledge acquisition, scientific discovery can be empirically tested by examining whether successful AI systems operate according to those theories. AI provides concrete examinable implementations allowing theory adjudication.

757. [SCI-003] Logic of Discovery is Possible
   Sources: Essay 4
   Thesis: Contrary to traditional philosophy of science claiming logic of discovery is impossible, examining AI scientific reasoning reveals identifiable principles guiding successful theory generation. Genuine logic of discovery exists.

758. [SCI-004] AI Falsifies Popperian Falsificationism
   Sources: WORK-011 (Essay 3: How AI Falsifies Popper)
   Thesis: AI's success in scientific discovery falsifies Popper's theory that science proceeds primarily through conjecture and refutation. AI systems generate successful theories through pattern matching and inductive generalization, not primarily through bold conjectures and attempts at falsification.

759. [SCI-005] Inductive Discovery Precedes Deductive Testing
   Sources: WORK-011 (Essay 3)
   Thesis: Contra Popper, successful scientific discovery requires inductive pattern recognition to generate plausible hypotheses before deductive testing. AI demonstrates that purely conjectural approaches without inductive guidance are ineffective.

760. [SCI-006] Reverse Brain Engineering as Scientific Method
   Sources: WORK-011 (Essay 4: Reverse Brain Engineering)
   Thesis: By building AI systems that replicate cognitive functions, we can infer the computational architecture necessary for those functions. This 'reverse engineering' of the brain through AI construction represents a new and powerful methodology in philosophy of science and cognitive science.

761. [SCI-007] AI Falsifies Deductive-Nomological Model of Explanation
   Sources: WORK-011 (Essay 18: AI and Explanation)
   Thesis: AI's successful explanatory practices falsify the deductive-nomological (covering law) model of explanation. AI generates successful explanations through pattern recognition, analogy, and causal modeling that don't require deduction from universal laws.

762. [SCI-008] Causal-Mechanistic Explanation Doesn't Require Universal Laws
   Sources: WORK-011 (Essay 18)
   Thesis: AI demonstrates that causal-mechanistic explanation can be successful without appeal to universal laws. Understanding how something works doesn't require subsuming it under exceptionless generalizations.

763. [SCI-009] Explanatory Understanding Through Pattern Recognition
   Sources: WORK-011 (Essay 18)
   Thesis: AI reveals that explanatory understanding can be achieved through recognition of patterns and structural similarities rather than derivation from laws. This suggests explanation is more about grasping relevant relationships than deductive systematization.

764. [SCI-010] Laws of Nature Not Confined to Actual Objects
   Sources: WORK-014
   Thesis: The scope of natural law is not confined to actual or even possible objects. Many laws hold with respect to classes all of whose members are merely possible or even prohibited by other natural laws.

765. [SCI-011] Knowledge of Imperceptibles Identical with Conditional Knowledge
   Sources: WORK-014
   Thesis: Knowledge of the imperceptible is identical with knowledge of conditional truth. Knowledge of future, past, possible, and imperceptible present states is always conditional knowledge based on laws.

766. [SCI-012] Three Kinds of Imperceptibles
   Sources: WORK-014
   Thesis: Physical objects can be imperceptible in three ways: (1) imperceptible due to severed causal processes (objects in other rooms); (2) imperceptible due to size but perceptible with technology (cells, molecules); (3) imperceptible by natural law regardless of technology (photons, subatomic particles).

767. [SCI-013] The Epistemic Function of Natural Law
   Sources: WORK-014
   Thesis: Scientists aspire to identify natural laws so they can, when given context-specific information, make true statements about future, past, or possible behavior of contexts. Laws enable conditional prediction and explanation.

768. [SCI-014] Science Prioritizes Principles Over Particular Facts
   Sources: WORK-014
   Thesis: Any interest science has in a given particular fact is subordinate to its interest in the general principles in terms of which that fact is to be understood. Scientists study particular instances only insofar as they instantiate general laws.

769. [SCI-015] Laws May Be Place and Time-Sensitive
   Sources: WORK-014
   Thesis: Some natural laws are place- and time-sensitive rather than spatiotemporally invariant. Laws need not hold uniformly across all regions of space-time to be genuine laws.

770. [SCI-016] Hume's Regularity Analysis of Causation Is False
   Sources: WORK-014
   Thesis: Hume's Regularity Analysis - the view that causation is nothing but constant conjunction, that 'X causes Y' means 'events of type X are regularly followed by events of type Y' - is demonstrably false.

771. [SCI-017] Hume-Worlds Observationally Different from Non-Humean Worlds
   Sources: WORK-014
   Thesis: A Hume-world (where causation equals regularity with no underlying powers) would be observationally different from our world. The concept of a Hume-world cannot support Hume's analysis.

772. [SCI-018] The Deductive-Nomological Model of Explanation Is False
   Sources: WORK-014
   Thesis: The Deductive-Nomological (DN) model - which holds that to explain event E is to derive E from natural laws plus antecedent conditions - is fundamentally mistaken. Explanation requires causal knowledge, not merely law-subsumption.

773. [SCI-019] DN Viciously Circular via Counterfactual Support
   Sources: WORK-014
   Thesis: The DN model is viciously circular if it requires laws to support counterfactuals (as Hempel proposes). Counterfactuals are cryptocausal statements; knowing them requires knowing causes; but knowing causes already provides explanations.

774. [SCI-020] Causal Knowledge as Differential Knowledge
   Sources: WORK-014
   Thesis: Causal knowledge is differential knowledge - knowledge of what varies with what. To know causes is to know which changes depend on which other changes and in what proportions.

775. [SCI-021] Causation as Proportionality Restoration
   Sources: WORK-014
   Thesis: Causation is fundamentally proportionality restoration. Effects are proportional to their causes (threshold effects aside). When a force acts on an object, the resulting change is proportional to the force magnitude.

776. [SCI-022] Physical Laws as Regularities of Proportion
   Sources: WORK-014
   Thesis: Physical laws are regularities of proportion rather than simple universal generalizations. Laws describe how magnitudes vary proportionally with each other rather than stating that all Fs are Gs.

777. [SCI-023] Knowledge-Why Equals High-Resolution Knowledge-What
   Sources: WORK-014
   Thesis: To have knowledge-why is to have high-resolution knowledge-what. Explanatory knowledge differs from mere descriptive knowledge in degree of detail and specificity, not in kind.

778. [SCI-024] The Raven Paradox a By-Product of Regularity Analysis
   Sources: WORK-014
   Thesis: The Raven Paradox (that non-black non-ravens confirm 'all ravens are black') is an artifact of the Regularity Analysis of causation. Once causation is properly understood, the paradox dissolves.

779. [SCI-025] Determinism Doesn't Entail Complete Predictability
   Sources: WORK-014
   Thesis: Determinism (every event has a cause) does not entail complete predictability. Two reasons: (1) interference effects make prediction impossible without infinite precision, and (2) knowledge growth itself cannot be predicted.

780. [SCI-026] Implementation-Indeterminism Distinguished from Program-Determinism
   Sources: WORK-014
   Thesis: Program-determinism (software-level determinism) is compatible with implementation-indeterminism (hardware-level indeterminism). The same program can be implemented by different physical processes.

781. [SCI-027] Truths Not Objects Are Objects of Explanation
   Sources: WORK-014
   Thesis: Truths, not objects or states of affairs themselves, are the proper objects of explanation. We explain why propositions are true, not why objects exist (except derivatively).

782. [SCI-030] Relativity Theory Reveals Causal Structure of Spacetime
   Sources: Chapter Part 2, Section V
   Thesis: Recognition that temporal order is causal was forced on us by empirical discoveries, particularly Relativity Theory. If events E and E* are such that no causal signal can pass between them, they have no determinate temporal order. But this recognition that temporal order is causal is itself less like an empirical statement ('all rhenates are chordates') than like a hard analytic truth ('triangles are regions bounded by three coplanar lines').

783. [SCI-031] Complete Description Entails Neighborhood Events
   Sources: Chapter Part 2, Section VIII
   Thesis: For an arbitrary event E, if D is a complete description of E, then D entails the occurrence of events that, by ordinary standards, are distinct from E. A correct and complete description of an empirical state of affairs permits deduction of events in its neighborhood because spatiotemporal continuity is causal.

784. [SCI-032] Psychological Versus Physical Explanation Unified
   Sources: Chapter Part 3, Section VII
   Thesis: Explanation always consists in showing logical and principled relation between initial and terminal conditions. There is no need to reduce psychology to statistics (Hempel, Mill) or to create artificial division between human and natural sciences (Dilthey). Psychological and physical explanation are fundamentally the same kind - both show why it makes sense that events occurred.

785. [SCI-033] Explanation as Principled Relationship, Not Mere Regularity
   Sources: Chapter Part 3, Sections VII, VIII
   Thesis: Explanation exposes principled relationships, not mere regularities. Regularities express rather than constitute principled relationships. The existence of a regularity (e.g., flipping switch causes light to turn on) is consequence, not substance, of principled relationship among properties. If this is wrong, regularity becomes coincidence of unspeakable proportions.

786. [SCI-034] Logically equivalent statements are not necessarily confirmationally equivalent
   Sources: WORK-008 (Raven Paradox)
   Thesis: Logically equivalent statements are not necessarily confirmationally equivalent

787. [SCI-035] Confirmation tracks nomic or causal content, not mere logical form
   Sources: WORK-008 (Raven Paradox)
   Thesis: Confirmation tracks nomic or causal content, not mere logical form

788. [SCI-036] 'All metal expands when heated' can be confirmed but not 'all objects in Smith's pocket expand when heated' (only principled generalizations confirmable)
   Sources: WORK-008 (Raven Paradox)
   Thesis: 'All metal expands when heated' can be confirmed but not 'all objects in Smith's pocket expand when heated' (only principled generalizations confirmable)

789. [SCI-037] Philosophical resistance to neuroscience parallels historical science resistance
   Sources: WORK-027 (lines 1800-1850)
   Thesis: Philosophers' resistance to neuroscientific findings about consciousness and free will parallels historical examples of disciplines resisting scientific findings that threatened their authority (e.g., Catholic Church vs. heliocentrism, vitalists vs. mechanistic biology). In each case, defensive reactions disguised as methodological sophistication protected cherished beliefs.

790. [SCI-038] Natural Laws and Modal Space
   Sources: WORK-031 (lines 27-33)
   Thesis: The relationship between natural laws and what's metaphysically possible is a substantive question that PWS presupposes rather than answers.

791. [SCI-047] Laws cannot be defined except via counterfactuals
   Sources: WORK-037
   Thesis: There is widespread agreement that the concept of a law of nature cannot be defined except in terms of counterfactuals - a law is inter alia something that supports counterfactuals. This creates circularity for the factualist analysis, which must understand counterfactuals in terms of laws.

792. [SCI-048] Probability definable from actual events only
   Sources: WORK-037
   Thesis: The relevant kind of probability can be defined wholly in terms of what has happened (not what would happen and not even what must happen in a nomic sense). This avoids the circularity problem in analyzing counterfactuals.

793. [SCI-049] Critique of Humean analysis of laws
   Sources: WORK-037
   Thesis: The Humean analysis of laws as regularities is viciously circular. If states of affairs are themselves causal processes (as they must be), then defining causation as regular concomitance of states of affairs is circular. Additionally, temporal succession itself appears to be a causal notion, making the analysis doubly circular.

794. [SCI-050] Probability must be interpreted causally, not statistically
   Sources: WORK-014
   Thesis: When we say the probability of an event is X%, this statement must be interpreted causally, not statistically. What is being said is that, given the laws of physics/nature and the construction of the system, it is a possibility (with degree X) that the event will occur, whether or not it ever actually occurs. Probability is determined by causal mechanisms and laws, not by observed frequencies.

795. [SCI-050] Probability is causal, not statistical
   Sources: WORK-014 (Chapter 7: Determinism and natural laws)
   Thesis: When it is said that probability of a computer-malfunction is greater than 0%, the statement being made is to be interpreted CAUSALLY, not statistically. Probability is a function of laws and causal mechanisms, not observed frequencies.

796. [SCI-051] Statistics are evidence of probabilities but not themselves probabilities
   Sources: WORK-014
   Thesis: Statistics (observed frequencies) are evidence for what the probabilities are, but they are not identical with probabilities. The actual probability is determined by the underlying causal/nomic structure, and statistics can be misleading if they happen to diverge from that structure due to coincidence. Two worlds with identical laws have identical probabilities even if their statistics differ radically.

797. [SCI-051] Statistics are evidence for probability, not identical with probability
   Sources: WORK-014 (Chapter 7)
   Thesis: Statistics are evidence of probabilities; statistics are not themselves probabilities. Frequency Theory (FT) wrongly identifies statistics with probability.

798. [SCI-052] The W1/W2 thought experiment refutes the Frequency Theory of Probability
   Sources: WORK-014
   Thesis: Consider W1 and W2, two worlds with identical laws where computers have probability P of malfunctioning. In W1, the statistics match this probability. In W2, by sheer coincidence, no computer ever malfunctions (0% frequency). Frequency Theory says W2-probability = 0%, but this is false. The actual probability in both worlds is P (determined by the laws), even though the statistics differ. This refutes Frequency Theory.

799. [SCI-052] W1/W2 thought experiment refutes Frequency Theory
   Sources: WORK-014 (Chapter 7)
   Thesis: W1: laws say P(malfunction)=10%, statistics show 10%. W2: same laws, P(malfunction)=10%, but by coincidence statistics show 0%. Frequency Theory wrongly says P(W2)=0% but P(W1)=10%. Both actually have P=10% (determined by laws).

800. [SCI-053] Probability remains constant even when statistics are misleading due to coincidence
   Sources: WORK-014
   Thesis: In a world with the same biological laws as ours, but where by sheer coincidence smokers never get cancer, doctors would be wrong to say smoking is harmless. The probability that a smoker will get cancer in that world is the SAME as in our world, because the probability is determined by the biological laws (which are identical), not by the observed frequencies (which differ).

801. [SCI-053] Smoking-cancer example refutes Frequency Theory
   Sources: WORK-014 (Chapter 7)
   Thesis: In a world with our biological laws but where by coincidence no smoker gets cancer, Frequency Theory says P(cancer|smoking)=0%. Wrong. P(cancer|smoking) = same as our world (determined by biological laws), regardless of coincidental statistics.

802. [SCI-054] Worlds with identical laws have identical probabilities regardless of statistical divergences
   Sources: WORK-014
   Thesis: If two worlds W1 and W2 have the same laws of nature, they have the same probabilistic structure - the same probabilities for all events - even if their actual statistical frequencies happen to diverge dramatically due to coincidence. Probability supervenes on laws/causal mechanisms, not on observed patterns.

803. [SCI-054] Same laws entail same probabilities regardless of statistics
   Sources: WORK-014 (Chapter 7)
   Thesis: Worlds with identical laws of nature have identical probabilities, regardless of any statistical divergences caused by coincidence.

804. [SCI-055] Worlds with different causal/nomic structures have different probabilities even if event-sequences are identical
   Sources: WORK-014
   Thesis: If universe U1 is governed by laws while universe U2 is governed by pure chance (or different laws), then the probabilities of events in U1 and U2 are DIFFERENT, even if the actual sequence of events that occurs in each universe is identical. This is because probability is determined by the underlying causal/nomic structure, not by the pattern of events. U1's events have probabilities determined by laws; U2's events have probabilities determined by chance (or by different laws).

805. [SCI-055] Different causal/nomic structures entail different probabilities
   Sources: WORK-014 (Chapter 7)
   Thesis: If two universes have different causal/nomic structures (different laws), they have different probabilities, even if their event-sequences are observationally identical.

806. [SELF-001] Minds ≠ Selves
   Sources: WORK-005 (Essay 1)
   Thesis: Having a mind does not entail being a self. Co-corporeal, informationally integrated mental states = mind, but NOT sufficient for selfhood.

807. [SELF-002] Selves Require Values
   Sources: WORK-005 (Essay 1)
   Thesis: No values = no self (though may have mind). Values necessary for agency. No agency without selves.

808. [SELF-003] Selfhood as Matter of Degree
   Sources: WORK-005 (Essay 1)
   Thesis: Selfhood not binary but admits of degrees. Correlates with degree of value-structured architecture.

809. [SET-001] PWS Creates Set-Theoretic Paradoxes
   Sources: WORK-031 (lines 730-793)
   Thesis: Identifying worlds with sets of propositions creates vicious circle problems analogous to classical set-theoretic paradoxes.

810. [VAL-013] Freedom Has Intrinsic Value Within Reasonable Limits
   Sources: Defense of Hayek, paragraph on whether Hayek is right
   Thesis: People should, within reason, be allowed to live the way they want to live. Overly invasive governments prevent this and are therefore objectionable on that basis. The ability to choose one's own path in life has intrinsic value.

811. [VAL-014] One learns more from success than from failure (contra common wisdom)
   Sources: WORK-026 (One learns from adversity, not from failure)
   Thesis: One learns more from success than from failure (contra common wisdom)

812. [VAL-015] Each success opens up new and completely unforeseen vistas; each failure is nothing but a dead end from which nothing is learned
   Sources: WORK-026 (One learns from adversity, not from failure)
   Thesis: Each success opens up new and completely unforeseen vistas; each failure is nothing but a dead end from which nothing is learned

813. [VAL-016] One learns from adversity, not from failure
   Sources: WORK-026 (One learns from adversity, not from failure)
   Thesis: One learns from adversity, not from failure

814. [VAL-017] Failure is the end-result of adversity that was not triumphed over; adversity and failure are distinct
   Sources: WORK-026 (One learns from adversity, not from failure)
   Thesis: Failure is the end-result of adversity that was not triumphed over; adversity and failure are distinct

815. [VAL-018] Everybody wants money, including those who claim to spurn it
   Sources: WORK-026 (Does everybody want money?)
   Thesis: Everybody wants money, including those who claim to spurn it

816. [VAL-019] Authentic religious sentiment does not require membership in an organized religion
   Sources: WORK-024 (VRE Lecture II summary)
   Thesis: Authentic religious sentiment does not require membership in an organized religion

817. [VAL-020] Authentic religious sentiment requires a personal relationship with the divine
   Sources: WORK-024 (Analysis: God as Superego)
   Thesis: Authentic religious sentiment requires a personal relationship with the divine

818. [VAL-021] Religious people believe life to be meaningful and are therefore relatively adversity-tolerant
   Sources: WORK-024 (VRE Lecture II summary)
   Thesis: Religious people believe life to be meaningful and are therefore relatively adversity-tolerant

819. [VAL-022] Religious sentiment makes people sane (when properly functioning)
   Sources: WORK-024 (Overall analysis)
   Thesis: Religious sentiment makes people sane (when properly functioning)

820. [VALUE-001] Intrinsic Value and Self-Consolidation
   Sources: WORK-005 (Essay 1)
   Thesis: Intrinsically valuable = what consolidates one's agency. Not hedonistic.

821. [VALUE-002] Instrumental vs Intrinsic Good
   Sources: WORK-001 (Chapter 19)
   Thesis: Goodness divides into instrumental good (useful for goals) and intrinsic good (good in itself). Ethics concerns intrinsic goodness.

822. [VALUE-003] Intrinsic Good vs Commendable
   Sources: WORK-001 (Chapter 19)
   Thesis: Intrinsic goodness and praiseworthiness are distinct. Some intrinsically good things are not praiseworthy.

823. [VALUE-004] Moral Responsibility Based on Intentions
   Sources: WORK-001 (Chapter 19)
   Thesis: Praise/blame depends on intended outcome, not actual outcome.

824. [VALUE-005] Against Emotivism
   Sources: WORK-001 (Chapter 20)
   Thesis: Moral judgments are not merely expressions of emotion. They are genuine assertions with truth-values.

825. [VALUE-006] Against Moral Relativism
   Sources: WORK-001 (Chapter 21)
   Thesis: Moral relativism is false. There are objective moral truths.

826. [VALUE-007] Against Kant's Categorical Imperative
   Sources: WORK-001 (Chapter 23)
   Thesis: Kant's categorical imperative fails as a criterion for right action.

827. [VALUE-008] Against Pure Hedonism
   Sources: WORK-001 (Chapter 24)
   Thesis: Pleasure is not the only intrinsic good. Hedonism is false.

828. [VALUE-009] Against Pure Utilitarianism
   Sources: WORK-001 (Chapter 24)
   Thesis: Act utilitarianism is false. It violates rights and permits obviously wrong actions.

829. [VALUE-010] Against Divine Command Theory
   Sources: WORK-001 (Chapter 25)
   Thesis: Morality is not based on God's commands. Euthyphro dilemma refutes divine command theory.

830. [VALUE-011] We Cannot Choose Our Values
   Sources: WORK-001 (Chapter 26)
   Thesis: We cannot freely choose what we value. The idea of 'choosing one's own values' is incoherent.

831. [VALUE-012] Law Must Be Based on Justice
   Sources: WORK-001 (Chapter 27)
   Thesis: The purpose of law is to secure justice. Legal systems must be evaluated by whether they achieve justice.

832. [VIRTUE-001] Superior Person's Vigilant Stability
   Sources: Dialogue on security and danger
   Thesis: The superior person maintains stable, centered attitude while being appropriately responsive to changing circumstances. 'When resting in safety, does not forget danger may come. When secure, does not overlook possibility of ruin. When orderly, knows disorder may come. Therefore, when disaster strikes, is ready.'

833. [VIRTUE-002] Judicious Speech as Virtue
   Sources: Dialogue on speech and action
   Thesis: The superior person is careful about what they say and how they say it; they do not speak loosely. Carefulness in speech reflects carefulness in thought and respect for words' consequences.

834. [VIRTUE-003] Practice-Preaching Unity
   Sources: Dialogue on action and acceptance
   Thesis: The superior person practices what they preach and either reconciles themselves to their situation or changes it. They are never idle.

835. [VIRTUE-004] Moral Courage as Essential Virtue
   Sources: Dialogue on will power and courage
   Thesis: To know what you must do and still not do it shows lack of moral courage, which is the worst sin. Excellence requires moral courage, not merely will power.

836. [VIRTUE-005] Earnest Striving Constitutes Achievement
   Sources: Dialogue on becoming superior person
   Thesis: If you earnestly try to be a superior person, you are, for that very reason, on your way to being such a person. The sincere attempt itself constitutes progress toward the goal.
